الفضل بهذا الإسناد كلهم ثقات، ونظر فيه البيهقي بأن عبد الله بن عباد غير مشهور ويحيى بن أيوب ليس بالقوي وهو من رجاله . وقال عبد الله بن عباد البصري يقلب الأخبار وقال : روى عنه روح بن الفرج نسخة موضوعة، در مشايخنا الكرام حيث قدموا حديث صوم عاشوراء الصحيح المتفق على صحته وعملوا بعبارته ودلالته وعملوا بهذا المختلف فيما وافق القياس هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم فافهم
That the Prophet said: 'Do you have anything?' We said: 'No.' He said: 'Then I am fasting.' Then he came to us another day and we said: 'O Messenger of Allah, we have been gifted some Hays.' He said: 'Show it to me; I started the day fasting,' and he ate. Reported by Muslim. This is clear regarding intention during the day for supererogatory fasting. This is only valid if fasting is not divisible and fasting part of the day is not considered fasting. But if it is divisible and part of the day is worship, as the author of al-Hidayah narrated from Imam al-Shafi'i that fasting part of the day is fasting, but its condition is abstention from dawn, then there is room for discussion. For the one who intends supererogatory fasting during the day is fasting part of the day from the time of intention, not from the beginning. So precedence of intention over fasting is a condition in every fast, but the matter is not hidden from the knowledgeable; it is a legal prescription, and it must have evidence, so understand. And that the objection is valid in the month of Ramadan, where he said after witnessing the crescent, and on the day of Ashura when its fast was obligatory before the obligation of Ramadan, and 'whoever has not eaten, let him fast.' As for the first, it was mentioned in al-Hidayah that after the Bedouin testified to seeing the crescent, the Prophet said: 'Whoever has eaten, let him not eat for the rest of his day, and whoever has not eaten, let him fast.' This is a clear text on the permissibility of intention during the day. But it is said in Fath al-Qadir: this is odd, and what is in Sunan al-Daraqutni is that the Bedouin testified at night, so he ordered us to fast the next day—this is another incident that does not serve as evidence for what we are discussing. As for the second: al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Salamah ibn al-Akwa' that the Prophet ordered a man from Aslam to announce to the people: 'Whoever has eaten, let him fast the rest of his day; whoever has not eaten, let him fast, for today is the day of Ashura.' This clearly indicates that Ashura was obligatory, because the command indicates obligation, and that the obligatory fast is fulfilled by intention during the day, and it requires abstention from dawn; if he intends, it becomes worship and fasting, otherwise not. And what is a clear text on the obligation of this fast is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Aisha: 'Ashura was a day that Quraysh used to fast in the Jahiliyyah, and the Messenger of Allah used to fast it. When he came to Medina, he fasted it and ordered its fast. When Ramadan was made obligatory, he said: Who wishes, let him fast it, and who wishes, let him leave it.' If you have grasped what we have recited to you, it becomes clear that Ibn al-Jawzi's denial of the obligation of this fast is incorrect. And if the validity of intention during the day is established for Ashura and Ramadan, it follows for a specified vow because it is a specified obligation, and specified obligations have no difference. So nothing remains except unspecified obligations like absolute vow, expiation, and make-up, because the day is not specified for this fast. So abstention at the beginning of the day depends only on intention for what is specified for it, which is supererogatory. So they acted on all the evidence as much as possible, and interpreted it as there being no virtue for one who did not intend fasting from the night, and that there is no fast for one who did not intend it to be a fast from the night, even if intention is made during the day. And they specified, after descending to generality, with this fast, and specification is not among far-fetched interpretations. It is better than completely disregarding some evidence as these people did. Then the hadith: 'There is no fast for one who does not intend [from the night]'—also narrated as 'does not resolve' and 'does not determine'—is disputed in terms of being raised, connected, authentic, and weak. As for the first: because Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that it is the saying of Ibn 'Umar, Aisha, and Hafsa. As for the second: because al-Daraqutni said that Abdullah ibn 'Abbad is unique in narrating it from al-Fadl with this chain, all of whom are trustworthy, but al-Bayhaqi criticized it because Abdullah ibn 'Abbad is not well-known and Yahya ibn Ayyub is not strong. And Abdullah ibn 'Abbad al-Basri used to flip narrations, and it is said that Ruh ibn al-Faraj narrated from him a fabricated version. Our noble teachers gave precedence to the authentic agreed-upon hadith of Ashura and acted on its wording and indication, and acted on this disputed narration in accordance with qiyas. This is how one should understand, so understand.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the requirement of intention (niyyah) for fasting, specifically whether intention during the day suffices. The author begins by citing the well-known hadith from Muslim where the Prophet voluntarily fasted after stating he had no food, indicating intention during the day for supererogatory (nafl) fasts. The author then discusses the premise: this only works if fasting is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi); otherwise, part-day worship is not valid. He notes that Imam al-Shafi'i held that part-day fasting is valid but requires abstention from dawn, creating tension. The author argues that in nafl, the intention makes the person fasting from the moment of intention, not from dawn, so precedence of intention over the fast is still required, but this is a legal prescription needing evidence. He then addresses objections: in Ramadan, the hadith about the Bedouin testifying to the crescent is cited as evidence for daytime intention, but the author notes that another version places the testimony at night, weakening that proof. For Ashura, the hadith from Salamah ibn al-Akwa' is presented as clear evidence that the fast was obligatory (the command indicates obligation) and that intention during the day suffices. The author emphasizes the well-known report from Aisha confirming that Ashura was obligatory before Ramadan. He then concludes that if daytime intention is valid for Ramadan and Ashura, it also applies to specified vows (nadhr mu'ayyan). The remaining category is unspecified obligations (nadhr mutlaq, kaffarah, qada'), where intention from night is required. The author explains that the scholars reconciled all evidence by interpreting the hadith 'no fast for one who does not intend from the night' as referring to lack of virtue or absence of a perfect fast, not invalidity, and that this specification is not far-fetched and is better than discarding authentic hadiths. Finally, he discusses the status of that hadith, noting its shaky transmission: some report it as a saying of the Companions (mawquf), and its chain has weaknesses. The preferred approach is to prioritize the authentic Ashura hadith and apply the disputed hadith where it aligns with qiyas.

Key Terms
واجب معين (wajib mu'ayyan): A specified obligatory act, like fasting on a specific day (e.g., Ramadan day, Ashura when obligatory, specified vow).
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; a command that is binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, which type of obligatory fast requires intention from night?
A) Specified obligations like Ramadan and Ashura.
B) Unspecified obligations like absolute vows, expiation, and make-up.
C) All obligatory fasts require night intention.
D) Only voluntary fasts allow daytime intention.

Key Takeaway
The Ashura hadiths provide authentic evidence that intention during the day suffices for specified obligatory fasts, specifying the general hadith that seems to require night intention.

The Ghaylan Hadith: Deriving the Ruling on Keeping Four Wives for a New Muslim
Explaining the ruling for a new Muslim with more than four wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of amr to the Ghaylan hadith and derive the ruling on retaining spouses upon conversion, distinguishing between simultaneous and sequential marriages.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command to 'keep four' requires either renewal of marriage or retaining the first four, depending on whether marriages were simultaneous or sequential.

The hadith of Ghaylan is a key text for understanding how a prophetic command is interpreted in the context of conversion. This lesson walks through the hadith, the Hanafi interpretation, and the usul reasoning behind it. By the end, you will see how a seemingly straightforward command can have nuanced implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its authenticity
Locate the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban. Note that it is declared authentic (sahih). This establishes the dalil.
The chain is sound, but a note about Ibn al-Hajib's error in naming is provided.
2
Extract the general ruling from the command
The Prophet's command 'أمسك أربعاً' (keep four) is a direct command (amr). In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command indicates obligation). Therefore, it is wajib to keep four and separate from the rest.
This is the basic ruling, but it is qualified by circumstances.
3
Apply the condition of simultaneity vs sequentiality
If the wives were married simultaneously, the command requires renewal of the marriage contract (tajdid al-nikah) to select which four to keep. If sequentially, the first four in order are retained without renewal. This distinction is derived from the need to determine which wives are meant by 'keep four' when all are equally valid.
This shows how usul principles (like istihsan or qiyas) may come into play.
4
Respond to the objection of improbability
Some argue it is improbable that the Prophet would address a new Muslim with ambiguous speech. The response is that the hadith is authentic and its meaning is clear to those with knowledge. The lack of transmitted renewal is not evidence against it, as the practice was well-known.
This objection is based on a mistaken assumption about the clarity needed for new Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها قولهم في قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (لغيلان بفتح الغين المعجمة وسكون التحتانية (ابن سلمة الثقفي بفتح السين واللام وابن غيلان خطأ من ابن الحاجب (و) الحال أنه قد أسلم على عشر من النساء أسلمن معه ومقولة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم أمسك أربعاً وفارق سائرهن ومقولة قولهم (أي) أمسك أربعاً بتجديد النكاح إن كان تزوج بهن معاً (أو) أمسك (الأوائل) منهن في صورة التعاقب والحديث رواه الترمذي وابن ماجه وابن حبان وصححه ووجه البعد قوله فإنه يبعد أن يخاطب مثله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم (١) في إبانة الأحكام بكلام خال عن الإغلاق (مثله) أي مثل غيلان متجدد الإسلام الجاهل بالأحكام بمثله) أي مثل هذا الكلام الدقيق المغلق (مع أنه لم ينقل تجديد للنكاح (قط) لا منه ولا من غيره ولو وقع لنقل وهذا وجه آخر للبعد (أقول) (١) قوله : (في إبانة الأحكام بكلام (خال الخ، كذا في أصله وهو غير مستقيم فحرره.
And among them is their statement concerning his saying (peace be upon him) to Ghaylan (with a fatha on the ghayn and sukun on the ya) ibn Salama al-Thaqafi (with a fatha on the sin and lam) – and 'Ibn Ghaylan' is an error by Ibn al-Hajib – while he had embraced Islam with ten women who had also embraced Islam with him. And the purport of his saying (peace be upon him) is: 'Keep four and separate from the rest.' And the purport of their saying is: 'Keep four by renewing the marriage if he had married them all at once, or keep the first ones among them in the case of sequential marriage.' The hadith is narrated by al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban, and he declared it authentic. And the aspect of its improbability is his statement: For it is improbable that he (peace be upon him) should address someone like him in explaining rulings with speech devoid of ambiguity – someone like Ghaylan, a new Muslim ignorant of rulings – with something like this precise and ambiguous speech, especially since no renewal of marriage has ever been transmitted from him or anyone else, and if it had occurred, it would have been transmitted. And this is another aspect of improbability. I say: His statement: 'in explaining rulings with speech devoid of' etc. – in his original it is not straight, so correct it.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the hadith regarding Ghaylan ibn Salama al-Thaqafi who converted to Islam while having ten wives. The Prophet commanded him to keep four and separate from the rest. The Hanafis interpret this as requiring a renewal of marriage if the ten were married simultaneously, or keeping the first four if they were sequential. The author notes that some consider it improbable that the Prophet would give such a precise ruling to a new Muslim with ambiguous speech. However, the hadith is authentic. The author also points out an error by Ibn al-Hajib in naming the narrator, and a textual issue in the original manuscript.

Key Terms
غيلان بن سلمة (Ghaylan ibn Salama): A companion of the Prophet who converted with ten wives.
تجديد النكاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewing the marriage contract – necessary if the multiple marriages were contracted simultaneously.
الأوائل (al-awa'il): The first ones in the order of marriage – kept if the marriages were sequential.

Key Takeaway

Ijmal in the Hadith: The Hanafi Position on Lifting of Mistakes
Debate on whether the hadith about lifting mistakes is mujmal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument that the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' is not mujmal and apply the role of 'urf in specifying ambiguous texts.

Core Idea
Custom before Shari'ah resolves ambiguity: 'رفع' means lifting punishment, not compensation.

The hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (Mistake and forgetfulness are lifted from my nation) is often cited in discussions of legal responsibility. Hanafi usul scholars argue that despite the word 'رفع' having multiple possible meanings, the hadith is not ambiguous (mujmal). Their reasoning relies on customary usage ('urf) before Islam, which specified that 'رفع' in such contexts refers to the lifting of punishment. This lesson examines the debate, contrasting the Hanafi position with that of Mu'tazilite scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested text and issue
Locate the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' and identify that the dispute is whether the word 'رفع' makes the hadith mujmal or not.
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite objection
Analyze why Mu'tazilites (Abu al-Husayn and Abu Abdullah al-Basri) claim the hadith is mujmal: multiple possible meanings (punishment, compensation, validity) with no determiner.
3
Examine the Hanafi response using 'urf
Study the Hanafi argument that pre-Islamic custom ('urf) specifies that 'رفع' means lifting of punishment, thus removing ambiguity.
4
Analyze subsidiary arguments
Consider why compensation (daman) is not punishment (obligatory on children) and why expiation (kaffarah) is for negligence, not punishment.
5
Conclude the role of 'urf
Understand that 'urf acts as a mubayyin (specifier) for ambiguous texts, and in this case, it resolves the ambiguity, making the hadith non-mujmal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : لا إجمال في مثل قوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم (رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان») أي فيما رفع الشيء ولم يرفع نفسه (خلافاً لأبي الحسين وأبي عبد الله البصريين المعتزليين لنا العرف في مثله قبل الشرع رفع العقوبة قيل : إما بتجوز الشيء بعقوبة أو التقدير (وهو المراد ههنا فإن قيل : أليس الضمان واجباً كما في القتل وتلف المال سهواً؟ قال : (وليس الضمان عقوبة ألا ترى يجب على الصبي مع أنه ليس محل العقوبة (بل). (جبر) المال (المغبون) والإنسان الهالك، وأما وجوب الكفارة فلترك التثبت والاحتياط الواجب (ولو سلم أنه عقوبة فتخصيص) الضمان عن عموم العقوبة (الدليل) المجملون (قالوا: الإضمار) ههنا (متعين لعدم ارتفاع نفس الخطأ والنسيان والاحتمال متكثر) رفع العقوبة ورفع الضمان ورفع الصحة ولا معين فتعين الإجمال (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه لا معين (بل العرف) معين فافهم .
Issue: There is no ambiguity in like the statement of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Lifted from my nation the mistake and forgetfulness' i.e., in what lifts the thing and does not lift itself, contrary to Abu al-Husayn and Abu Abdullah al-Basri the Mu'tazilites. For us, custom in similar matters before the Shari'ah is the lifting of punishment. It is said: either by a metaphor of the thing with punishment or by estimation, and that is intended here. If it is said: Is not compensation obligatory as in killing and loss of property by mistake? He said: Compensation is not a punishment; do you not see that it is obligatory upon a child even though he is not a subject of punishment? Rather, it is a reparation for the lost property and the destroyed person. As for the obligation of expiation, it is due to lack of caution and the required precaution. And if it is conceded that it is a punishment, then the specification of compensation from the generality of punishment by evidence. The proponents of ambiguity said: The ellipsis here is necessarily required because the mistake and forgetfulness themselves are not lifted, and the possibilities are many: lifting punishment, lifting compensation, lifting validity, and there is no determiner, so ambiguity is necessitated. We say: We do not accept that there is no determiner; rather, custom is the determiner. Understand.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage addresses the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (Mistake and forgetfulness are lifted from my nation) and whether it is ambiguous (mujmal). The Hanafi position is that there is no ambiguity because custom ('urf) before the Shari'ah determined that 'lifting' in such contexts refers to lifting punishment. The Mu'tazilite opponents argue that the hadith is ambiguous because the word 'رفع' can mean lifting punishment, compensation, or validity, and there is no specifying factor. The Hanafi response is twofold: First, compensation (daman) is not a punishment; it is a reparation, as seen by its obligation on a child who is not subject to punishment. Expiation (kaffarah) is for lack of caution, not a punishment. Second, even if compensation were a punishment, it would be excluded from the general lifting by other evidence. Thus, custom specifies that lifting of punishment is intended, so no ambiguity exists. The passage concludes with 'فافهم' emphasizing understanding.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Customary usage that specifies the meaning of a text
الإضمار (al-idmar): Ellipsis; assuming an omitted verbal object

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the word 'رفع' is used metaphorically for punishment.
B) Because custom ('urf) before Shari'ah indicates that 'رفع' refers to lifting punishment.
C) Because the hadith was narrated in multiple ways.
D) Because the prophet explained it in another hadith.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' is not mujmal because 'urf specifies it means lifting of punishment, not compensation or validity.

The Hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور': An Analysis of Ambiguity (Ijmal)
Usul dispute on whether the hadith is mujmal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies that the hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' is mujmal and identify the role of Shari'ah and linguistic custom in resolving ambiguity.

Core Idea
Negation in Shari'ah texts is not ambiguous when custom specifies the intended meaning.

The hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' is a foundational text requiring purification for prayer. Some scholars, like al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, argued that the phrase 'no prayer' could mean negation of validity, perfection, or benefit, making it ambiguous. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that it is clear, relying on established customs (Shari'ah or linguistic) to determine the intended meaning. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi argument and its methodological basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The issue is whether the hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' is ambiguous (mujmal). Al-Qadi Abu Bakr claims it is, due to multiple possible interpretations. The Hanafi position denies ambiguity.
2
Understand the Hanafi argument using custom
The Hanafi argument proceeds in stages: first, if a Shari'ah custom exists for 'prayer' as the valid reality, the negation targets that reality. Second, if no Shari'ah custom, linguistic custom (negation of benefit) applies. Third, if both absent, the closest interpretation is negation of validity, since what is invalid is like non-existence.
The priority is: Shari'ah custom > linguistic custom > validity (closest to essence).
3
Analyze the exception for negation of perfection
If external evidence shows that the Shari'ah reality is present but lacks perfection (e.g., reciting Fatiha), the negation is of perfection. Example: 'لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب' supported by Quranic allowance for easy recitation.
This is the only case where the negation is not of the reality itself.
4
Recognize the methodological principle
The Hanafi method is not based on arbitrary preference but on custom in similar cases ('urf fi mithlihi). It is a preference among possible metaphorical meanings guided by prevailing usage.
This refutes the claim that it establishes language by opinion.
5
Synthesize the conclusion
In all scenarios, the hadith is clear. The presence of custom or the logical priority of validity ensures no ambiguity (la ijmal).
Thus, the Hanafi position is that purification is required for a valid prayer from this text alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة) لا إجمال في نحو قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (لا صلاة إلا بطهور) أي فيما نفي الحقيقة الشرعية ولم ينتف وجوده الحسي (خلافاً للقاضي) أبي بكر من الشافعية لنا أن ثبت عرف الشرع في الصحيح منها (فنفي المسمى الشرعي (متعين) بالإرادة، لأنه أمكن الحقيقة فلا يترك إلا بباعث فلا إجمال إلا إذا دل دليل من خارج على أن الحقيقة الشرعية موجودة ولم ينتف شيء من أركانه وشرائطه، فيحمل على نفي الكمال نحو: «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب رواه الشيخان، فإنه دل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزمل : ۲۰] واقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن في حديث طويل رواه البخاري ومسلم عند تعليم الصلاة للأعرابي حين لم يعدل أركان الصلاة ((وإلا ) أي : وإن لم يثبت عرف الشرع في الصحيح منها فإن ثبت فيه عرف اللغة وهو نفي الفائدة مثل : لا كلام إلا ما أفاد فهو المتعين بالإرادة فلا اجمال أيضاً) (ولو قدر (انتفاؤهما) أي انتفاء العرف الشرعي واللغوي (لزم تقدير الصحة أي لا صلاة صحيحة إلا بالطهور ولا يقدر الكمال (لأنه) أي نفي الصحة أقرب إلى نفي الذات من تقدير (الكمال) والمجاز الأقرب إلى الحقيقة أولى. فإن ما لا يصح كالعدم) فإن قلت فيه إثبات اللغة بالترجيح والرأي قال : وهذا ليس إثبات اللغة بالترجيح والرأي، بل هذا (ترجيح لإرادة بعض المجازات المحتملة (بالعرف في مثله أي فيما تعدد المجازات . قال :
Issue: There is no ambiguity in like the statement of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: 'No prayer without purification' i.e., in what negates the Shari'ah reality and does not negate its sensory existence, contrary to al-Qadi Abu Bakr from the Shafi'ites. For us, if the Shari'ah custom is established in the valid prayer, then the negation of the Shari'ah name is determined by intention, because the reality is possible, so it is not abandoned without a motive. So there is no ambiguity unless an external evidence indicates that the Shari'ah reality exists and nothing of its pillars and conditions is negated, then it is interpreted as negation of perfection, like: 'No prayer for one who does not recite Fatiha' narrated by the two sheikhs, for it is indicated by His statement: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' [al-Muzzammil: 20] and 'Recite what is easy of the Quran' in a long hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim when teaching prayer to the bedouin when he did not perfect the pillars of prayer. Otherwise, i.e., if the Shari'ah custom in the valid prayer is not established, then if the linguistic custom is established in it, which is negation of benefit, like: 'No speech except what is beneficial', then it is determined by intention, so also no ambiguity. And if both are assumed to be absent, then the estimation of validity, i.e., 'no valid prayer except with purification' is necessary, and perfection is not estimated, because negation of validity is closer to negation of essence than estimation of perfection, and the metaphor closer to the reality is preferable. For what is not valid is like non-existence. If you say that this establishes the linguistic meaning by preference and opinion, he said: This is not establishing the language by preference and opinion; rather, it is a preference for intending some of the possible metaphors by custom in similar cases, i.e., where metaphors are multiple. He said:
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage examines the hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' (No prayer without purification) and whether it is ambiguous. The Hanafi position is that it is not mujmal. The author explains that if a Shari'ah custom ('urf shari) for the term 'prayer' as a valid prayer is established, then the hadith necessarily negates the Shari'ah reality (i.e., valid prayer), so it means 'no valid prayer without purification'. There is no ambiguity unless an external evidence suggests that the Shari'ah reality exists but lacks perfection, as in the hadith about reciting Fatiha, which is interpreted as negation of perfection due to the Quranic evidence allowing easy recitation. If no Shari'ah custom exists, then the linguistic custom of negation of benefit applies, like 'no speech except beneficial', which is also clear. If both customs are absent, then the only plausible interpretation is negation of validity (sihha), not perfection (kamal), because negation of validity is closer to negation of essence. Thus, in all cases, the hadith is not ambiguous. The author also refutes claims that this involves personal opinion, stating it is a preference based on custom.

Key Terms
الحقيقة الشرعية (al-haqiqah al-shari'iyyah): The Shari'ah reality of a term, e.g., prayer with its specific pillars and conditions
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamal): Negation of perfection (i.e., the prayer is valid but not perfect)
العرف الشرعي (al-'urf al-shar'i): Shari'ah custom: the meaning a term takes in Islamic legal discourse (e.g., 'prayer' meaning the specific act of worship).
العرف اللغوي (al-'urf al-lughawi): Linguistic custom: the common usage of a term among native speakers (e.g., 'prayer' as supplication).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis, when is the hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' interpreted as negation of perfection?
A) When there is a Shari'ah custom for 'prayer' as the valid reality.
B) When there is an external evidence that the Shari'ah reality exists but lacks perfection.
C) When there is a linguistic custom for negation of benefit.
D) When both Shari'ah and linguistic customs are absent.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' is not ambiguous; the presence of custom ('urf) specifies the intended negation, making it a clear textual proof for the obligation of purification.

No Ijmāl in 'Lā Ṣalāta illā bi-Ṭuhūr': The Hanafi Rebuttal of al-Bāqillānī
Arguing that the hadith is not mujmal because shar‘ī custom determines the meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of shar'ī haqīqa to determine that the hadith 'Lā Ṣalāta illā bi-Ṭuhūr' is not mujmal but clearly negates the shar‘ī validity of prayer without purification.

Core Idea
If a word has a defined shar'ī meaning, that meaning is default, and its negation is unambiguous.

This passage from Ibn al-Humām's Fatḥ al-Qadīr tackles a classic usul dispute: is the hadith 'Lā Ṣalāta illā bi-Ṭuhūr' ambiguous? Al-Bāqillānī of the Shāfi‘īs argued it is, because 'ṣalāt' can refer to either 'valid prayer' or 'perfect prayer'. The Hanafīs respond that the shar‘ī custom fixes the meaning as the valid prayer, so the hadith is clear. Understanding this argument reveals how Hanafī usul relies on custom, preponderance, and the nearest metaphor to resolve textual ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
The two schools differ on whether the hadith is mujmal (ambiguous). The opponent, al-Bāqillānī, claims ijmāl because 'ṣalāt' is used in two senses (validity and perfection).
The Hanafī position is that it is not mujmal.
2
Analyze the Hanafī 'three scenarios' argument
The text presents three possibilities: (1) a shar‘ī custom exists, (2) only a linguistic custom of benefit exists, (3) neither exists. In every case, the hadith is clear – negation of the shar‘ī entity (valid prayer), negation of benefit, or negation of validity (closest to essence).
External evidence can shift the meaning to perfection, but that is exceptional.
3
Understand the principle of preponderance
The Hanafīs assert that negation of validity (ṣiḥḥa) is preponderant over negation of perfection (kamāl). This is because ṣiḥḥa is closer to the literal essence; the metaphor for validity (invalid = non‑existent) is nearer than the metaphor for perfection.
This preponderance is based on the principle: 'al-majāz al-aqrab ilā al-ḥaqīqa aulā'.
4
Examine the rebuttal of the opponent's claim of multiplicity
Al-Bāqillānī claimed that the shar‘ī custom is shared equally between validity and perfection, leading to ambiguity. The Hanafī response is that the two usages are not equal; negation of validity is far more common and is the default. The claim of multiplicity is refuted by induction (istiqrā’).
This inductive argument grounds the Hanafī position in observable language use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسألة) لا إجمال في نحو قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (لا صلاة إلا بطهور) أي فيما نفى الحقيقة الشرعية ولم ينتف وجوده الحسي (خلافاً للقاضي) أبي بكر من الشافعية لنا أن ثبت عرف الشرع في الصحيح منها (فنفي المسمى الشرعي (متعين) بالإرادة، لأنه أمكن الحقيقة فلا يترك إلا بباعث فلا إجمال إلا إذا دل دليل من خارج على أن الحقيقة الشرعية موجودة ولم ينتف شيء من أركانه وشرائطه، فيحمل على نفي الكمال نحو: «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب رواه الشيخان، فإنه دل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزمل : ۲۰] واقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن في حديث طويل رواه البخاري ومسلم عند تعليم الصلاة للأعرابي حين لم يعدل أركان الصلاة ((وإلا ) أي : وإن لم يثبت عرف الشرع في الصحيح منها فإن ثبت فيه عرف اللغة وهو نفي الفائدة مثل : لا كلام إلا ما أفاد فهو المتعين بالإرادة فلا اجمال أيضاً) (ولو قدر (انتفاؤهما) أي انتفاء العرف الشرعي واللغوي (لزم تقدير الصحة أي لا صلاة صحيحة إلا بالطهور ولا يقدر الكمال (لأنه) أي نفي الصحة أقرب إلى نفي الذات من تقدير (الكمال) والمجاز الأقرب إلى الحقيقة أولى. فإن ما لا يصح كالعدم) فإن قلت فيه إثبات اللغة بالترجيح والرأي قال : وهذا ليس إثبات اللغة بالترجيح والرأي، بل هذا (ترجيح لإرادة بعض المجازات المحتملة (بالعرف في مثله أي فيما تعدد المجازات . قال : مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره نفي الصحة راجع إلى نفي الفائدة، وهي في الشرعيات الصحة كما لا يخفى، فنفي الصحة أيضاً على مقتضى عرف اللغة فافهم. المجملون (قالوا: العرف شرعاً فيه مختلف في الكمال والصحة فإنه تارة يطلق على الكمال وتارة على الصحة (فكان مشتركاً عرفاً شرعياً ولا معين فالإجمال (قلنا : لا استواء في الإطلاقين، بل نفي الصحة راجح ولذلك لا يصرف إلى الكمال في خصوصيات الموارد إلا لدليل) خارج، وعلى أصول الحنفية يحمل على نفي الذات وهو الحقيقة فلا مساغ للاطلاقين (أقول : الخصم يدعي تعدد العرف شرعاً في الكمال والصحة فالملازمة الأولى في دليل المختار) وهي قوله : إن ثبت فيه عرف الشرع تعين (ممنوعة) في زعمه (تأمل) فإنه يدفع بالاستقراء .
(Issue: There is no ijmāl in the like of his statement, peace be upon him, his family, and his Companions: 'No prayer except with purification' – i.e., it negates the shar‘ī reality and does not negate its physical existence, contrary to al-Qāḍī Abū Bakr from the Shāfi‘īs. For us, if shar‘ī custom is established in the valid [prayer], then negation of the shar‘ī named [entity] is determined by intention, because the [literal] reality is possible and is not abandoned without a motive, so there is no ijmāl unless external evidence indicates that the shar‘ī reality exists and none of its pillars and conditions are negated, in which case it is interpreted as negation of perfection, like: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Fātiḥa' – transmitted by the two Shaykhs – for that is indicated by His statement: 'So recite what is easy of the Qur'an' [al-Muzzammil 73:20] and the long hadith narrated by Bukhārī and Muslim when teaching prayer to the Bedouin who did not perfect the pillars. Otherwise – i.e., if shar‘ī custom is not established in the valid [prayer] – but if linguistic custom is established as negation of benefit, like 'No speech except what is beneficial', then it is determined by intention and there is no ijmāl. If both are assumed absent, then it necessitates interpretation as [negation of] validity – i.e., no valid prayer except with purification – and not perfection, because negation of validity is closer to negation of essence than the interpretation of perfection, and the metaphor closest to reality is preferable. For what is not valid is like non-existence. If you say: This is establishing language by preponderance and opinion, he said: This is not establishing language by preponderance and opinion; rather, this is preponderance for intending some of the possible metaphorical meanings by custom in such cases, i.e., where there are multiple metaphors. He said: The author of ‘Maṭla‘ al-Asrār al-Ilāhiyya’ – may his secret be sanctified – [said]: Negation of validity refers back to negation of benefit, and in shar‘ī matters that is validity, as is not hidden. So negation of validity is also in accordance with linguistic custom – understand. The proponents of ijmāl said: Shar‘ī custom in this matter varies between perfection and validity; sometimes it is used for perfection, sometimes for validity; it has become a shar‘ī equivocal, and there is no determiner, so ijmāl. We said: The two usages are not equal; rather, negation of validity is preponderant, and therefore it is not diverted to perfection in particular instances except by external evidence. According to the principles of the Ḥanafīs, it is interpreted as negation of essence, which is the literal meaning, so there is no room for the two [equal] usages. I say: The opponent claims multiplicity of shar‘ī custom in perfection and validity, so the first implication in the argument of the chosen [position] – which is: if shar‘ī custom is established it is determined – is denied in his claim. Reflect, for it is repelled by induction.)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage examines whether the hadith 'لا صلاة إلا بطهور' (No prayer except with purification) is mujmal (ambiguous). The Hanafi position, against Qāḍī Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī of the Shāfi‘īs, is that it is not mujmal. First, if a shar‘ī custom exists for the word 'صلاة' meaning the valid prayer (the shar‘ī reality), then the negation naturally targets that shar‘ī named entity, not the physical existence. Thus the hadith means 'no prayer that is shar‘īly valid except with purification,' and there is no ambiguity. Only if external evidence shows that the shar‘ī reality is present but something is missing, it might be interpreted as negation of perfection (e.g., 'no prayer without Fātiḥa' indicates perfection). Second, if no shar‘ī custom is established, but linguistic custom negates benefit (like 'no speech except beneficial speech'), then the intended meaning is clear. Third, if both customs are absent, the default is to interpret it as negation of validity (i.e., no valid prayer) because that is closer to the literal essence than negation of perfection. The passage also addresses the objection that shar‘ī custom is ambiguous between perfection and validity. The Hanafi response is that negation of validity is preponderant and not equal to perfection; external evidence is needed to shift to perfection. On Hanafi principles, the default is negation of the very reality (i.e., the shar‘ī name), so no double usage. The author supports this by referring to an earlier commentator and by arguing that the opponent's claim of multiplicity is refuted by induction.

Key Terms
الحقيقة الشرعية (al-ḥaqīqa al-shar‘iyya): The meaning assigned by Islamic Law to a word, here 'صلاة' meaning the valid ritual prayer with its conditions.
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamāl): Negation of perfection, i.e., the act exists but lacks some perfection, like reciting Fātiḥa.
الإجمال (al-ijmāl): Ambiguity in a text such that its meaning is not determinable without external evidence; here, al-Bāqillānī claims the hadith is mujmal, the Hanafīs reject that.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Negation of perfection (kamāl)
B) Negation of physical existence
C) Negation of shar‘ī validity (ṣiḥḥa)
D) Negation of all forms of prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī position is that the hadith is not mujmal; it clearly negates the shar‘ī validity of prayer without purification, with no ambiguity.

The Silence of a Virgin as Consent: A Usul Rule from Hadith
Ruling that silence of a virgin indicates consent in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hadith proof for the ruling on a virgin's silence in marriage and apply the principle that silence can indicate consent due to shyness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's statement 'Her silence is her consent' establishes a legal presumption for virgins due to their natural shyness.

In Hanafi usul, specific statements from the Prophet (s.a.w.) provide direct rulings. This passage examines how a single hadith (ahad) governs a socially sensitive situation: a virgin's consent to marriage. We will explore the reasoning that transforms her silence into a legally valid expression of agreement, rooted in the understanding of human nature and modesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
Recognize the question: How does a virgin express consent to marriage when her guardian asks? The passage addresses this specific scenario.
The issue arises because a virgin may be too shy to speak.
2
Extract the Prophetic Proof
Locate the hadith from Aisha (r.a.): The Prophet (s.a.w.) said 'Sukutuha idhnuha' (Her silence is her consent). Note the exact wording and its source (Bukhari and Muslim).
This is a direct statement from the Sunnah, a primary source of law.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (Illat)
Understand why silence is taken as consent: the virgin's natural shyness (haya) prevents her from speaking explicit consent. The silence is a reliable indicator of agreement under these circumstances.
The legal cause (illah) is shyness, which is specific to virgins.
4
Classify the Dalil
Determine the type of evidence: this is a hadith ahad (single-narrator hadith), but it is sahih (authentic). Its transmission is qat'i (certain) and its meaning is clear (qat' al-dalalah) because of the explicit wording.
In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith can still provide definitive rulings if the meaning is unambiguous.
5
Apply the Ruling
Conclude that for a virgin (even if mature), silence in response to the guardian's request for permission is considered consent. This is the mufta bihi position.
This ruling does not apply to a previously married woman, who is expected to speak explicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه أي هذا القسم (سكوت البكر) ولو بالغة (عند الاستئذان) أي عند استئذان الولي إياها بالنكاح فإنه يدل على رضاها، لأن حياءها مانع عن التكلم بالرضا صريحاً، ويؤيده ما روى الشيخان عن أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله تعالى عنها قالت: تستأمر النساء؟ قال: «نعم» قلت: إن البكر تستحي فتسكت؟ فقال : سكوتها إذنها
And from it, meaning this category: the silence of the virgin, even if she is mature, when seeking permission, i.e., when the guardian seeks her permission for marriage, for it indicates her consent, because her shyness prevents her from speaking explicit consent. And it is supported by what the two Shaykhs narrated from the Mother of the Believers Aisha al-Siddiqah, may Allah be pleased with her, who said: 'Are women asked for permission?' He said: 'Yes.' I said: 'The virgin feels shy and remains silent.' So he said: 'Her silence is her consent.'
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents another application of the principle that silence can indicate a ruling. Specifically, when a guardian asks a virgin woman for her consent to marriage, her silence is taken as acceptance. The reason is her natural shyness, which prevents her from openly expressing consent. The proof is the hadith from Aisha (r.a.) where the Prophet (s.a.w.) explicitly stated that the silence of a virgin is her consent. This ruling applies even if she is mature. The Hanafi school uses this as an example of the indication of silence in legal contexts.

Key Terms
سكوت البكر (sukut al-bikr): The silence of a virgin woman when asked about her marriage; it is considered consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's hadith 'Sukutuha idhnuha' establishes that a virgin's silence when asked for marriage consent is legally valid due to her natural shyness.

The Validity of Explanation by Action (Bayan bi al-Fi'l)
Debate over whether action can serve as bayan for mujmal or other texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to defend the Hanafi position that explanation by action is valid by citing the relevant hadiths and rebutting the objection of delay.

Core Idea
Action explains better than speech — 'the report is not like witnessing'.

This passage addresses a key usul question: can the Prophet's actions explain ambiguous texts or general commands, or is only verbal explanation valid? The Hanafi school, based on the hadith 'Pray as you have seen me praying' and the principle that witnessing is superior to hearsay, affirms the validity and even superiority of action-based explanation. The small group (shirdhima) who object on grounds of delay are rebutted systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the issue is whether explanation (bayan) of a mujmal or other text can be accomplished by action (fi'l) as it is by speech (qawl). The Hanafis affirm; a small group (shirdhima) denies.
The passage begins with the ruling: 'يصح البيان للمجمل أو غيره بالفعل كالقول'.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis use both naqli (hadith) and aqli (rational) proofs. The key hadith is 'ليس الخبر كالمعاينة' (the report is not like witnessing), and the Prophet's actual demonstrations in prayer and Hajj. The rational proof is that action is direct witnessing, which is stronger than speech.
The hadith 'صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي' is cited to show the Prophet's action is explanatory.
3
Analyze the objection
The deniers argue that action takes longer than speech, causing a delay in explanation, which is impermissible. The Hanafi response is that some actions are shorter, and even if longer, the stronger explanation is preferred, and prompt initiation counts as promptness.
The text also discusses the example of entering Basra and traveling to Basra to illustrate promptness.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi counter-rebuttal
The Hanafis further argue that the delay is relative to speech, not to the explained matter, and that lengthy verbal explanations also cause delay. The final response is that delay beyond the time of need is prohibited, not absolute delay.
A key distinction: تأخير عن القول vs تأخير عما هو بيان له.
5
Apply the principle
Understand that in teaching Islamic rituals, demonstrating by action is a valid and even stronger method of explanation. The Hanafi school consistently applies this principle.
For example, teaching wudu by showing is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كالقول بل أولى منه إذ (ليس الخبر كالمعاينة) والفعل معاين والقول خبر في التيسير روى أحمد وابن حبان مرفوعاً: ليس الخبر كالمعاينة فإن الله أخبر موسى بن عمران عما صنع قومه من بعده فلم يلق الألواح فلما الفعل يدل على أن بيانيته بالشرع فبطل الدليل الأوّل من كون الفعل مفهماً لأن الفهم حينئذ بالشرع ويلزم أن تكون البيانية بالشرع، ويلغو الفعل إذ به كفاية وليس كما ظن فإن الشرع كاشف عن دلالة الفعل في نفسه لا أنه هو الدال، وههنا بحث فإن هذا الحديث ورد في المدينة، وحديث خذوا في حجة الوداع يوم النحر وكانت الصلاة مفروضة في مكة، وكذا الحج مفروضاً من قبل وكان المخاطبون يعرفون الصلاة والحج ويصلون ويحجون، فليس هذا إشارة إلى بيان المجمل بل الحديث الأول لبيان الصلاة مثل صلاته صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فإنها كانت مشتملة على المندوبات والسنن وحينئذ الأمر للندب الحديث الثاني لبيان أن أمر الحج متقرر على ما فعلت، ولا ينسخ شيء من أفعاله خذوا عني هذا النحو واتركوا النحو السابق، فليس هذان من الباب في شيء، وأما الإيراد بأن خذوا عام في القول والفعل ولا حجة في تبيين الفعل فمندفع بأن العام كالخاص فيفيد أن الفعل يصلح بياناً فتدبر، المنكرون (قالوا) الفعل (أطول من القول، فيلزم التأخير أي تأخير البيان (مع إمكان التعجيل بالقول عند كون الفعل بياناً، وهو باطل، فبطل بيانية الفعل (قلنا : الأطولية) مطلقاً (ممنوعة) فإن بعض الأفعال يكون أخصر من القول ( ولو سلم) الأطولية فلا نسلم امتناعه وأما اختياره الأطول (فلسلوك أقوى البيانين) من القول والفعل، لأن الخبر ليس كالمعاينة (ولو) سلم عدم القوّة فالتأخير لا يمتنع مطلقاً، بل) إنما يمتنع عن وقت الحاجة كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى فإن قلت هذا إنما يتأتى في المجمل أما غيره كتخصيص العام فلا يتم فيه وقد عممت المسألة؟ قلت: إنما يمتنع التأخير فيه عندنا بتأخير يأبى عن صلوحه قرينة وهو غير لازم وقد يجاب أيضاً بمنع لزوم التأخير) ههنا لأنه شرع فيه على الاتصال (لكن الفعل استدعى زماناً) فيوجد فيه فلزم تأخير انصرامه (كمن قيل له أدخل البصرة، فسار في الحال حتى دخلها لا يعد مؤخراً مع أنه إنما يكون الدخول بعد أيام وشهور بل مبادراً فكذا ههنا لا يعد المبين بالفعل مؤخراً (بل مبادراً كذا في «شرح المختصر، قيل ليس من سافر مبادراً (بل مؤخراً لأن (الدخول) الذي مثل به المجمل إذا أمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل فتحصيله في كثير تأخير البتة فلا يكون مبادرة ولو لم يمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل فلا يصلح مثالاً لما في الباب فإن البيان ههنا يمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل بالقول ( ولو قيل : سافر إلى البصرة) فسافر في الحال يعد مبادراً (لسلم) عن الإيراد (أقول : السفر إلى البصرة يتحقق بأول الخروج بالنية إليها والبيان إنما يتحصل بالآخر) فلا يصلح مثالاً له كالدخول : فالمثال المطابق نحو: صم هذا اليوم فشرع فيه) لا يعد مؤخراً هذه الكلمات قليلة الجدوى ليس من دأب المحصلين ( ثم أقول : لو قيل المعنى) من استدلالهم لو جاز البيان بالفعل لزم تأخير حصوله مع إمكان تعجيل تحصيله بالقول) فالتأخير تأخير عن القول لا عما هو بيان له (الاندفع) هذا المنع فافهم لكن يرد عليه حينئذ أولاً النقض بالبيان بالقول المطنب ، فإنه يتأخر بيانيته مع إمكان تعجيلها وثانياً: بأن جواز هذا التأخير لم يخالف فيه أحد، فلا يتأتى دعوى بطلان التالي بخلاف التأخير عما هو بيان له، فإنه قد معاً عليه منع
Explanation is valid for the ambiguous (mujmal) or other (texts) by action just as by speech, i.e., just as it is valid by speech, contrary to a small group. Our proof: an action suitable for clarification, occurring after the ambiguous text (or after speech absolutely), fully conveys the intended meaning, so it is suitable as an explanation like speech, indeed even more so, because 'the report is not like witnessing'. Action is witnessing, and speech is a report facilitating understanding. Ahmad and Ibn Hibban narrated in marfu' form: 'The report is not like witnessing, for Allah informed Musa ibn 'Imran about what his people did after he left, so he did not throw the tablets; when he witnessed that, he threw the tablets.' In al-Durar al-Manthura, it is narrated by Ahmad, 'Abd ibn Hamid, al-Bazzar, Ibn Abi Hatim, Ibn Hibban, and al-Tabarani with the wording: 'May Allah have mercy on Musa; the witness is not like the report. His Lord told him that his people had been tested after him, so he did not throw the tablets; when he saw them and witnessed them, he threw the tablets, and what broke broke.' Perhaps this was an example and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) spoke it. That is why it occurred in Sharh al-Mukhtasar and elsewhere, and the proverb 'The report is not like witnessing' was stated. And Allah knows best. And our proof: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) explained prayer and Hajj by his action to many legally responsible people, and his statement (peace be upon him): 'Pray as you have seen me praying' narrated by al-Bukhari in a long hadith, and his statement: 'Take your rites from me' as narrated by Muslim from Jabir who said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) throwing pebbles on the day of Nahr and he said to us: '"Take your rites from me, for perhaps I will not perform Hajj after this Hajj of mine."' This indicates that he explained by action. I say: Because the meaning of each of the two hadiths is: 'Do what you understand: what prayer is and what Hajj is.' So understanding from action is not by the Shari'ah as was thought in al-Tahrir. It was said: By witnessing. So according to this, the two hadiths being disclosers of explanation by action indicate that the explanatory quality is by the Shari'ah, thus the first proof (that action conveys understanding) is invalid because understanding then is by the Shari'ah, and it would follow that the explanatory quality is by the Shari'ah, and the action becomes superfluous since it is sufficient. But it is not as thought, for the Shari'ah discloses the indication of the action itself, not that it is the indicator. There is a discussion here: This hadith was narrated in Madina, and the hadith 'Take' was during the Farewell Hajj on the day of Nahr. Prayer was already ordained in Makkah, and Hajj was also ordained before. The addressees knew prayer and Hajj and prayed and performed Hajj. So this is not an indication of explanation of the ambiguous, but rather the first hadith is for explaining prayer like his prayer (peace be upon him and his family and companions), which included recommended acts and sunnahs, and in that case the command is for recommendation. The second hadith is for explaining that the matter of Hajj is settled as I have done, and no action of it is abrogated: 'Take from me this way and leave the previous way.' So these two are not from this chapter at all. As for the objection that the word 'take' is general for speech and action, and there is no proof in explaining action, it is repelled because the general is like the specific, so it indicates that action is suitable as an explanation. So reflect. The deniers said: Action is longer than speech, so delay (of explanation) is necessary with the possibility of expediting by speech when action is used as explanation, which is invalid, so the explanatory nature of action is invalid. We say: The lengthiness is absolutely denied, for some actions are shorter than speech. Even if lengthiness is granted, we do not concede its impossibility. As for choosing the longer, it is to follow the stronger of the two explanations (speech and action), because the report is not like witnessing. Even if the lack of greater strength is granted, delay is not absolutely impossible; rather, it is only impossible when it delays beyond the time of need, as will come. If you say: this applies only to the ambiguous; but what about other types like specification of the general? The issue has been generalized. I say: Delay in it, according to us, is only impossible if the delay renders it unsuitable as a contextual indication, and that is not necessary. It can also be answered by denying the necessity of delay here, because he began it immediately. But action takes time, so there is a delay in its completion. Like if one is told: 'Enter Basra,' and he immediately travels and enters, he is not considered delaying even though entry occurs after days or months, but rather he is prompt. So here, the one who explains by action is not considered delaying but rather prompt, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. It was said: The one who travels is not prompt but delaying because the entry (the example of the ambiguous) if it can be achieved in a short time, achieving it in a longer time is definitely a delay, so it is not prompt. If it cannot be achieved in a short time, then it is not a valid example for the topic, because here the explanation can be achieved in a short time by speech. If it were said: 'Travel to Basra,' and he travels immediately, he is considered prompt; this is saved from the objection. I say: Travel to Basra is realized from the first step with the intention, but the explanation is only obtained at the end, so it is not a valid example like entry. A fitting example is: 'Fast this day' and he begins; he is not considered delaying. These words are of little benefit; it is not the practice of meticulous scholars. Then I say: If it is said that the meaning of their proof is: 'If explanation by action were permissible, it would necessitate a delay in its occurrence while it is possible to expedite it by speech,' then the delay is a delay relative to speech, not relative to what is being explained. This refutation is not repelled, so understand. But then it can be objected: first, by a counterexample of an unnecessarily lengthy speech explanation, which also delays its explanatory effect while it could be expedited; second, by the fact that permissibility of this delay (relative to speech) is not disagreed upon by anyone, so the claim of the impossibility of the consequent cannot be made, unlike the delay relative to what is being explained, which is unanimously prohibited.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that explanation (bayan) of a mujmal or other text is valid by action just as it is by speech, contrary to a small group (shirdhima) who deny this. The author provides both naqli (transmitted) and aqli (rational) proofs. The naqli proofs include the hadith 'The report is not like witnessing' cited in various sources, and the actual practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who explained prayer and Hajj by demonstrating them, along with his statements 'Pray as you have seen me praying' and 'Take your rites from me'. The rational proof is that action is a direct witness (mu'āyana) while speech is only a report (khabar), and witnessing is stronger. The passage then addresses several objections: (1) That action takes longer than speech, causing delay. The response is that some actions are actually shorter, and even if longer, choosing the stronger explanation is preferred. (2) That delay in explanation is impermissible, but the response distinguishes between delay relative to the time of need and mere temporal extension; initiating the action immediately counts as promptness, similar to traveling to Basra when commanded. (3) A discussion about whether the two hadiths actually indicate explanation of something unknown; the author argues that the addressees already knew prayer and Hajj, so the purpose was to teach recommended acts and confirm the rites, not to explain a mujmal. However, the general command 'take' includes both speech and action, supporting the validity of action-based explanation. The text then refines the argument about delay, showing that the objection confuses delay relative to speech (which is permissible) with delay relative to the explained matter (which is not), and provides a counterexample of lengthy speech explanation to show the consistency of the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
بيان بالفعل (bayan bi al-fi'l): Explanation by means of action rather than speech
مجمل (mujmal): A word that is ambiguous and requires explanation
معاينة (mu'āyana): Direct witnessing, as opposed to hearsay
شرط اللبيان (shart al-bayan): Condition that explanation must not be delayed beyond the time of need

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why does the longer duration of action not invalidate its use as bayan?
A) Because action is always shorter than speech.
B) Because the delay is relative to speech, not to the explained matter, and prompt initiation counts as promptness.
C) Because the small group never actually objected to delay.
D) Because the Quran explicitly commands action-based explanation.

Key Takeaway
Bayan by action is valid and stronger than speech because action is direct witnessing, and the Prophet's demonstrations are authoritative.

6 min
Defense of Action as Bayan Against the Delay Objection
Refuting the claim that action as bayan causes impermissible delay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi response to the objection that action-based bayan causes impermissible delay, and apply the principle that delay is only prohibited when it misses the time of need.

Core Idea
Action as bayan is valid because delay is only prohibited when it prevents fulfilling the need, not when it takes longer than speech.

This passage defends a key Hanafi usul position: the Prophet's actions can elucidate ambiguous texts (mujmal). Critics argue that actions take longer than speech, thus causing impermissible delay in explanation. The Hanafi response distinguishes between types of delay and shows that starting immediately counts as proactivity. Understanding this argument is crucial for appreciating the full scope of Prophetic Sunnah as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The deniers argue that action is longer than speech, so using action as bayan necessitates delay in explanation, which is invalid. Ensure you understand this logical link.
The objection assumes that any delay is impermissible.
2
Examine the Hanafi response: length is not absolute
The Hanafis respond that not all actions are longer; some are more concise than speech. Even if longer, the Prophet chose the stronger bayan (direct observation over hearsay).
This rebuts the premise of necessary delay.
3
Apply the rule on delay: only prohibited when it misses the need
The author clarifies that delay is only prohibited if it prevents fulfilling the time of need. In the case of the Prophet's actions, this condition is not met.
This is a key principle: ta'khir al-bayan 'an waqt al-haja is haram, but not absolute.
4
Analyze the analogy of entering Basra
The author uses the analogy of a person told 'Enter Basra' who starts immediately; they are considered proactive even if entry occurs later. Similarly, starting the action of bayan immediately makes one proactive, not a delayer.
The focus is on initiation, not completion.
5
Distinguish delay relative to speech vs. delay relative to explanation
The objection confuses two types of delay. The Hanafis argue that the delay here is relative to speech, not to the explanation itself, and such delay is not universally rejected.
This nuanced distinction resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلى هذا أي كون الحديثين كاشفين عن بيان الفعل يدل على أن بيانيته بالشرع فبطل الدليل الأوّل من كون الفعل مفهماً لأن الفهم حينئذ بالشرع ويلزم أن تكون البيانية بالشرع، ويلغو الفعل إذ به كفاية وليس كما ظن فإن الشرع كاشف عن دلالة الفعل في نفسه لا أنه هو الدال ، وههنا ،بحث فإن هذا الحديث ورد في المدينة، وحديث خذوا في حجة الوداع يوم النحر وكانت الصلاة مفروضة في مكة، وكذا الحج مفروضاً من قبل وكان المخاطبون يعرفون الصلاة والحج ويصلون ويحجون، فليس هذا إشارة إلى بيان المجمل بل الحديث الأول لبيان الصلاة مثل صلاته صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فإنها كانت مشتملة على المندوبات والسنن وحينئذ الأمر للندب الحديث الثاني لبيان أن أمر الحج متقرر على ما فعلت، ولا ينسخ شيء من أفعاله خذوا عني هذا النحو واتركوا النحو السابق، فليس هذان من الباب في شيء، وأما الإيراد بأن خذوا عام في القول والفعل ولا حجة في تبيين الفعل فمندفع بأن العام كالخاص فيفيد أن الفعل يصلح بياناً فتدبر، المنكرون (قالوا) الفعل (أطول من القول، فيلزم التأخير أي تأخير البيان (مع إمكان التعجيل بالقول عند كون الفعل بياناً، وهو باطل، فبطل بيانية الفعل (قلنا : الأطولية) مطلقاً (ممنوعة) فإن بعض الأفعال يكون أخصر من القول ( ولو سلم) الأطولية فلا نسلم امتناعه وأما اختياره الأطول (فلسلوك أقوى البيانين) من القول والفعل، لأن الخبر ليس كالمعاينة (ولو) سلم عدم القوّة فالتأخير لا يمتنع مطلقاً، بل) إنما يمتنع عن وقت الحاجة كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى فإن قلت هذا إنما يتأتى في المجمل أما غيره كتخصيص العام فلا يتم فيه وقد عممت المسألة؟ قلت: إنما يمتنع التأخير فيه عندنا بتأخير يأبى عن صلوحه قرينة وهو غير لازم وقد يجاب أيضاً بمنع لزوم التأخير) ههنا لأنه شرع فيه على الاتصال (لكن الفعل استدعى زماناً) فيوجد فيه فلزم تأخير انصرامه (كمن قيل له أدخل البصرة، فسار في الحال حتى دخلها لا يعد مؤخراً مع أنه إنما يكون الدخول بعد أيام وشهور بل مبادراً فكذا ههنا لا يعد المبين بالفعل مؤخراً (بل مبادراً كذا في «شرح المختصر، قيل ليس من سافر مبادراً (بل مؤخراً لأن (الدخول) الذي مثل به المجمل إذا أمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل فتحصيله في كثير تأخير البتة فلا يكون مبادرة ولو لم يمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل فلا يصلح مثالاً لما في الباب فإن البيان ههنا يمكن تحصيله في زمان قليل بالقول ( ولو قيل : سافر إلى البصرة) فسافر في الحال يعد مبادراً (لسلم) عن الإيراد (أقول : السفر إلى البصرة يتحقق بأول الخروج بالنية إليها والبيان إنما يتحصل بالآخر) فلا يصلح مثالاً له كالدخول : فالمثال المطابق نحو: صم هذا اليوم فشرع فيه) لا يعد مؤخراً هذه الكلمات قليلة الجدوى ليس من دأب المحصلين ( ثم أقول : لو قيل المعنى) من استدلالهم لو جاز البيان بالفعل لزم تأخير حصوله مع إمكان تعجيل تحصيله بالقول) فالتأخير تأخير عن القول لا عما هو بيان له (الاندفع) هذا المنع فافهم لكن يرد عليه حينئذ أولاً النقض بالبيان بالقول المطنب ، فإنه يتأخر بيانيته مع إمكان تعجيلها وثانياً: بأن جواز هذا التأخير لم يخالف فيه أحد، فلا يتأتى دعوى بطلان التالي بخلاف التأخير عما هو بيان له، فإنه قد مجمع عليه منع
Thus, this—meaning the two hadiths as revealing the explanation of the action—indicates that its explanatory power is by the Law, so the first evidence (that the action is understood) is invalid because understanding then is by the Law, and it would be necessary that explanation be by the Law, and the action becomes superfluous since it is sufficient; but it is not as he thought, for the Law reveals the indication of the action itself, not that it is the indicator. And here is a discussion: this hadith was revealed in Medina, while the hadith 'Take (rites) from me' on the Day of Sacrifice during the Farewell Pilgrimage—and prayer was ordained in Mecca, and similarly Hajj was ordained before, and the addressees knew prayer and Hajj and prayed and performed Hajj. So this is not an indication of explaining the ambiguous; rather, the first hadith explains prayer like his prayer—peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions—which included recommended acts and Sunan, and then the command is for recommendation; the second hadith explains that the matter of Hajj is settled as I have done, and nothing of its actions is abrogated: 'Take from me this way and leave the previous way.' So these two are not of this topic at all. As for the objection that 'take' is general for speech and action and there is no proof in the action for explanation, it is rebutted: the general is like the specific, so it indicates that action is suitable for explanation. So reflect. The deniers said that action is longer than speech, so delay—i.e., delay of explanation—is necessary, despite the possibility of expediting by speech when action is the explanation, and this is invalid, so explanation by action becomes invalid. We say: lengthiness is not admitted absolutely, for some actions are more concise than speech. Even if lengthiness is granted, we do not admit its impossibility. As for choosing the longer, it is to adopt the stronger of the two explanations (speech and action), because news is not like direct observation. Even if lack of strength is granted, delay is not absolutely impossible; rather, it is only impossible when there is need, as will come if Allah wills. If you say: this applies only to the ambiguous; but other cases like specification of the general do not apply here, and you have generalized the issue? I say: delay is only impossible in our view if it prevents it from being a suitable context; and it is not necessary. It may also be answered by denying the necessity of delay here because he started it in continuity. But action requires time, so its completion is delayed. Like one who is told 'Enter Basra,' and he sets out immediately until he enters; he is not considered a delayer even though entry only occurs after days and months, but rather a proactive one. So here too, the one explaining by action is not a delayer but proactive. This is from Sharh al-Mukhtasar. It is said that the traveler is not proactive but a delayer, because entry—which is the example—if it can be achieved in a short time, then achieving it in a long time is certainly a delay, so it is not proactivity. If it cannot be achieved in a short time, then it is not a suitable example for this topic, because explanation here can be achieved in a short time by speech. And if it is said: 'Travel to Basra,' and he travels immediately, he is considered proactive; this is sound regarding the objection. I say: travel to Basra becomes actual by the first departure with intention, whereas explanation is only achieved at the end, so it is not a suitable example like entry. So a matching example is like: 'Fast this day,' and he starts it; he is not considered a delayer. These words are of little benefit, not the practice of scholars. Then I say: if the meaning of their inference is that if explanation by action were permissible, then its attainment would be delayed despite the possibility of expediting its attainment by speech, then the delay is relative to speech, not relative to what it is an explanation for. This rebuttal is rebutted, so understand. But then it is objected, firstly, by counterexample: explanation by verbose speech, for its explanatory effect is delayed despite the possibility of expediting it. Secondly: the permissibility of this delay is not disagreed upon by anyone, so the claim of the invalidity of the consequent cannot be maintained, unlike delay relative to what it is an explanation for, for it is agreed upon to be prevented.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage continues the defense of the position that the Prophet's actions can serve as bayan (elucidation) for mujmal (ambiguous) texts. The author responds to the objection that actions take longer than speech, thus causing impermissible delay in explanation. He argues that not all actions are longer; some are shorter. Even if longer, the Prophet chose the stronger bayan (direct observation vs. hearsay). Delay is only prohibited when it misses the time of need; here it does not. The analogy of entering Basra or traveling is discussed to show that beginning immediately counts as proactivity. The author concludes that the delay is relative to speech, not to the explanation itself, and this kind of delay is not universally rejected.

Key Terms
بيان الفعل (bayan al-fi'l): Elucidation of a legal ruling through the action of the Prophet
تأخير البيان (ta'khir al-bayan): Delay in communicating the intended meaning after the time of need

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why is an action that takes longer than speech still valid as bayan?
A) Because actions are always shorter than speech.
B) Because the Prophet adopted the stronger bayan, and delay is only prohibited if it misses the time of need.
C) Because opponents of action-based bayan are always wrong.
D) Because speech cannot be used for bayan at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis defend action-based bayan by showing that delay is not automatically invalid; it depends on missing the need, and immediate action counts as proactivity.

Weighing Conflicting Proofs: Tawaf in Qiran
Dispute over whether one tawaf suffices for both hajj and umrah in qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih (preponderance) to conflicting hadith evidence regarding the number of tawafs in qiran.

Core Idea
When actions and statements of the Prophet appear to conflict, the Hanafi school weighs evidence by strength of narrators and consistency with the Quran.

In this passage, we encounter a classic usul al-fiqh problem: two contradictory reports about the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions. The question is whether someone performing qiran (combining hajj and umrah with one ihram) must perform two separate tawafs or one suffices. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of 'Umar and the Quranic imperative, argues for two. This lesson will walk you through the analytical process of weighing conflicting evidence—a core skill in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting proofs
List the different narrations cited: the hadith of 'Umar praising two tawafs, the hadith of 'Ali (action), and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar reporting one tawaf from the Prophet.
The key is to distinguish between reports of action (fi'l) and reports of speech (qawl).
2
Classify each report as fi'l or qawl
Recognize that Ibn 'Umar's report is an action (he did one tawaf), while 'Umar's statement is a qawl (a verbal declaration). In Hanafi usul, a qawl has different evidentiary weight than a fi'l.
The author discusses whether the qawl (Umar's praise) is clarificatory (bayani) or not.
3
Apply the rule of tarjih
The Hanafi school gives preponderance to the report of 'Umar and 'Ali over Ibn 'Umar due to their superior reliability, precision, and fiqh. Also, the Quranic verse 2:196 (Complete the Hajj and 'Umrah) supports the requirement of separate rites.
Qiyas is also used: combining two worships does not reduce the pillars of each.
4
Consider the counterargument
The opponent argues that speech (qawl) should be preferred for clarification. The Hanafi response: speech is only preferred if there is no evidence for the strength of the action; here, Umar's action and the Quran provide that strength.
This shows how Hanafi usul balances qawl and fi'l.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In qiran, the Hanafi school obligates two tawafs, while some others consider one sufficient. The student must understand how usul principles lead to this ruling.
This difference has implications for hajj rituals.

كما مر ، فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت/ الجزء الثاني عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام : دخلت العمرة في الحج واستدلوا لنا بما مر من حديث أمير المؤمنين علي فأوردوا أنه نقل فعل وحديث ابن عمر نقل قول، والقول هو البيان فإن قلت : كشفنا عنك الغطاء وبينا أنه لا وجه لبيانية القول قلت : إنما كشفت الغطاء فيما يعلم القبلية للفعل، وهي ههنا مجهولة بعد وأجاب عنه المصنف ناقلاً عن التقرير أن القول إنما يتعين للبيانية إذا لم يدل دليل على قوة الفعل وترجيحه وههنا قد دل، وهو قول أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه لمن طاف طوافين وسعى سعيين : هديت لسنة نبيك هذا، وهذا الحديث رواه الإمام أبو حنيفة عن صبي بن معبد في قصة طويلة، فإن قلت: قد روي هذا الحديث وليس فيه ذكر الطوافين إنما أخبر صبي بالقران فأجاب أمير المؤمنين بما ذكر ففيه اضطراب؟ قلت كلا فإن زيادة الثقة مقبولة، كيف وليس في الروايات الأخر ما ينافيه، بل هذا مبين للروايات الأخر وكاشف لإجمالها ، لكن هذا غير وافٍ كما لا يخفى على المتأمل، فإن فعل أمير المؤمنين عمر إنما حكم بهداية السنة وموافقتها، وهذا لا يدل على الوجوب أما عند الخصم فظاهر لأن السنة المطلقة عنده تحمل على فعل الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعندنا على الطريقة في الدين وهو يشمل الواجب والمندوب والمواظب عليه، بل نقل الفعلان أيضاً متعارضين فإنه روى الشيخان عن ابن عمر أنه قرن فطاف لهما طوافاً واحداً وقال : وهكذا فعل رسول الله فالحق إذن أن الفعلين قد تعارضا، والقول وافق أحدهما، فإذن توجه بأن الترجيح في مثله للقول فإن قلت الفعلان لا يتعارضان؟ قلت : ههنا علم التعارض من خارج، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لم يحج بعد الهجرة إلا مرة واحدة فإن كان نسكه قراناً كما نطق به أكثر الروايات فهو في حجة الوداع لا غير، وقد نقل الفعلان فقد تعارضا ،البتة وإنما يتعارضان إذا احتمل التعدد، وقد رجح أصحابنا فعل الطوافين بأن رواية أمير المؤمنين عمر وأمير المؤمنين علي رضي الله عنهما، أرجح على رواية ابن عمر فإنهما راجحان في الضبط والاتقان والفقاهة، مع أن هذا مذهبهما ومذهب عبد الله بن مسعود ومذهب عمران بن الحصين رضي الله تعالى عنهم، وهم أرجحون على ابن عمر وأيضاً قد اعتضد هذا بالقياس فإن ضم عبادة إلى عبادة لا يوجب نقصاً في أركان أحدهما، كيف وإذا ضم شفع نفل إلى شفع في التحريمة لا يتداخل شيء من أركان أحدهما في الآخر، مع أن الاحتياط في العبادات يقتضي ذلك أيضاً، والحق في الاستدلال عند هذا العبد أن يستدل بقوله تعالى : ﴿وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٩٦] فهذا يدل بالعبارة على أن إتمام أركان كل واجب فإن معناه : ائتوهما تامين فلا يعارضه خبر الواحد لا سيما الذي حكم بغرابته فيتأول بأنه أجزأه طواف واحد لكل منهما طواف للعمرة وطواف للحج، ويكون الإشارة إلى أن طوافي القدوم والوداع ليسا ركنين فافهم.

وأما الجواب : عن الثاني فبأن الحديث محمول على القرآن لا على أن العمرة، ذهب من البين وقام طواف الحج مقامهما فافهم.
As previously mentioned. Fawatih al-Rahmut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut, part two. Upon him and his family and companions blessings and peace: 'Umrah entered into Hajj. They argued against us with the hadith of the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali, but we responded that it is a report of action, while the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is a report of speech, and speech is clarification. If you say: We have unveiled the matter and shown that there is no basis for the speech being clarificatory, I say: You have unveiled only regarding the priority of action, which is unknown here. The author answered quoting from al-Taqrir that speech is designated for clarification only if there is no evidence for the strength and preponderance of action, and here there is such evidence, namely the statement of 'Umar to the one who performed two tawafs and two sa'ys: 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' This hadith was narrated by Imam Abu Hanifa from Subay' ibn Ma'bad. If you say: This hadith does not mention two tawafs; Subay' only reported qiran and 'Umar responded as mentioned, so there is inconsistency. I say: No, because the addition of a trustworthy narrator is accepted, especially since there is no contradiction in other narrations; rather this clarifies them. But this is not sufficient, as is obvious to the thoughtful. The action of 'Umar only indicates the guidance of the Sunnah, not obligation. According to the opponent, the absolute Sunnah refers to the Prophet's action; according to us, it refers to the way of religion, which includes obligatory, recommended, and persistent practices. Moreover, the two actions conflict: the two Shaykhs narrated that Ibn 'Umar performed qiran and made one tawaf for both, saying 'Thus the Messenger of Allah did.' So the two actions contradict, and speech agrees with one. Therefore preference in such cases is for speech. If you say: The two actions do not contradict, I say: Contradiction is known externally; the Prophet only performed Hajj once after Hijra, and if it was qiran as most narrations indicate, then it was only the Farewell Pilgrimage, and the two actions are reported, so they definitely conflict. They only conflict if multiplicity is possible. Our companions gave preponderance to the action of two tawafs because the narration of 'Umar and 'Ali is stronger than that of Ibn 'Umar. They are superior in accuracy, precision, and jurisprudence, and this is also the position of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and 'Imran ibn Husayn. Furthermore, qiyas supports this: combining one worship with another does not cause deficiency in the pillars of either. The correct inference for this servant is to use the verse: {Complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah} (2:196), which clearly indicates completing each obligation. This cannot be contradicted by a khabar wahid, especially one considered strange. It is to be interpreted that one tawaf sufficed for him: one tawaf for 'umrah and one for hajj, and the indication is that tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-wada' are not pillars. So understand. As for the answer to the second, it is that the hadith is interpreted as qiran, not that 'umrah disappeared and tawaf al-hajj stood for both. So understand.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqh dispute about whether someone performing qiran (combining hajj and umrah with one ihram) needs two separate sets of tawaf and sa'y or one set suffices. The author examines various hadith evidence. The Hanafi position is that two tawafs are required. The key proof is the hadith of 'Umar, who told a man who performed two tawafs and two sa'ys, 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' Additionally, the verse 'Complete the Hajj and 'Umrah for Allah' is cited as demanding completion of each. The argument against the single tawaf view (attributed to Ibn 'Umar) is that his narration is a single report of action, whereas the narrations of 'Umar and 'Ali are given more weight due to their reliability and knowledge. The author also uses qiyas: combining two worships does not reduce the requirements of each. The overall discussion shows how Hanafi fiqh weighs conflicting evidence.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): Combining hajj and umrah with one ihram
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba
ترجيح (tarjih): Preponderance given to one piece of evidence over another based on strength of proof or reliability
قول (qawl): A statement, as opposed to an action (fi'l)
فعل (fi'l): An action, as opposed to a statement

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 'And perform the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (2:196)
B) 'And whoever seeks to perform Hajj, let him do so'
C) 'And complete the rites'
D) 'And do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires two tawafs in qiran because combining acts does not reduce their individual pillars, and the evidence from Umar and the Quran overrides Ibn Umar's single tawaf report.
