Definition of Sunnah in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining sunnah in usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul definition of sunnah and explain why it excludes both the Quran and shadhdh qira'at.

Core Idea
Sunnah is everything from the Prophet except the Quran; shadhdh qira'at is abrogated Quran, not sunnah.

In this passage, the author moves from the Quran (first source) to the Sunnah (second source). The definition of sunnah is carefully constructed to include all non-Quranic prophetic output—speech, action, and approval—while excluding the Quran itself and also anomalous recitations that were once revealed but later abrogated. Understanding this definition is key to appreciating the Hanafi view of revelation and prophetic authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Start with the literal meaning of sunnah: 'custom' or 'way' (al-‘adah wa al-sira). This sets the stage for the technical definition.
Linguistic meaning is broader than the technical.
2
Extract the technical definition in usul
Find the phrase 'what issued from the Prophet other than the Quran, of speech, action, and approval.' This is the core definition.
The definition explicitly includes actions and approvals, not just speech.
3
Understand the qualifier 'other than the Quran'
Notice that this phrase excludes the Quran itself. It also implicitly excludes shadhdh qira'at, which the Hanafis classify as abrogated Quran.
This qualifier is the key to the later dispute with the Shafi'is.
4
See the inclusion of hadith qudsi
The author interprets 'issuing' as 'appearing' to ensure that hadith qudsi (divine sayings narrated by the Prophet) are included within sunnah.
This shows the comprehensiveness of the definition.

لما فرغ من أصل الكتاب شرع في السنة لتأخرها عن الكتاب رتبة وتقدمها على الباقين (وهي لغة : العادة) والسيرة (و) هي (ههنا) أي في الأصول وإنما قيد به إشارة إلى أن السنة في الفقه : فعل واظب عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، ولا يحسن التقييد بالترك أحياناً وإلا خرج الأذان والإقامة ونحوهما، وإنما قيد من قيد زعماً بأن المواظبة المستمرة من غير ترك أصلاً دليل الوجوب وسيتضح لك إن شاء الله تقدس وتعالى وأنه ليس الأمر كذلك (ما) صدر ) وظهر ( عن الرسول صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه (غير القرآن من قول وفعل وتقرير وإنما فسرنا الصدور بالظهور ليدخل الحديث القدسي ويظهر لقوله غير القرآن فائدة (كذا في شرح المختصر ») وإنما أحاله إليه إشارة إلى أنه موافقنا في هذا التعريف ليتجه إليه إيراده المشار إليه بقوله : أقول القراءة الشاذة ليست بقرآن ولا خبر عند الشافعية، ولذا لم تكن (حجة ولو كانت قرآناً وخبراً كانت حجة لأنهما حجتان اتفاقاً (فيرد نقضاً عليهم لصدق التعريف عليها فلا يكون مانعاً؟ والجواب : بأن المراد ما صدر من الرسول بعنوان الخبرية وليست القراءة الشاذة، كذلك تكلف لأن هذه الإرادة بعيدة في التعريفات وإن أجيب بأنه خبر في الواقع وعدم الحجية لكونها مشروطة بالنقل خبراً قال : (وأما اعتقاد الخبرية وجعل الحجية مشروطة بالنقل بعنوان الخبرية فلا يخفى ومنه) لأن بعد اعتقاد صدوره عمن لا ينطق عن الهوى لا معنى لنفي الحجية والحق في الجواب من قبلهم أنها ليست عندهم مما صدر عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لأنه لم ينقل خبراً ولا بد منه، وإنما نقل قرآناً، وهو خطأ بيقين فلا إشكال وأما على ما هو التحقيق عند أصحابنا أن دعوى الصحابي العادل المقطوع العدالة أنه قرآن لا يصح إلا بالسماع من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم والخطأ بيقين إنما هو في بقائها قرآناً لافي السماع فالقراءة الشاذة قرآن منسوخ التلاوة كما مر فليس بخبر وخرج بقوله : غير القرآن فافهم فإنه المتلقى بالقبول عند الحافظين بالأدب .
When he finished the first source (the Book), he began with the Sunnah because it is lower in rank than the Book and precedes the others. (It is in language: custom and practice. And it here means in usul. He restricted it to indicate that sunnah in fiqh is an action that the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) continuously performed, and it is not good to restrict it by leaving sometimes, otherwise adhan and iqama and the like would be excluded. Some restricted it claiming that continuous observance without leaving at all is evidence of obligation, and it will become clear to you, if Allah wills, that it is not so. (What) issued and appeared from the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions) other than the Quran, of speech, action, and approval. We interpreted 'issuing' as 'appearing' to include the hadith qudsi, and the benefit of saying 'other than the Quran' appears. (As in Sharh al-Mukhtasar.) He referred to it to indicate that he agrees with this definition, to face his objection mentioned in his saying: 'I say: the shadhdh recitation is neither Quran nor a report according to the Shafi'is, hence it is not a hujja. If it were Quran and a report, it would be a hujja because both are hujja by agreement. Then there is a refutation against them because the definition applies to it, so it is not a preventer. The answer: that what is meant is what issued from the Messenger with the character of a report, and the shadhdh recitation is not like that. This is far-fetched in definitions. Even if it is answered that it is a report in reality and lack of hujjiyya is because it is conditioned on transmission as a report. He said: 'As for believing it to be a report and making hujjiyya conditioned on transmission as a report, it is not hidden.' Because after believing it originated from one who does not speak from desire, there is no meaning to denying hujjiyya. The correct answer from their side is that it is not considered by them to have issued from the Messenger (peace be upon him) because it was not transmitted as a report, and that is necessary. Rather, it was transmitted as Quran, and that is an error with certainty. There is no problem. As for what is the verification among our companions: that the claim of a just companion with sure justice that it is Quran cannot be correct except by hearing from the Messenger of Allah, and the error is only in its remaining as Quran, not in hearing. So the shadhdh recitation is Quran whose recitation is abrogated (mansukh al-tilawa) as previously mentioned, so it is not a report. So it is excluded by the phrase 'other than the Quran'. Understand, for it is accepted by the preservers of adab.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage begins the second source of Sharia: the Sunnah. It defines sunnah linguistically as 'custom' and 'way', and technically in usul as whatever issues from the Prophet (non-Quran) including speech, action, and approval. The phrase 'non-Quran' is crucial to exclude the Quran itself and also the shadhdh (anomalous) recitations. The commentary then discusses the status of shadhdh qira'at: the Shafi'is consider them neither Quran nor hadith and therefore not hujja. The Hanafis respond that shadhdh qira'at are actually Quran that has been abrogated in recital (mansukh al-tilawa), so they are not sunnah. The definition of sunnah thus excludes them. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi definition is accepted by the preservers.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): What issues from the Prophet (non-Quran) of speech, action, and approval.
الحديث القدسي (al-hadith al-qudsi): A divine saying related by the Prophet but not part of the Quran; included in the definition of sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of sunnah in usul is precise: it includes all non-Quranic prophetic output, explicitly excluding the Quran and abrogated qira'at.

Status of Shadhdh Qira'at: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Addressing the status of shadhdh qira'at and the Shafi'i objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that shadhdh qira'at is abrogated Quran (mansukh al-tilawa) and explain the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Shadhdh qira'at is abrogated Quran, not sunnah, and thus is not a hujja in either school, but for different reasons.

The passage continues from the definition of sunnah to address a critical objection: if the definition of sunnah is 'non-Quranic prophetic output', then shadhdh (anomalous) qira'at would appear to fit, since they are not part of the recited Quran. However, the Hanafis argue that shadhdh qira'at are actually abrogated Quran (mansukh al-tilawa), so they are excluded by the phrase 'other than the Quran'. The Shafi'is, on the other hand, deny them any prophetic origin. Understanding this dispute illuminates how different usul frameworks classify revelation.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
According to the Shafi'is, shadhdh qira'at is neither Quran (since not mutawatir) nor hadith (since not transmitted as a report), so it has no evidentiary value (hujja).
This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that if something is believed to have originated from the Prophet, it must be either Quran or sunnah. Since shadhdh qira'at is not transmitted as a report (hadith), it cannot be sunnah; therefore it must be Quran that was later abrogated in recital.
This is the key Hanafi argument.
3
Understand the Hanafi verification
The Hanafis point out that a just companion's claim that a recitation is Quran must have been heard from the Prophet. The error is not in the hearing but in the assumption that the recitation remains Quran. Hence it is mansukh al-tilawa.
This justifies categorizing it as abrogated Quran.
4
See the thamarah (practical consequence)
The dispute has no practical effect? Actually both schools agree that shadhdh qira'at is not a hujja. The difference is theoretical: Hanafis consider it abrogated Quran, while Shafi'is deny its prophetic origin altogether.
The thamarah may affect how one treats verses that were abrogated in recital but not in ruling.

لما فرغ من أصل الكتاب شرع في السنة لتأخرها عن الكتاب رتبة وتقدمها على الباقين (وهي لغة : العادة) والسيرة (و) هي (ههنا) أي في الأصول وإنما قيد به إشارة إلى أن السنة في الفقه : فعل واظب عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، ولا يحسن التقييد بالترك أحياناً وإلا خرج الأذان والإقامة ونحوهما، وإنما قيد من قيد زعماً بأن المواظبة المستمرة من غير ترك أصلاً دليل الوجوب وسيتضح لك إن شاء الله تقدس وتعالى وأنه ليس الأمر كذلك (ما) صدر ) وظهر ( عن الرسول صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه (غير القرآن من قول وفعل وتقرير وإنما فسرنا الصدور بالظهور ليدخل الحديث القدسي ويظهر لقوله غير القرآن فائدة (كذا في شرح المختصر ») وإنما أحاله إليه إشارة إلى أنه موافقنا في هذا التعريف ليتجه إليه إيراده المشار إليه بقوله : أقول القراءة الشاذة ليست بقرآن ولا خبر عند الشافعية، ولذا لم تكن (حجة ولو كانت قرآناً وخبراً كانت حجة لأنهما حجتان اتفاقاً (فيرد نقضاً عليهم لصدق التعريف عليها فلا يكون مانعاً؟ والجواب : بأن المراد ما صدر من الرسول بعنوان الخبرية وليست القراءة الشاذة، كذلك تكلف لأن هذه الإرادة بعيدة في التعريفات وإن أجيب بأنه خبر في الواقع وعدم الحجية لكونها مشروطة بالنقل خبراً قال : (وأما اعتقاد الخبرية وجعل الحجية مشروطة بالنقل بعنوان الخبرية فلا يخفى ومنه) لأن بعد اعتقاد صدوره عمن لا ينطق عن الهوى لا معنى لنفي الحجية والحق في الجواب من قبلهم أنها ليست عندهم مما صدر عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لأنه لم ينقل خبراً ولا بد منه، وإنما نقل قرآناً، وهو خطأ بيقين فلا إشكال وأما على ما هو التحقيق عند أصحابنا أن دعوى الصحابي العادل المقطوع العدالة أنه قرآن لا يصح إلا بالسماع من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم والخطأ بيقين إنما هو في بقائها قرآناً لافي السماع فالقراءة الشاذة قرآن منسوخ التلاوة كما مر فليس بخبر وخرج بقوله : غير القرآن فافهم فإنه المتلقى بالقبول عند الحافظين بالأدب .
When he finished the first source (the Book), he began with the Sunnah because it is lower in rank than the Book and precedes the others. (It is in language: custom and practice. And it here means in usul. He restricted it to indicate that sunnah in fiqh is an action that the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) continuously performed, and it is not good to restrict it by leaving sometimes, otherwise adhan and iqama and the like would be excluded. Some restricted it claiming that continuous observance without leaving at all is evidence of obligation, and it will become clear to you, if Allah wills, that it is not so. (What) issued and appeared from the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions) other than the Quran, of speech, action, and approval. We interpreted 'issuing' as 'appearing' to include the hadith qudsi, and the benefit of saying 'other than the Quran' appears. (As in Sharh al-Mukhtasar.) He referred to it to indicate that he agrees with this definition, to face his objection mentioned in his saying: 'I say: the shadhdh recitation is neither Quran nor a report according to the Shafi'is, hence it is not a hujja. If it were Quran and a report, it would be a hujja because both are hujja by agreement. Then there is a refutation against them because the definition applies to it, so it is not a preventer. The answer: that what is meant is what issued from the Messenger with the character of a report, and the shadhdh recitation is not like that. This is far-fetched in definitions. Even if it is answered that it is a report in reality and lack of hujjiyya is because it is conditioned on transmission as a report. He said: 'As for believing it to be a report and making hujjiyya conditioned on transmission as a report, it is not hidden.' Because after believing it originated from one who does not speak from desire, there is no meaning to denying hujjiyya. The correct answer from their side is that it is not considered by them to have issued from the Messenger (peace be upon him) because it was not transmitted as a report, and that is necessary. Rather, it was transmitted as Quran, and that is an error with certainty. There is no problem. As for what is the verification among our companions: that the claim of a just companion with sure justice that it is Quran cannot be correct except by hearing from the Messenger of Allah, and the error is only in its remaining as Quran, not in hearing. So the shadhdh recitation is Quran whose recitation is abrogated (mansukh al-tilawa) as previously mentioned, so it is not a report. So it is excluded by the phrase 'other than the Quran'. Understand, for it is accepted by the preservers of adab.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage begins the second source of Sharia: the Sunnah. It defines sunnah linguistically as 'custom' and 'way', and technically in usul as whatever issues from the Prophet (non-Quran) including speech, action, and approval. The phrase 'non-Quran' is crucial to exclude the Quran itself and also the shadhdh (anomalous) recitations. The commentary then discusses the status of shadhdh qira'at: the Shafi'is consider them neither Quran nor hadith and therefore not hujja. The Hanafis respond that shadhdh qira'at are actually Quran that has been abrogated in recital (mansukh al-tilawa), so they are not sunnah. The definition of sunnah thus excludes them. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi definition is accepted by the preservers.

Key Terms
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'a al-shadhdha): An anomalous recitation that is not mutawatir, considered by Hanafis as abrogated Quran.
الحجية (al-hujjiyya): Evidentiary authority; whether a source is binding evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Hanafis classify shadhdh qira'at as abrogated Quran rather than sunnah?
A) Because it was not transmitted by reliable narrators
B) Because it was originally recited as Quran but later abrogated
C) Because the Prophet explicitly said it was Quran
D) Because the Shafi'is do not accept it

Key Takeaway
Shadhdh qira'at is abrogated Quran (mansukh al-tilawa) according to the Hanafis, not sunnah, and is excluded from the definition by the phrase 'other than the Quran'.

The Hanafi Definition of Sunnah
Defines Sunnah linguistically and technically, addressing shadhdh qira'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Sunnah and explain why shadhdh qira'at are excluded from it.

Core Idea
Sunnah is everything from the Prophet except the Quran; shadhdh qira'at are abrogated Quran, not Sunnah.

In this passage, the author defines the second source of Islamic law after the Quran: the Sunnah. You will learn both the linguistic and technical meanings, and see how the definition excludes shadhdh qira'at (irregular recitations) because they were transmitted as Quran and later abrogated in recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions
Find the linguistic meaning (custom, manner) and the technical meaning in usul (what issued from the Prophet other than the Quran).
2
Parse the definition components
Break down the technical definition: 'what issued from the Prophet... other than the Quran, of speech, action, and approval.' Note that 'issuance' is interpreted as 'appearance' to include hadith qudsi.
3
Understand the exclusion of shadhdh qira'at
Read the discussion: Shafi'is argue that shadhdh qira'at are neither Quran nor hadith, so not proof. The Hanafi response explains that they are abrogated Quran (transmitted as Quran, not as hadith), thus excluded by 'other than the Quran'.
Key: the transmission category (Quran vs. hadith) determines inclusion.
4
Apply the legal_definition_dissector
Use the provided dissector: the term 'Sunnah' has hukm (source of law), mahall (Prophetic utterances/actions/approvals), shart (not being Quran), mani (being Quran), and athar (provides rulings).

الأصل الثاني: السنة لما فرغ من أصل الكتاب شرع في السنة لتأخرها عن الكتاب رتبة وتقدمها على الباقين (وهي لغة : العادة) والسيرة (و) هي (ههنا) أي في الأصول وإنما قيد به إشارة إلى أن السنة في الفقه : فعل واظب عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، ولا يحسن التقييد بالترك أحياناً وإلا خرج الأذان والإقامة ونحوهما، وإنما قيد من قيد زعماً بأن المواظبة المستمرة من غير ترك أصلاً دليل الوجوب وسيتضح لك إن شاء الله تقدس وتعالى وأنه ليس الأمر كذلك (ما) صدر ) وظهر ( عن الرسول صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه (غير القرآن من قول وفعل وتقرير وإنما فسرنا الصدور بالظهور ليدخل الحديث القدسي ويظهر لقوله غير القرآن فائدة (كذا في شرح المختصر ») وإنما أحاله إليه إشارة إلى أنه موافقنا في هذا التعريف ليتجه إليه إيراده المشار إليه بقوله : أقول القراءة الشاذة ليست بقرآن ولا خبر عند الشافعية، ولذا لم تكن (حجة ولو كانت قرآناً وخبراً كانت حجة لأنهما حجتان اتفاقاً (فيرد نقضاً عليهم لصدق التعريف عليها فلا يكون مانعاً؟ والجواب : بأن المراد ما صدر من الرسول بعنوان الخبرية وليست القراءة الشاذة، كذلك تكلف لأن هذه الإرادة بعيدة في التعريفات وإن أجيب بأنه خبر في الواقع وعدم الحجية لكونها مشروطة بالنقل خبراً قال : (وأما اعتقاد الخبرية وجعل الحجية مشروطة بالنقل بعنوان الخبرية فلا يخفى ومنه) لأن بعد اعتقاد صدوره عمن لا ينطق عن الهوى لا معنى لنفي الحجية والحق في الجواب من قبلهم أنها ليست عندهم مما صدر عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لأنه لم ينقل خبراً ولا بد منه، وإنما نقل قرآناً، وهو خطأ بيقين فلا إشكال وأما على ما هو التحقيق عند أصحابنا أن دعوى الصحابي العادل المقطوع العدالة أنه قرآن لا يصح إلا بالسماع من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم والخطأ بيقين إنما هو في بقائها قرآناً لافي السماع فالقراءة الشاذة قرآن منسوخ التلاوة كما مر فليس بخبر وخرج بقوله : غير القرآن فافهم فإنه المتلقى بالقبول عند الحافظين بالأدب .
The second principle: The Sunnah. When he finished from the first principle of the Book, he started on the Sunnah because it comes after the Book in rank and precedes the remaining [principles]. (It is linguistically: custom) and manner. (And) it is (here) i.e. in usul al-fiqh. He only specified it to indicate that the Sunnah in fiqh is: an action that the Messenger of Allah, his family, and his companions continuously performed, and it is not proper to restrict it with occasional abandonment otherwise the adhan and iqamah and similar would be excluded. He only restricted it with the claim that continuous performance without any abandonment is evidence of obligation, and it will become clear to you, if Allah wills, that it is not so. (What) issued (and appeared) from the Messenger, peace and blessings be upon him and his family, (other than the Qur'an) of speech, action, and approval. And we interpreted 'issuance' as 'appearance' to include hadith qudsi, and the benefit of his saying 'other than the Qur'an' becomes apparent. (Like in Sharh al-Mukhtasar). He only referred to it indicating that he agrees with us in this definition so that his objection mentioned by his saying 'I say: the shadhdh qira'ah is not Qur'an nor hadith according to the Shafi'is, therefore it is not a proof. If it were both Qur'an and hadith, it would be a proof because they are both proofs by agreement. (It would be a refutation against them because the definition applies to it, so it would not be a preventer?) The answer: that the intended meaning is what issued from the Messenger with the designation of hadith, and the shadhdh qira'ah is not so. This is far-fetched because this intention is far in definitions. Although it was answered that it is a hadith in reality and the non-authoritativeness is because it is conditional on transmission as a hadith. He said: (As for the belief of being a hadith and making authoritativeness conditional on transmission with the designation of hadith, it is not hidden. And from it) because after believing its issuance from one who does not speak from desire, there is no meaning to negating authoritativeness. The correct answer from them is that it is not, according to them, what issued from the Messenger, because it was not transmitted as a hadith, and that is necessary, but it was transmitted as the Qur'an, and that is a definite error. So there is no problem. As for what is the verification according to our scholars: that the claim of a just companion of definite justice that it is Qur'an is not valid except by hearing from the Messenger of Allah, and the definite error is only in its remaining as Qur'an, not in the hearing. So the shadhdh qira'ah is abrogated Qur'an in recitation, as has passed, so it is not a hadith. And his saying 'other than the Qur'an' excludes it. Understand, for it is accepted by those who preserve adab.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines the second source of Islamic law after the Quran: the Sunnah. The author notes the linguistic meaning (custom) and the technical meaning in usul: whatever issued from the Prophet other than the Quran, including speech, action, and silent approval. The definition includes hadith qudsi by interpreting 'issuance' as 'appearance'. The text then addresses a potential problem: shadhdh qira'at (irregular recitations) are not considered Quran nor hadith by the Shafi'is, so they are not authoritative. But if the definition of Sunnah includes anything other than Quran, then shadhdh qira'at would be included, which they deny. The discussion resolves this by clarifying that shadhdh qira'at are not transmitted as hadith but as Quran, and they are actually abrogated recitations. Thus they are not part of the Sunnah. This shows the precision of the Hanafi definition.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): What issued from the Prophet other than the Quran, including speech, action, and approval.
الحديث القدسي (al-hadith al-qudsi): A hadith where the meaning is from Allah but wording from the Prophet, included in Sunnah by interpreting 'issuance' as 'appearance'.
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'ah al-shadhdhah): Irregular recitations not transmitted mutawatir; considered abrogated Quran in recitation, not hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They are not authentic hadith.
B) They were transmitted as Quran, not as hadith.
C) They contradict the Quran.
D) The Prophet did not approve them.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah is everything from the Prophet except the Quran; shadhdh qira'at are abrogated Quran, not Sunnah.

Prophetic Infallibility ('Isma) and the Reliability of Revelation
Theological argument for prophetic infallibility as a rational necessity for reliable revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of prophetic infallibility ('isma) as a non-compelling preventer and evaluate the Shi'a and Mu'tazili arguments using the rational evidence (dalil 'aqli) from trust in revelation.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from sin by a non-compelling preventer, preserving trust in revelation without negating human agency.

This lesson explores the theological foundation of the Sunnah as a source of law: the infallibility of the Prophet. The author clarifies the Hanafi position that prophets are protected from major sins and disbelief, refuting both the Shi'a claim of absolute sinlessness (which paradoxically allows kufr under taqiyya) and the Mu'tazila allowance of minor sins. Understanding this principle is essential for appreciating why the Prophet’s words and actions are authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Define 'isma
Identify the Hanafi definition: a non-compelling preventer (khilq mani' ghair mulj) from sin, so the prophet is protected but not compelled.
This contrasts with the view that 'isma is inability to sin, which is rejected.
2
Identify the three positions
Note the majority (Hanafi) view that sin is rationally possible but not actual; the Shi'a view that sin is rationally impossible; and the Mu'tazila view that only major sins are impossible.
Hanafis hold that minor sins are possible but did not occur.
3
Analyse the Shi'a contradiction
The Shi'a claim absolute infallibility yet allow kufr under taqiyya. This is internally inconsistent and destructive to the argument.
The author argues that if kufr is allowed under duress, the prophet could have concealed revelation out of fear.
4
Apply the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
If a prophet could commit kufr, then no revelation can be trusted. Since we know revelation is trustworthy (by consensus), the premise is false.
This proof is based on the necessity of trust in the message.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the Hanafi view upholds the reliability of the Prophet's sayings; the Shi'a view would undermine it, leading to rejection of many hadiths.
The Mu'tazila position is less damaging but still limits authority.

مسألة هذه المسألة كلامية لكن جرت عاداتهم بإيرادها صدر مباحث السنة لشدة التصاقها بها، وإن كان الأليق أن تورد في المبادىء الكلامية لكونها من المبادىء العامة لتوقف الأدلة كلها على عصمة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم المقرون بكلمة لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله اختلفوا في عصمة الأنبياء قبل النبوّة وهي عدم قدرة المعصية) عند البعض ونسبه بعض الروافض إلى الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري قدس سره (أو) هي (خلق مانع) عن ارتكاب المعصية (غير ملج) حتى لا يكون المعصوم مضطراً في ترك المعصية وفي فعل الواجب وهو المختار عند الجمهور (فالأكثر) من المسلمين على أنه لا يمتنع عقلاً ذنب) (منهم (مطلقاً) أي ذنب كان صغيرة أو كبيرة كفراً أو دونه (خلافاً للشيعة فإنهم لا يجوزون عقلاً ذنباً عليهم (مطلقاً) أي ذنب صغيرة أو كبيرة وهم مع قولهم بهذا يجوّزون عليهم الكفر تقية عقلاً وشرعاً قبل النبوة وبعدها، وهذا من غاية حماقتهم، فإنه لو جوز هذا الأمر العظيم عليهم لما الأمان في أمر التبليغ وهو ظاهر كيف وما من نبي إلا بعث بين أظهر أعدائه؟ فلعله كتم شيئاً من الوحي خوفاً منهم، وخصوصاً من مذهبهم الباطل وحماقتهم الكاملة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ما عاش من وقت البعثة إلى وقت الموت إلا في أعدائه، ولم يكن له صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قدرة لدفعهم مدة عمره وكان يخاف منهم، فاحتمل كتمانه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم شيئاً من الوحي فلا ثقة بالقرآن وغيره، فانظر إلى شناعتهم وحماقتهم، كيف التزموا هذه الشناعات خذلهم الله تعالى إلى يوم القيامة، ثم من أجلى حماقتهم أنهم استدلوا بنفرة الناس على العصمة عقلاً وهو لو تم لدل على عصمتهم عن المعصية مطلقاً فضلاً عن الكفر عند الخوف تقية للزوم، نفرة الناس عنهم بل النفرة ههنا أشد، لايهامه الجبن الذي هو أعلى النقائص والحق أنهم بمثل هذه الأقاويل خرجوا عن ربقة الإسلام، ولذا رآهم بعض أهل الله رضوان الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين على صورة الخنازير كما هو مشروح في «الفتوحات المكية للشيخ الأكبر وارث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بل حكم بعض أهل الله تعالى رضوان الله عليه أنهم يحشرون على صورة الخنازير والله أعلم بالصواب (و) خلافاً (للمعتزلة) فإنهم أيضاً يمنعون صدور المعصية عقلاً (إلا في الصغيرة) فإنهم يجوزونها (وأما الواقع فالمتوارث من لدن آدم أبي البشر إلى نبينا ومولانا أفضل للرسل وأشرف الخلق محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أنه لم يبعث نبي أشرك بالله طرفة عين) وعليه نص الإمام أبو حنيفة في الفقه الأكبر، وفي بعض المعتبرات أن الأنبياء عليهم السلام معصومون عن حقيقة الكفر وعن حكمه بتبعية آبائهم وعلى هذا فلا بد من أن يكون تولد الأنبياء بين أبوين مسلمين، أو يكون موتهما قبل تولدهم لكن الشق الثاني قلما يوجد في الآباء، لا يمكن في الأمهات ومن ههنا بطل ما نسب بعضهم من الكفر إلى أم سيد العالم مفخر بني آدم صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، وذلك لأنه حينئذ يلزم نسبة الكفر بالتبع وهو خلاف الإجماع بل الحق الراجح هو الأول، وأما الأحاديث الواردة في أبوي سيد العالم صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله وأصحابه فمتعارضة مروية أحاداً فلا تعويل عليها في الاعتقاديات، وأما آزر فالصحيح أنه لم يكن أبا إبراهيم عليه السلام، بل أبوه تارح كذا في بعض التواريخ، وإنما كان آزر عم إبراهيم عليه السلام ورباه الله تعالى في حجره والعرب تسمي العم الذي ولي تربية ابن أخيه أباً له، وعلى هذا التأويل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ لِأَبِيهِ وَازَرَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٧٤] وهو المراد بما روي في بعض الصحاح أنه نزل في أب سيد العالم صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : هو مَا كَانَ لِلنَّبِي وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا أَن يَسْتَغْفِرُوا لِلْمُشْرِكِينَ وَلَوْ
Issue: This issue is theological but they customarily bring it at the beginning of the discussions of Sunnah due to its strong attachment to it, although it would be more fitting to bring it in theological introductions because it is among general principles since all evidences depend on the infallibility of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who is joined with the phrase 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah'. They differed regarding the infallibility of prophets before prophethood: it is the inability to sin according to some, and some Rawafid attribute this to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah sanctify his soul). Or it is the creation of a non-compelling preventer from committing sin, so that the infallible is not compelled in abandoning sin and in performing obligation, and this is the chosen view of the majority. The majority of Muslims hold that sin is not rationally impossible from them absolutely, whether small or great, disbelief or less. Contrary to the Shi'a, for they do not deem a sin rationally possible upon them absolutely, i.e. any minor or major sin. Yet despite this they allow disbelief upon them under taqiyya, rationally and legally, before and after prophethood. This is the height of their foolishness, for if this great matter were permitted upon them, there would be no security in the matter of conveying [revelation], and it is obvious: is there any prophet who was not sent among his enemies? Perhaps he concealed something of revelation out of fear of them, especially according to their false sect and complete foolishness that the Messenger of Allah did not live from the time of his mission until death except among his enemies, and he did not have the power to repel them during his life and feared them. So it is possible he concealed something of revelation, thus there would be no trust in the Quran or other things. So look at their atrocity and foolishness, how they committed these atrocities, may Allah forsake them until the Day of Judgment. Then from the clearest of their foolishness is that they argued with people's aversion for infallibility rationally, which if complete, would indicate their infallibility from sin absolutely, even more than disbelief in fear of taqiyya because of the necessity of people's aversion from them. Rather aversion here is stronger, because it implies cowardice which is the highest defect. The truth is that by such sayings they left the bond of Islam. Hence some saints saw them in the form of pigs as detailed in al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya by the Greatest Shaykh, inheritor of the Messenger of Allah. Rather some saints ruled that they will be resurrected in the form of pigs, and Allah knows best the truth. (And) contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they also prevent the occurrence of sin rationally except for minor sins, which they allow. As for what actually happened, it is transmitted from the time of Adam, father of mankind, to our Prophet and master, the best of messengers and most noble of creation, Muhammad the Messenger of Allah, that no prophet was sent who associated partners with Allah for the blink of an eye. Upon this is the text of Imam Abu Hanifa in al-Fiqh al-Akbar. In some reliable sources, the prophets are infallible from the reality of disbelief and from its ruling by following their parents. On this, it is necessary that prophets be born from Muslim parents, or that their parents die before their birth. But the second scenario is rare for fathers, impossible for mothers. Hence what some have attributed of disbelief to the mother of the master of the world, the pride of the children of Adam, is invalid. Because then it would necessitate attributing disbelief by following, which is contrary to consensus. Rather the preferred truth is the first. As for the hadiths reported about the parents of the master of the world, they are contradictory and reported as ahad, so they are not relied upon in matters of belief. As for Azar, the correct view is that he was not the father of Ibrahim, rather his father was Tarikh, as in some histories. Azar was Ibrahim's uncle and Allah raised him in his care. The Arabs call the uncle who raises his nephew 'father'. On this interpretation is Allah's saying: 'And when Ibrahim said to his father Azar' (Quran 6:74). And this is what is meant by what is reported in some authentic books that it was revealed about the father of the master of the world: 'It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists, even if...'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage addresses the theological issue of prophetic infallibility ('isma), which is brought up in the context of Sunnah because the reliability of the Sunnah as a source depends on the Prophet's infallibility. The author defines 'isma as the creation of a non-compelling preventer from sin (the chosen view of the majority). The majority of Muslims hold that sin is not rationally impossible for prophets, but in reality they are protected from disbelief and major sins. The author refutes the Shi'a position that prophets are absolutely sinless yet allow kufr under taqiyya, arguing this destroys trust in revelation. He also refutes the Mu'tazila who allow only minor sins. Finally, he discusses the issue of the Prophet's parents and Azar, affirming that no prophet's parent was a disbeliever, and that Azar was Ibrahim's uncle, not father, reconciling Quranic verses.

Key Terms
العصمة (al-'isma): Creation of a non-compelling preventer from sin, so the prophet is not compelled but protected.
التقية (al-taqiyya): Dissimulation of faith under duress; Shi'a allow it even for kufr, which Hanafis reject as absurd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, what is the nature of prophetic infallibility?
A) It is rationally impossible for prophets to commit any sin
B) It is a non-compelling preventer from sin, protecting from major sins and disbelief
C) They are allowed to commit minor sins but not major ones
D) Infallibility only applies after prophethood

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility ('isma) is defined as a non-compelling preventer from sin, ensuring reliable transmission of revelation without negating human choice.

Prophetic Infallibility from Lying: Intentional and Accidental
Debate on whether prophets can accidentally utter falsehood after prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the majority of usul scholars (including Hanafis) reject the possibility of accidental lying by prophets after prophethood, and evaluate the counter-argument of Qadi Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
The miracle of prophethood guarantees absolute truthfulness, not just intentional truthfulness.

This lesson examines the critical usul principle that prophets are infallible (ma'sum) in conveying revelation. While all scholars agree that prophets cannot intentionally lie, a minority view allows accidental slips. We will explore the majority's proof and the consequences of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus
Locate the statement 'الإجماع على عصمتهم عن تعمد الكذب' — there is consensus on infallibility from intentional lying after prophethood. This is the foundational point of agreement.
The consensus is based on the miracle (mu'jiza) that proves their truthfulness.
2
Understand the majority's extension
The majority (Jamhūr) extend this infallibility to accidental lying (الكذب غلطاً). They argue that the miracle indicates truthfulness absolutely, not just intentionally.
The miracle is a divine endorsement that removes any possibility of error in what they convey.
3
Examine Qadi Abu Bakr's position
Qadi Abu Bakr permits accidental lies. He claims the miracle only guarantees truthfulness in intention, not that the tongue never slips.
He relies on the possibility of unintentional error, which is common for ordinary humans.
4
Follow the refutation (qīl)
The text presents a refutation: if accidental lies are possible, trust in revelation collapses because listeners cannot distinguish between a slip and a true report.
The response that Allah would provide an alert (tanbīh) is deemed impractical, as it requires waiting indefinitely.
5
Apply the principle
Recognize that the Hanafi usul stance is that all prophetic utterances (in conveying revelation) are qat'ī al-thubūt and must be accepted as absolutely true.
This principle underpins the authority of the Sunnah as a primary source of law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بعد النبوة فالإجماع على عصمتهم عن تعمد الكذب فيستحيل عليهم شرعاً، وأما قبل النبوة فالمتوارث عنهم عصمتهم عن تعمد الكذب أيضاً لدلالة المعجزة على صدقهم وأما الكذب غلطاً فمنع الجمهور صدوره عنه عليه السلام لما مر من دلالة المعجزة وما روي في الصحيحين وغيرهما كل ذلك لم يكن في جواب قول ذي اليدين أقصرت الصلاة أم نسيت فمعناه: كل ذلك لم يكن في ظني وهذا صادق مطابق للمحكي عنه، وكذا قول موسى عليه السلام لا في جواب من سأل: هل أحد أعلم منك؟ فقال الله تعالى: بلى عبدنا خضر كما في الصحيحين والمراد بالنفي الأعلمية عن الغير في ظنه فرد الله تعالى ذلك الظن أن يقال إن قول موسى صادق في نفس الأمر، ولم يكن أحد في زمانه أعلم منه، لكن لما لم تكن دعوى الأعلمية لائقة بشأن الأعلم، بل له أن يكل الأمر إلى الله تعالى عاتبه الله تعالى بقوله: بلى عبدنا خضر يعلم أشياء لا تعلمها فلا تليق هذه الدعوى منك، وإن كنت أعلم منه بالأسرار الإلهية فافهم وجوز القاضي أبو بكر صدور غلطاً فمنع هو دلالتها أي المعجزة على الصدق مطلقاً بل اعتقاداً بأن لا يجري على اللسان غلطاً خلاف الواقع، بل إنما دلالتها على العمد فقط قيل لإبطال هذا الرأي يلزم عدم الوثوق في التبليغ فإنه يجوز حينئذ أن يكون قوله من عند الله تعالى كذباً جارياً على لسانه الشريف غلطاً إذ لا دليل للسامع على الباطن غير الأخبار، وإذا جاز فيه الكذب ولو غلطاً انعدم الوثوق وأجيب اللازم عنده حين جريان الكذب غلطاً على اللسان التنبيه بأنه خلاف الواقع فإذا عدم التنبيه فهو الدليل على الصدق فالوثوق باق، ولهذا القائل أن يرجع ويقول يلزم أن لا يكون للأمة وثوق بصدق إخباراته حين السماع، بل ينتظر إلى زمان التنبيه والتزام ذلك بعيد من الأدب والإنصاف فتأمل
And after prophethood, there is consensus on their infallibility from intentional lying, so it is legally impossible for them. As for before prophethood, what has been transmitted from them is their infallibility from intentional lying as well, because the miracle indicates their truthfulness. As for accidental lying, the majority (Jamhūr) prevented its occurrence from him (peace be upon him) due to what passed from the indication of the miracle and what was narrated in the Sahihs and elsewhere: all that was not in response to the statement of Dhul-Yadayn: 'Did the prayer become short or did you forget?' Rather, its meaning is: 'All that was not in my opinion,' and this is truthful, corresponding to what is reported about him. Likewise, the statement of Moses (peace be upon him) 'No' in response to one who asked: 'Is there anyone more knowledgeable than you?' So Allah Almighty said: 'Yes, our servant al-Khidr' as in the Sahihs. The intent of the negation is the claim of being more knowledgeable than others in his opinion, so Allah Almighty replied to that opinion. It may be said that Moses' statement was true in itself, and there was no one in his time more knowledgeable than him. However, since the claim of being most knowledgeable was not befitting the status of the most knowledgeable—rather, he should delegate the matter to Allah—Allah reproached him saying: 'Yes, our servant al-Khidr knows things you do not know, so such a claim is not befitting of you, even if you are more knowledgeable than him in divine secrets.' So understand. Qadi Abu Bakr permitted the occurrence of [a lie] accidentally. He then denied that the miracle indicates truthfulness absolutely, rather only in belief that no accidental lie contrary to reality occurs on the tongue; rather, the miracle indicates only intention. It was said to refute this view: It would entail lack of trust in conveyance, for it would then be possible that his statement from Allah Almighty could be a lie occurring on his noble tongue accidentally, since there is no evidence for the listener of the inner state other than the report. If lying, even accidentally, is possible, trust is lost. The response: The necessary implication, according to him, when an accidental lie occurs on the tongue is a [divine] alert that it is contrary to reality. So if there is no alert, it is evidence of truthfulness, so trust remains. This proponent may retort: It would entail that the Umma has no trust in the truth of his reports at the time of hearing, but rather they wait until the time of the alert. Insisting on that is far from propriety and fairness. So reflect.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage addresses the infallibility of prophets regarding lying, distinguishing between intentional and accidental lies. After prophethood, there is consensus that prophets cannot intentionally lie—this is legally impossible. Before prophethood, it is also transmitted that they are protected from intentional lies because the miracle confirms their truthfulness. The majority (Jamhūr) also prevent accidental lies, citing the miracle and interpreting apparent incidents (like the Prophet’s reply to Dhul-Yadayn about the prayer, and Moses’ claim about knowledge) as not actual lies but truthful statements in their context. Qadi Abu Bakr, however, permits accidental lies and argues that the miracle only guarantees truthfulness in intention, not in the literal utterance. The refutation points out that this would undermine trust in revelation, as listeners cannot distinguish accidental lies from truth. The response suggests that when an accidental lie occurs, Allah would provide an alert (tanbīh), so absence of alert confirms truth. Yet critics find this expectation of alert unreasonable, as it would require suspending judgment indefinitely.

Key Terms
الكذب عمداً (al-kadhib amdan): Intentional falsehood; all scholars agree prophets are infallible from this.
الكذب غلطاً (al-kadhib ghalatan): Accidental falsehood; majority denies it, Qadi Abu Bakr permits.
المعجزة (al-mu'jiza): The miracle that proves a prophet's truthfulness.
التنبيه (al-tanbīh): A divine alert to correct an accidental slip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main consequence that the refutation (qīl) claims follows from permitting accidental lying by the Prophet?
A) It would make the Prophet a sinner
B) It would lead to lack of trust (ʿadam al-wuthūq) in his conveying of revelation
C) It would contradict the Quran
D) It would imply the miracle is invalid

Key Takeaway
The absolute truthfulness of prophets in conveying revelation is a foundational usul principle that ensures the authority of the Sunnah.

The Trust Argument for Prophetic Infallibility
Refutation of the objection that mistaken utterances destroy trust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mistaken utterances by prophets and apply the tanbih principle to defend trust in revelation.

Core Idea
The absence of correction (tanbih) is evidence of truth — trust in prophetic reports is preserved.

This lesson examines a subtle objection to prophetic infallibility: if a prophet could inadvertently utter a falsehood, listeners could never be certain of the truth of his reports. The Hanafi response, rooted in usul al-fiqh reasoning, is that the very absence of a subsequent correction (tanbih) confirms the report's truth. This reveals a core principle: trust in revelation is not undermined by the theoretical possibility of error, because the system of divine notification maintains it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Find the statement by the objector: that if a prophet can mistakenly lie, then the ummah has no trust in his reports at the time of hearing.
The objection is based on the absence of external evidence at the moment of speech.
2
Extract the Hanafi Response
The response uses the concept of 'tanbih' (notification). If the report were false, Allah would have notified the prophet and the community. The lack of notification is itself the evidence of truth.
This is a negative proof: absence of correction implies correctness.
3
Analyze the Counter-Objection
The objector then argues that one must wait for tanbih, which is impractical. The author dismisses this as impolite and unfair.
The counter-objection is effectively refuted by the author's appeal to practicality and adab.
4
Derive the Usul Principle
From this exchange, derive the principle: 'The absence of a specific exception (bayan) indicates continuation of the general ruling.' In this case, the general ruling is that prophetic speech is truthful.
This is a standard Hanafi usul maxim: al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجري على اللسان غلطاً خلاف الواقع، بل إنما دلالتها على العمد فقط (قيل) لإبطال هذا الرأي (يلزم عدم الوثوق في التبليغ فإنه يجوز حينئذ أن يكون قوله من عند الله تعالى كذباً جارياً على لسانه الشريف غلطاً إذ لا دليل للسامع على الباطن غير الأخبار، وإذا جاز فيه الكذب ولو غلطاً انعدم الوثوق (وأجيب اللازم عنده حين جريان الكذب غلطاً على اللسان (التنبيه) بأنه خلاف الواقع فإذا عدم التنبيه فهو الدليل على الصدق فالوثوق باق، ولهذا القائل أن يرجع ويقول يلزم أن لا يكون للأمة وثوق بصدق إخباراته حين السماع، بل ينتظر إلى زمان التنبيه والتزام ذلك بعيد من الأدب والإنصاف فتأمل وأما غير الكذب من الكبائر والصغائر الخسيسة) كسرقة لقمة وغيرها مما يدل على الخسة وإن كانت مباحة (فالاتفاق) بين فرق الإسلام على عصمتهم عن تعمدها سمعاً) عند أهل السنة القامعين للبدعة كثرهم الله تعالى (أو عقلاً) عند المعتزلة والروافض خذلهم يصدر عن يوسف عليه السلام هم الزنا أصلاً والمعنى ولقد همت زليخا أن تقتل يوسف لأجل إبائه عما أمرته، وهم يوسف بقتلها لأنها كانت مريدة لإيقاعه في الحرام ولولا أن رأى برهان ربه لقتلها، أو المعنى أنها همت بالزنا ويوسف عليه السلام لم يهم، ولولا أن رأى برهان ربه لهم، وليس المراد أنه وقع منه الهم، ولو لم ير برهان الرب لفعله، كيف وليس له أثر في الكلام ولا يليق بجنابه تعالى أن يمدح يوسف في هذا الهم، وهذه الآيات سيقت للمدح كما يظهر بأدنى تأمل، وأما قصة داود فغير صحيحة، لأنه لم ينقل عن الرسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بطريق صحيح، بل إنما أخذه المؤرخون عن كتب اليهود فلا اعتداد به، والذي يمكن إليه إلا من يجترىء على الخروج عن ربقة الإسلام فتثبت ولا تخبط (ومنعه) أي صدور الصغائر الخسيسة (الحنفية) رضوان الله عليهم (أقول : وهو الحق فإن صغيرتهم (كبيرة) في حقهم وإن كانت صغيرة في حقنا (ألا ترى مباحات العوام سيئات (الأبرار ألا ترى كيف قال داود الطائي الإمام العارف قدس سره: إمساك مائتي درهم سنة حرام على الصوفي المدعي محبة الله تعالى، هو ومن يجب فيه صدقه خمسه ومائتا درهم لنا، وللعوام يحل، ويجب ربع العشر (وحسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين ألم تر كيف قال السري بن المغلس السقطي ذلك الإمام: إني أستغفر الله قولي الحمد الله حين أخبرني رجل بوقوع الحرق الغالب في السوق وسلامة دكاني، ولما كانت الأنبياء عليهم السلام رؤوس المقربين كانت صغيرتنا كبيرة في حقهم فلا يصح صدورها عنهم، فافهم فهو الحق ولا تخبط وتثبت عليه هذا تمام الكلام فيما بعد النبوة، وأما قبل النبوة فالتحقيق، وعليه أهل الله من الصوفية الكرام أنهم معصومون أيضاً من الكبائر والصغائر عمداً، كيف لا وهم إنما يولدون على الولاية ولا يمر عليهم طرفة عين وهم غير مشاهدين الله تعالى، وولايتهم قوية من ولاية الأولياء الذين لا يتهم مأخوذة من ولايتهم والأولياء محفوظون من المعاصي فافهم وتثبت عليه (و) كل من الحنفية والشافعية (جوزوا الزلة فيهما) أي الكبائر والصغائر بعد النبوة وقبلها بأن يقصد المباح فيلزم (معصية أي فيلزم أمر يكون معصية لو صدر عمداً (كوكز (موسی) عليه وعلى نبينا الصلاة والسلام القبطي فاتون فمات فلزم القتل، وذلك حين أخذ إسرائيلياً ليحمل عليه الحطب، إلى مطبخ فرعون وكان يتأبى عنه، فاختصما، فاستغاث الإسرائيلي بموسى، فنهى القبطي عما كان عليه فلم ينته بل قيل : إنه قال : لقد هممت أن أحمل عليك فوكزه موسى عليه وعلى نبينا الصلاة والسلام تأديباً، فقضى عليه فمات فهذا زلة منه قبل النبوة، وإنما اختار مثال ما قبل النبوة إشارة إلى أن حال ما قبل النبوة وبعدها سواء في عدم صدور الذنب، ولو صغيرة إلا على وجه الزلة وفائدة صدور الزلة عنهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ابتلاؤهم ليستغفروا ويتوبوا فينالوا المنزلة الرفيعة (وتقترن) الزلة (بتنبيه من الفاعل أو من الله تعالى) بوحي لئلا يتأسى فيها ويحصل الابتلاء ثم الزلة ليس فيها عصيان من وجه، بل هي مباح كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِمُؤْمِنٍ أَن يَقْتُلَ مُؤْمِنًا إِلَّا خَطَئًا [النساء : ٩٢] واعلم أنه كما يجوز عليهم عليه الصلاة والسلام الزلة يجوز الخطأ، فيقعون فيما يكون معصية لو لم يكن خطأ، وكذا السهو، وتشنيع البعض على الشيخ الأكبر خاتم الولاية المحمدية قدس سره على حكمه بوقوع الخطأ لإبراهيم عليه وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام في تعبير رؤياه فهم بذبح ابنه إنما نشأ عن غلبة الهوى عليه فلا يستحق أن يلتفت إليه
It occurs on the tongue mistakenly contrary to reality, rather its indication is only upon intent. (It was said) to rebut this view: (Necessarily trust is lost in reporting, for then it would be possible that his statement from Allah the Exalted be a lie occurring on his noble tongue mistakenly, since the listener has no evidence of the inner state except reports. If lying is allowed in it, even mistakenly, trust ceases.) (And it was answered: The necessary consequence at the time of the occurrence of lying mistakenly on the tongue is (the notification) that it is contrary to reality. So when there is no notification, that is evidence of truthfulness, so trust remains. And the objector could return and say: It necessarily means that the ummah has no trust in the truthfulness of his reports at the time of hearing, rather they wait until the time of notification, and adherence to that is far from etiquette and fairness, so reflect. As for other than lying from major sins and base minor sins) like stealing a morsel and other things that indicate baseness, even if permissible, (there is consensus) among the sects of Islam on their infallibility from committing them intentionally, (by hearing) from the Ahl al-Sunnah, the suppressors of innovation, may Allah increase them, (or by reason) from the Mu'tazila and Rawafid, may Allah forsake them. You have known their suspicion and its answer. (And) also consensus on allowing them unintentionally and mistakenly, whether it be an error in ijtihad or intending the permissible in the forbidden. And the secret in allowing that is that it is not truly a sin, and from it is the taslim at the end of two rak'ahs forgetfully. (Except the Shia) for they do not allow them even forgetfully, but they allow them intentionally as dissimulation. It has passed. (And it is permissible to deliberately commit) minor sins other than them, i.e., other than major sins and base minor sins, (without) persistence, for persistence in a minor sin is a major sin according to most Shafi'is and Mu'tazila with cold suspicions, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'And she desired him and he would have desired her if he had not seen the proof of his Lord' [Yusuf: 24] and similar examples from the story of Dawud and Sulayman, peace be upon them. And the answer: that from Yusuf, peace be upon him, no desire for zinā occurred at all; the meaning is: Zulaykha desired to kill Yusuf because of his refusal to do what she commanded, and Yusuf desired to kill her because she was intent on causing him to fall into the unlawful. And if he had not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have killed her. Or the meaning: she desired zinā, and Yusuf, peace be upon him, did not desire. And if he had not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have desired. And it is not intended that desire occurred from him, and had he not seen the proof of the Lord he would have done it. How, while there is no trace of it in the speech, and it is not befitting the station of the Exalted that He should praise Yusuf for this desire. These verses are brought for praise, as appears with minimal reflection. As for the story of Dawud, it is not authentic, for it was not transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions, by a sound chain; rather historians took it from Jewish books, so no heed is paid to it. What can be relied upon is that Uriah was a suitor to a woman, and Dawud, peace be upon him, married her. The most of this is leaving the better choice, and there is no sin in it, neither minor nor major. As for the story of Sulayman, the sound and relied-upon account is that he said: 'Tonight I will approach my wives, and they will all give birth to a horseman who will fight in the way of Allah the Exalted,' and he did not say 'if Allah wills,' as narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari. Perhaps coupling the exception with the speech was not obligatory at that time, so there is nothing in it except leaving the better choice. Everything else that historians transmit is all a mistake that should not be paid attention to, except by one who dares to stray from the noose of Islam. So be certain and do not be confused. (And the Hanafis, may Allah be pleased with them, prevented) i.e., the occurrence of base minor sins. (I say: That is the truth, for their minor sin is major in their right, even if it is minor in our right. Do you not see that the permissible of the common people are the sins of the pious? Do you not see what Dawud al-Ta'i, the imam, the gnostic, said: 'Holding back 200 dirhams for a year is forbidden for the Sufi who claims love of Allah the Exalted,' and it is obligatory to pay zakat on it: 5 dirhams and 200 dirhams for us? And for the common people, it is permissible and one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory. (And the good deeds of the pious are the sins of the near ones.) Do you not see what al-Sari al-Saqati, that imam, said: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah for my saying Alhamdulillah when a man told me of the great fire in the market and the safety of my shop.' Since the prophets, peace be upon them, are the heads of the near ones, our minor sin is major in their right, so their occurrence from them is not sound. So understand, for it is the truth, do not be confused, and be certain. This completes the discussion regarding what is after prophethood. As for before prophethood, the investigation is, and the people of Allah from the noble Sufis affirm, that they are also infallible from major and minor sins intentionally. How not, for they are born on walayah and not a blink of an eye passes while they are not beholding Allah the Exalted. Their walayah is strong, taken from the walayah of the awliya who are not suspect, and the awliya are protected from sins. So understand and be certain. (And) both the Hanafis and Shafi'is (allowed the zalla in them), i.e., major and minor sins after prophethood and before it, by intending the permissible which results in (a sin), i.e., it results in something that would be a sin if done intentionally, (like the punch of Musa, peace and blessings be upon him and our Prophet, to the Copt, so he died and the killing was necessitated. That was when he took an Israelite to carry wood on him to the kitchen of Pharaoh, and he refused. So they argued, and the Israelite sought help from Musa. So Musa forbade the Copt from what he was doing, but he did not stop. Rather it is said: He said, 'I intended to carry you,' so Musa, peace and blessings be upon him and our Prophet, punched him as discipline, and he passed away and died. So this is a zalla from him before prophethood. And he chose the example from before prophethood only to indicate that the state before prophethood and after it are equal in not committing sin, even minor, except in the manner of zalla. And the benefit of the occurrence of zalla from them, peace and prayer be upon them, is to test them so that they seek forgiveness and repent and attain lofty rank. (And the zalla is accompanied) by a notification from the doer or from Allah the Exalted by revelation, so that imitation in it does not occur and the test is achieved. Then the zalla does not involve disobedience in one sense, rather it is permissible, as Allah the Exalted said: 'It is not for a believer to kill a believer except by mistake' [al-Nisa: 92]. And know that just as zalla is allowed for them, peace be upon them, so is error; they do something that would be a sin if it were not an error, and likewise forgetfulness. And the criticism of some against the greatest shaykh, the seal of Muhammadian walayah, may his secret be sanctified, for his ruling that error occurred from Ibrahim, peace be upon him and our Prophet and his family and companions, in interpreting his dream that he was about to sacrifice his son, only arose from the dominance of desire over him, so it does not deserve attention.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of prophetic infallibility (ʻisma) within a usul al-fiqh context. The author, commenting on the matn of Muslim al-thubut, addresses the crucial question: can prophets commit sins, especially minor ones? The passage clarifies that while there is consensus on major sins, minor sins are debated. The Hanafi position is that prophets are immune from all sins intentionally, even minor ones, because for them a 'minor' sin is like a major sin due to their high rank. However, the possibility of a 'zalla' (a slip that results in something that would be a sin if intentional) is accepted, as illustrated by the story of Musa (AS) killing the Copt accidentally. The author refutes objections about trust in prophetic reports by explaining that the very absence of subsequent correction (tanbih) confirms truthfulness. He also analyzes Quranic verses and stories of Yusuf, Dawud, and Sulayman (AS) to show that no sin occurred—only 'tark al-awla' (leaving the better option). The passage ends by noting that even before prophethood, prophets are protected, and both Hanafis and Shafi'is allow zalla. The key takeaway is that prophetic sinlessness is maintained categorically, with subtle allowance for unintentional slips that are not true sins.

Key Terms
عصمة (ʻiṣma): Protection from sin; the quality of being sinless.
زلة (zalla): A slip or unintended act that results in something that would be a sin if done intentionally.
تنبيه (tanbīh): Notification; divine correction of an error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what proves that a prophet's report is truthful?
A) The report itself is self-evidently true.
B) The absence of any divine correction (tanbih) after the report.
C) The presence of witnesses to the report.
D) The prophet's own affirmation of truth.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi trust argument: the absence of divine correction (tanbih) proves the truth of prophetic reports, preserving the integrity of revelation.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Position on Minor Sins and Base Acts
Explanation of Hanafi doctrine on minor sins and tark al-awla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between minor sins, base sins, and the allowance of zalla, and apply the concept of 'minor sin being major for prophets' to refute claims of prophetic sin.

Core Idea
Prophets are immune from all sins, even minor ones; what appears as a minor sin is either tark al-awla or a zalla.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi classification of sins regarding prophets. The passage establishes consensus on immunity from major sins and base minor sins, but then uniquely prohibits even non-base minor sins intentionally, arguing that for prophets, any small sin is magnified. The author defends this by interpreting prophetic stories as examples of tark al-awla (leaving the better) rather than sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Consensus
Note the agreement among Islamic sects that prophets are immune from major sins and base minor sins intentionally. Base sins are those that indicate meanness (khissah).
The Hanafis are the strictest, extending immunity to all minor sins.
2
Understand the Hanafi Innovation
The Hanafis uniquely prevent even non-base minor sins intentionally. Their reasoning: 'their minor sin is major in their right' due to their high rank.
This is based on the principle that the same act can have different moral weight for different people.
3
Apply the 'Tark al-Awla' Interpretation
When apparent sins appear in stories (e.g., Yusuf, Dawud, Sulayman), the Hanafi approach is to reinterpret them as tark al-awla (not choosing the optimal) rather than actual sins.
This protects ʻisma while accepting the text's apparent meaning.
4
Distinguish Zalla
The passage also introduces zalla: an unintentional act that would be a sin if done intentionally. This is the only exception to immunity, and it requires accompanying notification.
Zalla is not a sin, but a test leading to repentance and higher rank.

يصدر عن يوسف عليه السلام هم الزنا أصلاً والمعنى ولقد همت زليخا أن تقتل يوسف لأجل إبائه عما أمرته، وهم يوسف بقتلها لأنها كانت مريدة لإيقاعه في الحرام ولولا أن رأى برهان ربه لقتلها، أو المعنى أنها همت الفاعل أو من الله تعالى) بوحي لئلا يتأسى فيها ويحصل الابتلاء ثم الزلة ليس فيها عصيان من وجه، بل هي مباح كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِمُؤْمِنٍ أَن يَقْتُلَ مُؤْمِنًا إِلَّا خَطَئًا [النساء : ٩٢] واعلم أنه كما يجوز عليهم عليه الصلاة والسلام الزلة يجوز الخطأ، فيقعون فيما يكون معصية لو لم يكن خطأ، وكذا السهو، وتشنيع البعض على الشيخ الأكبر خاتم الولاية المحمدية قدس سره على حكمه بوقوع الخطأ It occurs on the tongue mistakenly contrary to reality, rather its indication is only upon intent. (It was said) to rebut this view: (Necessarily trust is lost in reporting, for then it would be possible that his statement from Allah the Exalted be a lie occurring on his noble tongue mistakenly, since the listener has no evidence of the inner state except reports. If lying is allowed in it, even mistakenly, trust ceases.) (And it was answered: The necessary consequence at the time of the occurrence of lying mistakenly on the tongue is (the notification) that it is contrary to reality. So when there is no notification, that is evidence of truthfulness, so trust remains. And the objector could return and say: It necessarily means that the ummah has no trust in the truthfulness of his reports at the time of hearing, rather they wait until the time of notification, and adherence to that is far from etiquette and fairness, so reflect. As for other than lying from major sins and base minor sins) like stealing a morsel and other things that indicate baseness, even if permissible, (there is consensus) among the sects of Islam on their infallibility from committing them intentionally, (by hearing) from the Ahl al-Sunnah, the suppressors of innovation, may Allah increase them, (or by reason) from the Mu'tazila and Rawafid, may Allah forsake them. You have known their suspicion and its answer. (And) also consensus on allowing them unintentionally and mistakenly, whether it be an error in ijtihad or intending the permissible in the forbidden. And the secret in allowing that is that it is not truly a sin, and from it is the taslim at the end of two rak'ahs forgetfully. (Except the Shia) for they do not allow them even forgetfully, but they allow them intentionally as dissimulation. It has passed. (And it is permissible to deliberately commit) minor sins other than them, i.e., other than major sins and base minor sins, (without) persistence, for persistence in a minor sin is a major sin according to most Shafi'is and Mu'tazila with cold suspicions, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'And she desired him and he would have desired her if he had not seen the proof of his Lord' [Yusuf: 24] and similar examples from the story of Dawud and Sulayman, peace be upon them. And the answer: that from Yusuf, peace be upon him, no desire for zinā occurred at all; the meaning is: Zulaykha desired to kill Yusuf because of his refusal to do what she commanded, and Yusuf desired to kill her because she was intent on causing him to fall into the unlawful. And if he had not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have killed her. Or the meaning: she desired zinā, and Yusuf, peace be upon him, did not desire. And if he had not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have desired. And it is not intended that desire occurred from him, and had he not seen the proof of the Lord he would have done it. How, while there is no trace of it in the speech, and it is not befitting the station of the Exalted that He should praise Yusuf for this desire. These verses are brought for praise, as appears with minimal reflection. As for the story of Dawud, it is not authentic, for it was not transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions, by a sound chain; rather historians took it from Jewish books, so no heed is paid to it. What can be relied upon is that Uriah was a suitor to a woman, and Dawud, peace be upon him, married her. The most of this is leaving the better choice, and there is no sin in it, neither minor nor major. As for the story of Sulayman, the sound and relied-upon account is that he said: 'Tonight I will approach my wives, and they will all give birth to a horseman who will fight in the way of Allah the Exalted,' and he did not say 'if Allah wills,' as narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari. Perhaps coupling the exception with the speech was not obligatory at that time, so there is nothing in it except leaving the better choice. Everything else that historians transmit is all a mistake that should not be paid attention to, except by one who dares to stray from the noose of Islam. So be certain and do not be confused. (And the Hanafis, may Allah be pleased with them, prevented) i.e., the occurrence of base minor sins. (I say: That is the truth, for their minor sin is major in their right, even if it is minor in our right. Do you not see that the permissible of the common people are the sins of the pious? Do you not see what Dawud al-Ta'i, the imam, the gnostic, said: 'Holding back 200 dirhams for a year is forbidden for the Sufi who claims love of Allah the Exalted,' and it is obligatory to pay zakat on it: 5 dirhams and 200 dirhams for us? And for the common people, it is permissible and one-quarter of a tenth is obligatory. (And the good deeds of the pious are the sins of the near ones.) Do you not see what al-Sari al-Saqati, that imam, said: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah for my saying Alhamdulillah when a man told me of the great fire in the market and the safety of my shop.' Since the prophets, peace be upon them, are the heads of the near ones, our minor sin is major in their right, so their occurrence from them is not sound. So understand, for it is the truth, do not be confused, and be certain. This completes the discussion regarding what is after prophethood. As for before prophethood, the investigation is, and the people of Allah from the noble Sufis affirm, that they are also infallible from major and minor sins intentionally. How not, for they are born on walayah and not a blink of an eye passes while they are not beholding Allah the Exalted. Their walayah is strong, taken from the walayah of the awliya who are not suspect, and the awliya are protected from sins. So understand and be certain. (And) both the Hanafis and Shafi'is (allowed the zalla in them), i.e., major and minor sins after prophethood and before it, by intending the permissible which results in (a sin), i.e., it results in something that would be a sin if done intentionally, (like the punch of Musa, peace and blessings be upon him and our Prophet, to the Copt, so he died and the killing was necessitated. That was when he took an Israelite to carry wood on him to the kitchen of Pharaoh, and he refused. So they argued, and the Israelite sought help from Musa. So Musa forbade the Copt from what he was doing, but he did not stop. Rather it is said: He said, 'I intended to carry you,' so Musa, peace and blessings be upon him and our Prophet, punched him as discipline, and he passed away and died. So this is a zalla from him before prophethood. And he chose the example from before prophethood only to indicate that the state before prophethood and after it are equal in not committing sin, even minor, except in the manner of zalla. And the benefit of the occurrence of zalla from them, peace and prayer be upon them, is to test them so that they seek forgiveness and repent and attain lofty rank. (And the zalla is accompanied) by a notification from the doer or from Allah the Exalted by revelation, so that imitation in it does not occur and the test is achieved. Then the zalla does not involve disobedience in one sense, rather it is permissible, as Allah the Exalted said: 'It is not for a believer to kill a believer except by mistake' [al-Nisa: 92]. And know that just as zalla is allowed for them, peace be upon them, so is error; they do something that would be a sin if it were not an error, and likewise forgetfulness. And the criticism of some against the greatest shaykh, the seal of Muhammadian walayah, may his secret be sanctified, for his ruling that error occurred from Ibrahim, peace be upon him and our Prophet and his family and companions, in interpreting his dream that he was about to sacrifice his son, only arose from the dominance of desire over him, so it does not deserve attention.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of prophetic infallibility (ʻisma) within a usul al-fiqh context. The author, commenting on the matn of Muslim al-thubut, addresses the crucial question: can prophets commit sins, especially minor ones? The passage clarifies that while there is consensus on major sins, minor sins are debated. The Hanafi position is that prophets are immune from all sins intentionally, even minor ones, because for them a 'minor' sin is like a major sin due to their high rank. However, the possibility of a 'zalla' (a slip that results in something that would be a sin if intentional) is accepted, as illustrated by the story of Musa (AS) killing the Copt accidentally. The author refutes objections about trust in prophetic reports by explaining that the very absence of subsequent correction (tanbih) confirms truthfulness. He also analyzes Quranic verses and stories of Yusuf, Dawud, and Sulayman (AS) to show that no sin occurred—only 'tark al-awla' (leaving the better option). The passage ends by noting that even before prophethood, prophets are protected, and both Hanafis and Shafi'is allow zalla. The key takeaway is that prophetic sinlessness is maintained categorically, with subtle allowance for unintentional slips that are not true sins.

Key Terms
صغيرة خسيسة (ṣaghīra khasīsa): A base minor sin; an act that is trivial but indicates low character (e.g., stealing a morsel).
ترك الأولى (tark al-awla): Leaving the better choice; an act that is not sinful but falls short of the ideal.
إصرار (iṣrār): Persistence in a minor sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why cannot a prophet commit a minor sin intentionally, even a non-base one?
A) Because prophets are always under divine supervision.
B) Because what is a minor sin for us is a major sin for them due to their high rank.
C) Because prophets lose their prophethood if they sin.
D) Because minor sins are only forbidden after prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds prophets immune from all sins, including minor ones, because their high rank magnifies any shortcoming into a major matter; apparent sins are explained as tark al-awla or zalla.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Concept of Zalla: Unintentional Slips and Their Purpose
Definition and purpose of zalla in prophetic life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define zalla in the Hanafi tradition, explain its conditions (unintentional, accompanied by notification), and state its purpose as a test leading to higher rank.

Core Idea
Zalla is an unintentional slip that is not a sin; it serves as a test for prophets, leading to repentance and elevation.

The passage concludes by addressing the concept of zalla (slip). Unlike intentional acts, zalla is allowed for prophets before and after prophethood. The example of Musa (AS) accidentally killing the Copt illustrates a zalla that occurred before prophethood. The passage emphasizes that zalla is always accompanied by notification (tanbih) to prevent imitation, and its purpose is to test the prophet and allow them to achieve higher ranks through repentance. This lesson clarifies the delicate balance between complete immunity from sin and the possibility of unintentional errors that are not sinful.

Guided Path
1
Define Zalla
Zalla is an act that would be a sin if done intentionally, but occurs unintentionally. It is not a sin (ma'siya) in reality.
The passage says: 'ليس معصية حقيقة' (it is not truly a sin).
2
Identify the Example
Musa (AS) punched a Copt to discipline him, and the man died. Musa intended only discipline, not killing. This is a zalla from before prophethood.
The passage uses this to show that zalla is possible even before prophethood.
3
Understand the Purpose
Zalla is a test (ibtila) for prophets, allowing them to seek forgiveness and repent, thereby attaining higher rank (al-manzila al-rafi'a).
It is not a punishment but a means of spiritual growth.
4
Note the Notification (Tanbih)
Every zalla is accompanied by a tanbih (notification) from the prophet himself or from Allah, so that people do not imitate the act.
This preserves the prophet's role as a perfect exemplar.
5
Distinguish from Forgetfulness (Sahw)
Forgetfulness is similar to zalla; both are unintentional. The passage mentions the taslim after two rak'ahs as an example of sahw that is not a sin.
The key is absence of intent to disobey.
