ثم أجاب عن قياسهم بقوله : (وأما تكذيب مدعي الرسالة عند عدم ظهور صدقه (فإنه بخلاف العادة) أي تكذيبه بسبب كون هذه الدعوى من غير بينة خلاف العادة (وهي) أي العادة توجب العلم قطعاً) فبهذا الوجه يعلم كذبه، لا لأنه لم يعلم صدقه، فقياسكم مع الفارق (وقيل) توجب العادة العلم (ظناً) فيظن بكذبه ، فلا علم في الأصل حتى يقاس عليه، لكن هذا خلاف الضرورة، فإن مدعي الرسالة العاجز عن إقامة معجزة مقطوع الكذب من غير ريب فافهم (وأيضاً) تقسيم آخر للخبر هو (متواتر إن كان خبر جماعة يفيد العلم بنفسه) أي من حيث إنه خبر هؤلاء المخبرين (لا) بالقرائن المنفصلة عن الخبر (بخلاف القرائن (اللازمة) له (من أحوال في المخبر) المتكلم (والمخبر ) السامع (والمخبر عنه) وهو مضمون الخبر فإن لهذه الأحوال دخلاً في إفادة العلم كما لا يخفى (ولذلك) أي لأجل كونه مفيداً للعلم بالنظر إلى أحوال المتكلم والسامع ومضمون الخبر يتفاوت عدد التواتر) بتفاوت الخبر، فأخبار العدول الأقلين ربما يفيد العلم دون الفسقة الأكثرين وكذا بتفاوت ،السامعين، فإن الأخبار عند ذي سلطنة يؤذي من كذب عنده من أقلين يفيد العلم دون أكثرين عند غيره، وكذا بتفاوت مضمون الخبر، فإن أخبار دخاليل الملك عن أسراره وإن كانوا أقلين يفيد العلم دون أكثرين غيرهم، وهذا كله ضروري (وإلا يكن خبر جماعة كذلك فخبر (الواحد وهذا التقسيم يشمل جميع الأخبار، لكن الظاهر أن المقصود تقسيم الخبر المروي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، إذ هو المطمح لنظر الأصولي ويؤيده ما بعده (فإن رواه) أي خبر الواحد رجل (واحد) فقط بأن يكون في السند واحد في مرتبة وإن كان الرواة أكثر من مرتبة أخرى فهو الغريب وإن رواه (اثنان ولا ينقض عن اثنين الرواة في كل مرتبة ولا يزيد عليه في مرتبة ما وإن زاد في أخرى فهو العزيز وليس شرطاً للصحيح من الخبر فالغريب أيضاً يكون صحيحاً و واجب العمل لعدم فرق الأدلة الدالة على الحجية (ولا) (للبخاري) الإمام محمد بن إسماعيل صاحب الصحيح رحمة الله عليه (في) المذهب (الصحيح) وإن زعم البعض أنه شرط العزة
The second source / Sunnah. (It is said that) when (actions) are attributed to people of intention, it is immediately understood that they are done with intention, so that is the meaning. Even if intention is not part of the concept of those actions, lying is among these actions; thus it is immediately understood that it is done with intention, so what is negated is the intention, not absolute lying. And (the commentator) said in Sharh al-Mukhtasar: What settles the dispute is the consensus that if a Jew says 'Islam is true', we judge him truthful, even though it contradicts his false belief; and if he says the opposite, we judge him lying, even though it agrees with his false belief. So it is known that conformity with belief is not included in the concept of truth, nor is it its essence, so understand. Also: The report is either known to be true necessarily by itself – that is, by virtue of being a report emanating from reporters – and that is mutawatir; or known to be true necessarily by something else – and that is the report that agrees with necessary knowledge that is known whether reported or not, such as 'one is half of two', for its content is known necessarily whether reported or not; or known to be true by reflection, such as the report of Allah the Exalted and the Messenger, for its truth is known through the intermediary that the report emanates from Allah and His Messenger, and everything that emanates from them is truthful. This is for one who has not reached the station of witnessing and intuition; as for one who has reached these two stations, it is known to be true necessarily. And the report of the people of consensus, the report that agrees with correct reflection in certain matters such as geometry and arithmetic. On this basis, the solitary report accompanied by contextual indicators is excluded, so an objection arises regarding the incompleteness of the classification for those who consider it knowledge-yielding, unless it is included in what yields knowledge by reflection or is known to be false necessarily or by reflection. And it is every report that contradicts – that is, contradicts what is known to be true – or nothing is known about it, i.e., about its truth or falsity. So one of them may be presumed, like the report of a solitary just narrator, for it is presumed truthful with the possibility of forgetfulness and error; and the report of a solitary liar, for it is presumed false with the possibility of truth, for a liar may sometimes be truthful; and sometimes they are equal in truth and falsehood, like the unknown narrator, i.e., the solitary report of one whose justice and lying are unknown. So they said, but there is an objection against it: his report is considered a proof according to some; indeed his testimony is accepted by the Imam al-Humam (may Allah be pleased with him); indeed his narration is also accepted according to what is transmitted from him outside the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). So how can his report be equal in truth and falsehood? Rather, it is presumed truthful, but the presumption is weak. Some Zahiris said: Everything whose truth is not known, its falsehood is known. But what appears is that they meant by it decisive conformity (like the report of a claimant of prophethood), i.e., they analogized to the report of a claimant of prophethood, for when his truth is not known by showing miracles, he is decisively judged false, because reports are equal. And this (the Zahiri statement) is false because it necessitates the raising of two contradictories, which necessitates their conjunction. Since the falsehood of each necessitates the truth of the other, their falsehood necessitates their truth. There is no impossibility in the relationship between an impossibility and its opposite; rather it is the truth as established by the consequent syllogisms. For detail, there is another place concerning the reports of two unknowns with two contradictories. Its detail: If an unknown person reports a report, his truth is not known, so his falsehood is known. Then if another unknown reports its opposite, his truth is not known, so his falsehood is also known, thus necessitating the raising of the two contradictories. That itself being impossible necessitates their conjunction. The commentator of al-Mukhtasar confined himself to the necessity of their conjunction, and building on this approach lengthens the distance, for their raising is impossible like their conjunction. So it is better to formulate his statement: If an unknown reports his report, his truth is not known, so his falsehood is known, then the truth of its opposite is known. Similarly in reporting its opposite. But the objector may object that if the falsehood of the unknown's report is known, then the truth of its opposite is known; so the report of that opposite by another unknown is not something whose truth is not known; rather it is known because its content agrees with knowledge, whether necessary or theoretical. But the matter is easy, for the invalidity of this opinion is necessary and independent of explanation, and what is mentioned is a reminder, so understand. I say: This, i.e., the necessity of raising the two contradictories necessitating their conjunction, is based on the fact that conformity to reality is considered in knowledge as is understood customarily, linguistically, and legally. Because if it also includes ignorance, then raising the two contradictories is not necessary in reality. In that case, the mentioned classification into known truth, known falsehood, presumed one of them, and equal is not exhaustive, since a report that agrees with compound ignorance – which is decisive judgment not conforming to reality – contains neither knowledge (due to lack of conformity) nor presumption nor doubt, because in them there is allowance for the opposing side, whether preponderant or equal, whereas the person of compound ignorance is decisive with no allowance at all for the opposite. So reflect, for the matter is easy: The purpose of the classification is not exhaustiveness, but rather to refute those who claim limitation to known truth and known falsehood. So reflect. This. Then he answered their analogy by saying: As for disbelieving a claimant of prophethood when his truth does not appear, it is contrary to custom, i.e., disbelieving him because this claim without evidence is contrary to custom, and custom necessitates knowledge decisively. So by this aspect his falsehood is known, not because his truth is not known. So your analogy is flawed. And it is said: Custom necessitates knowledge as presumption, so he is presumed false, so there is no knowledge originally to analogize from. But this contradicts necessity, for a claimant of prophethood unable to perform a miracle is decisively false without doubt, so understand. And also: Another classification of the report is: Mutawatir if it is a report of a group that yields knowledge by itself, i.e., by virtue of being a report of these reporters, not by separate contextual indicators, unlike necessary indicators from the circumstances of the speaker, the listener, and the subject matter, for these circumstances have a role in yielding knowledge, as is not hidden. Therefore, due to its being knowledge-yielding with respect to the circumstances of the speaker, listener, and content, the number of tawatur varies according to the variation of the report. For reports from fewer just persons may yield knowledge while those from more wicked persons do not. Similarly, with variation of listeners: reports in the presence of a ruler who punishes liars from fewer persons yield knowledge while reports from more persons elsewhere do not. Similarly with variation of content: reports of the king's confidants about his secrets, even if they are fewer, yield knowledge while reports of more others do not. All this is necessary. And if a group report is not like that, then it is the report of one. This classification encompasses all reports, but apparently the intention is to classify the report narrated from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions, for that is the goal of the usuli's consideration, and what follows supports it. If a single man narrates it, i.e., there is only one narrator in one level of the chain, even if there are more narrators in another level, then it is gharib. If two narrate it – and this does not refer to two narrators in every level but rather there are two and no more in one level, even if there are more in another – then it is aziz. And it is not a condition for the sahih report; rather gharib is also sahih and obligatory to act upon because there is no difference in the proofs indicating authority. And it is not a condition for al-Bukhari, Imam Muhammad ibn Isma'il, author of al-Sahih, may Allah's mercy be upon him, in the correct opinion, even if some claim it is a condition for aziz.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut, a commentary on the usul al-fiqh matn Musallam al-Thubut, discusses the second source of Islamic law: the Sunnah, but focuses on the epistemological classification of reports (akhbar). The author begins by clarifying the concept of truth (sidq) and falsehood (kadhb). He argues that when actions like lying are attributed to deliberate agents, they are immediately understood as intentional; thus, negating a lie negates the intention, not the mere utterance. He supports this with consensus (ijma'): if a Jew says 'Islam is true,' we consider him truthful despite his false belief, proving that truth is not conformity to belief. The passage then classifies reports by how their truth is known: (1) necessarily by itself (mutawatir), (2) necessarily by something else (agreement with necessary knowledge like mathematical truths), (3) by reflection (reports of Allah and the Messenger for those not at the level of witnessing, and reports of ahl al-ijma' on certainties). Solitary reports with contextual indicators may yield knowledge by reflection. Reports can be presumed truthful (from a just narrator), presumed false (from a known liar), or balanced between truth and falsehood (from an unknown narrator), though the commentator notes that an unknown narrator's report is still accepted by some, so it is presumed truthful weakly. The author then refutes the Zahiri claim that whatever is not known to be true is known to be false, showing it leads to absurdities like the raising of contradictories. Finally, he presents another classification: mutawatir (group report yielding knowledge by itself) and ahad (solitary). The number for tawatur varies with circumstances of speaker, listener, and content. Within ahad, he defines gharib (single narrator at one level) and aziz (two narrators at one level), stating both can be sahih and obligatory to act upon, contrary to some who require aziz for al-Bukhari's standard. The commentator emphasizes that the main concern is reports from the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This passage demonstrates the Hanafi usuli approach to classifying reports based on epistemic certainty, using rational analysis and consensus as tools.

Key Terms
الظاهرية (al-Zahiriyya): A school of thought that relies on apparent (zahir) meanings, but here specifically a group that claimed unknown truth implies known falsehood
العادة (al-ada): Custom, which can generate certain knowledge in legal contexts
النقيضان (al-naqidan): Two contradictories (A and not-A) that cannot both be true or both false

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary logical problem with the Zahiri position according to the Hanafi author?
A) It contradicts the consensus on the Jew example.
B) It leads to the conjunction of two contradictories.
C) It ignores the role of intention in truth.
D) It relies on weak narrators.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi refutation of the Zahiri claim uses both logical contradiction and the role of custom, preserving the epistemic diversity of reports.

The Hanafi Definition of Mutawatir and Its Variable Number
Defining mutawatir and its variable number requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir according to Hanafi usul and explain why its required number varies based on the circumstances of the reporter, listener, and content.

Core Idea
Mutawatir gives knowledge by itself; its number varies with circumstances—no fixed minimum.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut explains the Hanafi definition of mutawatir, emphasizing that the number of transmitters is not fixed but depends on the conditions of the reporters, the listeners, and the content. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating the authority of transmitted reports and avoiding simplistic assumptions about tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition of mutawatir
Identify the key phrase 'خبر جماعة يفيد العلم بنفسه' (a report of a group that gives knowledge by itself). Note that the knowledge arises from the report itself, not from external clues.
The definition excludes reports that become known through external indications (qara'in).
2
Distinguish internal vs. external causes of knowledge
The passage says knowledge from tawatur is not due to separate clues but due to intrinsic circumstances of the reporter, listener, and content. Recognize that these circumstances are 'lazimah' (necessary) to the report.
This nuance prevents conflating tawatur with other forms of certainty.
3
Identify the three variable factors
List the three factors: 1) حال المخبر (condition of the reporter), 2) حال المخبر (condition of the listener), 3) المخبر عنه (the substance of the report). Understand that each affects the number needed for certainty.
The examples given (just vs. wicked, ruler vs. commoner, king's secrets) illustrate each factor.
4
Apply the factors to hypothetical cases
Take each example from the text and explain why the number varies. For instance, a few just reporters may suffice while many wicked ones do not because reliability changes the threshold.
This reinforces that tawatur is a qualitative, not quantitative, concept.
5
Formulate the Hanafi position
Conclude that according to Hanafi usul, there is no predetermined minimum number for tawatur; it is determined by the production of certain knowledge in the specific context.
This contrasts with other madhahib that set fixed numbers (e.g., 5, 40, etc.).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً) تقسيم آخر للخبر هو (متواتر إن كان خبر جماعة يفيد العلم بنفسه) أي من حيث إنه خبر هؤلاء المخبرين (لا) بالقرائن المنفصلة عن الخبر (بخلاف القرائن (اللازمة) له (من أحوال في المخبر) المتكلم (والمخبر ) السامع (والمخبر عنه) وهو مضمون الخبر فإن لهذه الأحوال دخلاً في إفادة العلم كما لا يخفى (ولذلك) أي لأجل كونه مفيداً للعلم بالنظر إلى أحوال المتكلم والسامع ومضمون الخبر يتفاوت عدد التواتر) بتفاوت الخبر، فأخبار العدول الأقلين ربما يفيد العلم دون الفسقة الأكثرين وكذا بتفاوت ،السامعين، فإن الأخبار عند ذي سلطنة يؤذي من كذب عنده من أقلين يفيد العلم دون أكثرين عند غيره، وكذا بتفاوت مضمون الخبر، فإن أخبار دخاليل الملك عن أسراره وإن كانوا أقلين يفيد العلم دون أكثرين غيرهم، وهذا كله ضروري
And also: Another division of the report is: 'Mutawatir, if the report of a group gives knowledge by itself,' i.e., by virtue of being the report of these reporters, not by external indications, unlike the necessary indications (al-qara'in al-lazimah) from the circumstances of the reporter (speaker), the addressee (listener), and the substance of the report, for these circumstances have an effect in producing knowledge, as is not hidden. And therefore, i.e., because it produces knowledge in view of the circumstances of the speaker, listener, and content, the number of tawatur varies with the variation of the report. So the reports of a few just people may give knowledge while those of many wicked people do not. Similarly, with the variation of listeners: news related to a ruler who punishes the liar from a few may give knowledge, while many others do not. Likewise, with the variation of content: the reports of close associates of the king about his secrets, even if they are few, give knowledge, while the reports of many others do not. And all this is necessary.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage defines mutawatir as a report from a group that gives knowledge by itself, not through external clues. However, the number required for tawatur is not fixed; it varies based on three factors: the condition of the reporters (such as their reliability), the condition of the hearers (such as whether they would be punished for lying), and the nature of the report itself (such as secrets of a king). This shows that the Hanafi usul perspective focuses on the certainty produced rather than a mechanical number. The passage is an expansion on the definition from the matn.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): A report from a group that gives knowledge by itself, considering the circumstances of reporters, listeners, and content.
عدد التواتر (adad al-tawatur): The number of reporters needed for tawatur; it varies and is not predetermined.
قرائن لازمة (qara'in al-lazima): Indications that are necessary and inseparable from the report, such as the circumstances of the reporter, listener, and content.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the number of tawatur vary?
A) Because the strength of the chain varies.
B) Because of differences in the conditions of the reporter, listener, and content.
C) Because the number of transmitters is irrelevant.
D) Because all reports are mutawatir if there are at least 5 reporters.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mutawatir is defined by the production of certain knowledge, and its required number varies with the circumstances of the reporter, listener, and content—no fixed count applies.

Shafi'i Classification of Ahad: Gharib, Aziz, and Mashhur
Defining gharib, aziz, and mashhur (Shafi'i classification)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between gharib, aziz, and mashhur according to the Shafi'i/muhaddith classification and explain why gharib and aziz can still be sahih and binding.

Core Idea
Gharib, aziz, and mashhur differ only in number of narrators, but all three can be sahih and must be acted upon.

The Shafi'i and hadith scholar classification of ahad reports focuses purely on the number of narrators in the chain: gharib (one), aziz (two), mashhur (three or more). This lesson unpacks those definitions, clarifies misconceptions about their strength, and notes the discussion regarding Imam Bukhari's alleged condition for authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories and their numerical criteria
Read the definitions: gharib has a single narrator in at least one link; aziz has two narrators in every link; mashhur has three or more in every link. Note that the classification is based on the minimum number of narrators in any link.
The author emphasizes that 'the lesser number overrides the greater' — a mixed chain is classified by its smallest number.
2
Understand the rule of 'the lesser number overrides the greater'
If a hadith has one narrator in one link and two in another, it is gharib (the lesser number dominates). If it has two in some links and three in others, it remains aziz.
This rule ensures consistent classification.
3
Recognize that gharib and aziz can be sahih and binding
The passage explicitly states that gharib and aziz are not necessarily weak; they can be sahih and wajib al-’amal because the evidence for authority is the same for all ahad reports.
This corrects the misconception that only mashhur or mutawatir are reliable.
4
Examine the discussion about Imam Bukhari's condition
Note that some claim Bukhari required aziz (two narrators) for his Sahih, but the author argues this is not a fixed condition; Bukhari’s practice was to require multiple verifiers, not necessarily two narrators in every link.
This shows the nuanced application of these classifications.

الأصولي ويؤيده ما بعده (فإن رواه) أي خبر الواحد رجل (واحد) فقط بأن يكون في السند واحد في مرتبة وإن كان الرواة أكثر من مرتبة أخرى فهو الغريب وإن رواه (اثنان ولا ينقض عن اثنين الرواة في كل مرتبة ولا السند (واثنان أو ثلاثة في موضع (آخر فهو غريب فالغريب ما تخلل في مرتبة من مراتب السند واحد، سواء كان قبله أو بعده اثنان فصاعداً أم لا والعزيز ماله سندان متخالفا الرواة، ولا يزيد في مرتبة ما من المراتب فالمتواتر عنده مفيد للعلم ضرورة والمشهور نظراً، واستدل بأنه إذا نقله هذه الجماعة وتلقته بالقبول صار كونه حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم مجمعاً عليه والإجماع مفيد للعلم، وجوابه أنه لا يلزم من نقل هذه الجماعة الإجماع، بل يجوز أن لا يكون فيهم مجتهداً أصلاً عن إجماعهم، ثم التخصيص بالتواتر في القرن الثاني حينئذ تحكم، فإنه لو كان رواية هذا العدد إجماعاً فيكون بالتواتر في كل قرن مجمعاً عليه، فيكون مقطوعاً، وما قيل إنه لو سلم الإجماع أيضاً فلا يلزم ثبوت الخبر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، بل غاية ما يلزم ثبوته عن ذلك الراوي والصحة مجمعاً عليه ومقطوعاً، وكذا تلقي الأمة بالقبول ليس إلاّ للصحة، لا لأنه عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قطعاً، فليس بشيء فإن تلقي الأمة ليس إلا لأنه ثبت عندهم أنه أمر الله ورسوله، فبعد تسليم أن هذا التلقي إجماع لا وجه للمنع،
The Second Principle: The Sunnah. And if it is not a report of a group as such, then it is a single report. This division includes all reports, but it is apparent that the intention is to divide the report narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family) and his Companions, for it is the focus of the usuli's view, supported by what follows. 'If it is narrated by one man' (i.e., the single report by one man only) such that there is a single narrator in one link, even if there are more narrators in other links, then it is gharib. If it is narrated by two (i.e., two narrators in each link) — and there is no condition of two narrators in every link, nor does it increase in any link, even if it increases in other links — then it is aziz. And it is not a condition for a sound hadith; the gharib can also be sound and obligatory to act upon, as the evidence for its authority is no different. And it is not [a condition] for Bukhari — Imam Muhammad ibn Isma'il, author of the Sahih, may Allah have mercy on him — in the correct opinion, even if some claim that he made it a condition for aziz upon himself in his Sahih; examining his collection shows otherwise. And what is narrated from Hakim al-Imam that Imam Bukhari committed in his Sahih to narrate from a companion who had two narrators, then each of the two narrators had two narrators, and so on up to Bukhari — likely his intention is that he did not suffice with a single verification, but required for the verification of a trustworthy person that he narrates and at least two derive benefit from him, not that he only included a companion from whom two successors narrated that hadith, then from each of them two narrated that hadith, for that would likely be contrary to reality, even if some critics relied on it. So ponder well. 'And if it is narrated by three or more' — i.e., the hadith has three chains with different narrators or more, and not less than three in any link — then it is mashhur and mustafid. It is said: up to three is aziz, and what exceeds three is mashhur. The more well-known is the first, and here the lesser number overrides the greater, i.e., it predominates. So if one narrates in one place in the chain, and two or three in another place, it is gharib. Thus gharib is where there is one narrator in a link of the chain, whether before or after there are two or more. Aziz is that which has two chains with different narrators, and does not exceed two narrators in any link; if two narrate in one link and three or four in another, it is still aziz. Mashhur is that which has three or more chains with different narrators. Know that this is the division of the Shafi'is and hadith scholars, and there is no basis for deriving these divisions and naming each except for those who give preference based on numerous narrators. But according to this, they should name every hadith whose chain increases but does not reach the level of tawatur with a specific name, as is not hidden from one with insight. And Allah knows best what is correct. And according to the generality of the Hanafis (may Allah have mercy on them), what is not mutawatir is ahad and mashhur. Thus the division is threefold according to them. The basis of the exclusivity is: if a report is narrated by a group whose collusion on lying cannot be imagined, then it is mutawatir. Otherwise, if it is narrated from a companion by a group whose collusion cannot be imagined, then it becomes mutawatir in the second and third centuries, and the ummah received it with acceptance, then it is mashhur, as he said: 'And it is that which is ahad in origin' — i.e., it is narrated from the Messenger by one or two, in short a number not reaching tawatur — 'but becomes mutawatir in the second and third centuries and thereafter, with the acceptance of the ummah.' If it is not like that, then it is khabar al-wahid. And Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi (may Allah have mercy on him) made it a part of mutawatir, followed by some like Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi and Ibn Furak as in the Hashiya, deeming it productive of theoretical knowledge. For him, mutawatir gives knowledge necessarily and mashhur gives knowledge theoretically. He argued that if this group transmitted it and the ummah received it with acceptance, it becomes a matter of consensus that it is the hadith of the Messenger, and consensus gives knowledge. The answer is that the transmission of this group does not necessarily entail consensus; it is possible that none of them are mujtahids at all regarding their consensus. Then specifying tawatur in the second century is arbitrary, because if the narration of this number were consensus, it would be consensus in every century, and thus definitive. And what is said that even if consensus is conceded, it does not necessitate the report's being proven from the Messenger; rather, at most it necessitates its being proven from that narrator and its authenticity is agreed upon and definitive. Likewise, the ummah's acceptance with approval is only for authenticity, not because it is from him definitively. But this is nothing, for the ummah's acceptance is only because it was established with them that it is the command of Allah and His Messenger. So after conceding that this acceptance is consensus, there is no ground for denial.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is divided into two main parts. First, it presents the Shafi'i/muhaddithin classification of ahad reports: gharib (one narrator at some link), aziz (two narrators at every link), and mashhur (three or more). It clarifies that gharib and aziz can be sahih and binding, and discusses Imam Bukhari's alleged condition of aziz. Second, it presents the Hanafi threefold division: mutawatir (definitive), mashhur (which starts as ahad but becomes mutawatir in later generations with ummatic acceptance, yielding theoretical knowledge), and ahad (the remainder). It also discusses al-Jassas's view that mashhur is a type of mutawatir (theoretical) and refutes it. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining that the Hanafi classification is based on the actual production of knowledge, not merely numbers.

Key Terms
غريب (gharib): A hadith with a single narrator in at least one link of the chain.
عزيز (aziz): A hadith with two narrators in every link of the chain.
مشهور (mashhur): According to Shafi'is: a hadith with three or more narrators in every link.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Shafi'i classification, what is the defining characteristic of aziz?
A) It has exactly two narrators in every link.
B) It has at least two narrators in every link.
C) It has two chains.
D) It is narrated by two companions.

Key Takeaway
In Shafi'i usul, gharib, aziz, and mashhur are categories of ahad based on narrator count; all can be sahih and legally binding.

Hanafi Threefold Division: Mutawatir, Mashhur, and Ahad
Defining mashhur and comparing Shafi'i and Hanafi classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi threefold division of khabar, define mashhur as a separate category with its epistemic status, and explain the Hanafi response to al-Jassas' view.

Core Idea
Mashhur hadith is ahad in origin but becomes equivalent to mutawatir in later centuries due to ummatic acceptance, giving it higher epistemic weight.

Unlike the Shafi'i numerical classification, the Hanafis divide reports into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. Mashhur occupies a middle ground: starting as ahad, it gains widespread transmission and acceptance, producing theoretical knowledge. This lesson unpacks its definition, conditions, and the debate with al-Jassas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi threefold division
Read that the Hanafis divide reports into mutawatir (definitive), mashhur (theoretical knowledge), and ahad (probable). The division is based on the epistemic value produced, not just numerical count.
This is a fundamental difference from the Shafi'i approach.
2
Grasp the double condition for mashhur
Mashhur must be ahad in origin (not reaching tawatur in the first generation) but later become transmitted by a group whose collusion is impossible (like mutawatir) in the second and third centuries, and the ummah must accept it.
The acceptance of the ummah (talaqqi bi’l-qabul) is crucial.
3
Distinguish mashhur from mutawatir
Mutawatir gives necessary knowledge (ilm daruri) while mashhur gives theoretical knowledge (ilm nazari). Both are certain but differ in the mode of knowledge acquisition.
The Hanafi mashhur is epistemologically stronger than any ahad report.
4
Examine al-Jassas’ view and the Hanafi response
Al-Jassas considered mashhur as a type of mutawatir (producing theoretical knowledge). The Hanafis respond that the transmission of the group does not necessarily entail consensus; the acceptance is for authenticity, not for certainty of wording. Also, specifying tawatur in the second century is arbitrary.
This refines the understanding of mashhur's epistemic status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الأصولي ويؤيده ما بعده (فإن رواه) أي خبر الواحد رجل (واحد) فقط بأن يكون في السند واحد في مرتبة وإن كان الرواة أكثر من مرتبة أخرى فهو الغريب وإن رواه (اثنان ولا ينقض عن اثنين الرواة في كل مرتبة ولا يزيد عليه في مرتبة ما وإن زاد في أخرى فهو العزيز وليس شرطاً للصحيح من الخبر فالغريب أيضاً يكون صحيحاً و واجب العمل لعدم فرق الأدلة الدالة على الحجية (ولا) (للبخاري) الإمام محمد بن إسماعيل صاحب الصحيح رحمة الله عليه (في) المذهب (الصحيح) وإن زعم البعض أنه شرط العزة على نفسه في صحيحه» فإن تتبعه يحكم بخلافه، وما روى عن الحاكم الإمام رحمه الله تعالى أن الإمام البخاري التزم في صحيحه أن يروي عن صحابي له راويان، ثم لكل واحد من الراويين ،راويان وهكذا إلى الإمام البخاري فلعل مراده أنه لم يكتف بتوثيق واحد، بل يشرط في توثيق ثقة أن يروي ويستفيد منه اثنان فصاعداً، لا أنه إنما أخرج صحابي روى عنه التابعيان ذلك الحديث، ثم عن كل واحد منهما اثنان بذلك الحديث، فإن ذلك لعله يكون خلاف الواقع وإن اعتمد عليه بعض النقاد فتدبر أحسن التدبر ( وإن رواه ثلاثة أو أكثر) بأن يكون للحديث ثلاثة أسانيد برواة مختلفة فصاعداً، ولا ينقص في كل مرتبة عن ثلاثة (فالمشهور والمستفيض، وقيل إلى الثلاثة عزيز وما زاد على الثلاثة (فمشهور) والأشهر الأول والأقل ههنا يقضي على الأكثر) أي يغلبه فإذا) روى واحد في موضع (ما من مواضع السند (واثنان أو ثلاثة في موضع (آخر فهو غريب فالغريب ما تخلل في مرتبة من مراتب السند واحد، سواء كان قبله أو بعده اثنان فصاعداً أم لا والعزيز ماله سندان متخالفا الرواة، ولا يزيد في مرتبة ما من المراتب على راويين اثنين فإن روى اثنان في موضع وثلاثة وأربعة في آخر فهو عزيز لا غير، والمشهور ماله ثلاثة أسانيد أو أزيد متخالفة الرواة. اعلم أن هذا تقسيم الشافعية وأهل الحديث، ولا يظهر لتخريج هذه الأقسام وتسمية كل بسم وجه إلا عند من يرجح بكثرة الرواة، لكن ينبغي على هذا أن يسموا كل ما زاد سنده ولم يبلغ حد التواتر باسم خاص، كما لا يخفى على صاحب الدراية والله أعلم بالصواب وعند عامة (الحنفية رحمهم الله تعالى (ما ليس بمتواتر احاد ومشهور) فالقسمة مثلثة عندهم وجه الحصر إن الخبر إن رواه جماعة لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب ثم وثم فمتواتر وإلا فإن روى عن صحابي جماعة لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب ثم وثم وتلقته الأمة بالقبول فمشهور كما قال (وهو ما كان آحاد (الأصل بأن يروى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم واحد واثنان وبالجملة عدد غير بالغ حد التواتر (متواتراً في القرن الثاني والثالث) ومن بعدهم (مع قبول (الأمة وإن لم يكن كذلك فهو خبر الواحد (وجعله) الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر (الجصاص) الرازي رحمه الله (قسماً من المتواتر) وتبعه بعضهم كأبي منصور البغدادي وابن فروك على ما في «الحاشية» (مفيداً للعلم نظراً) فالمتواتر عنده مفيد للعلم ضرورة والمشهور نظراً، واستدل بأنه إذا نقله هذه الجماعة وتلقته بالقبول صار كونه حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم مجمعاً عليه والإجماع مفيد للعلم، وجوابه أنه لا يلزم من نقل هذه الجماعة الإجماع، بل يجوز أن لا يكون فيهم مجتهداً أصلاً عن إجماعهم، ثم التخصيص بالتواتر في القرن الثاني حينئذ تحكم، فإنه لو كان رواية هذا العدد إجماعاً فيكون بالتواتر في كل قرن مجمعاً عليه، فيكون مقطوعاً، وما قيل إنه لو سلم الإجماع أيضاً فلا يلزم ثبوت الخبر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، بل غاية ما يلزم ثبوته عن ذلك الراوي والصحة مجمعاً عليه ومقطوعاً، وكذا تلقي الأمة بالقبول ليس إلاّ للصحة، لا لأنه عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قطعاً، فليس بشيء فإن تلقي الأمة ليس إلا لأنه ثبت عندهم أنه أمر الله ورسوله، فبعد تسليم أن هذا التلقي إجماع لا وجه للمنع،
The Second Principle: The Sunnah. And if it is not a report of a group as such, then it is a single report. This division includes all reports, but it is apparent that the intention is to divide the report narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family) and his Companions, for it is the focus of the usuli's view, supported by what follows. 'If it is narrated by one man' (i.e., the single report by one man only) such that there is a single narrator in one link, even if there are more narrators in other links, then it is gharib. If it is narrated by two (i.e., two narrators in each link) — and there is no condition of two narrators in every link, nor does it increase in any link, even if it increases in other links — then it is aziz. And it is not a condition for a sound hadith; the gharib can also be sound and obligatory to act upon, as the evidence for its authority is no different. And it is not [a condition] for Bukhari — Imam Muhammad ibn Isma'il, author of the Sahih, may Allah have mercy on him — in the correct opinion, even if some claim that he made it a condition for aziz upon himself in his Sahih; examining his collection shows otherwise. And what is narrated from Hakim al-Imam that Imam Bukhari committed in his Sahih to narrate from a companion who had two narrators, then each of the two narrators had two narrators, and so on up to Bukhari — likely his intention is that he did not suffice with a single verification, but required for the verification of a trustworthy person that he narrates and at least two derive benefit from him, not that he only included a companion from whom two successors narrated that hadith, then from each of them two narrated that hadith, for that would likely be contrary to reality, even if some critics relied on it. So ponder well. 'And if it is narrated by three or more' — i.e., the hadith has three chains with different narrators or more, and not less than three in any link — then it is mashhur and mustafid. It is said: up to three is aziz, and what exceeds three is mashhur. The more well-known is the first, and here the lesser number overrides the greater, i.e., it predominates. So if one narrates in one place in the chain, and two or three in another place, it is gharib. Thus gharib is where there is one narrator in a link of the chain, whether before or after there are two or more. Aziz is that which has two chains with different narrators, and does not exceed two narrators in any link; if two narrate in one link and three or four in another, it is still aziz. Mashhur is that which has three or more chains with different narrators. Know that this is the division of the Shafi'is and hadith scholars, and there is no basis for deriving these divisions and naming each except for those who give preference based on numerous narrators. But according to this, they should name every hadith whose chain increases but does not reach the level of tawatur with a specific name, as is not hidden from one with insight. And Allah knows best what is correct. And according to the generality of the Hanafis (may Allah have mercy on them), what is not mutawatir is ahad and mashhur. Thus the division is threefold according to them. The basis of the exclusivity is: if a report is narrated by a group whose collusion on lying cannot be imagined, then it is mutawatir. Otherwise, if it is narrated from a companion by a group whose collusion cannot be imagined, then it becomes mutawatir in the second and third centuries, and the ummah received it with acceptance, then it is mashhur, as he said: 'And it is that which is ahad in origin' — i.e., it is narrated from the Messenger by one or two, in short a number not reaching tawatur — 'but becomes mutawatir in the second and third centuries and thereafter, with the acceptance of the ummah.' If it is not like that, then it is khabar al-wahid. And Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi (may Allah have mercy on him) made it a part of mutawatir, followed by some like Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi and Ibn Furak as in the Hashiya, deeming it productive of theoretical knowledge. For him, mutawatir gives knowledge necessarily and mashhur gives knowledge theoretically. He argued that if this group transmitted it and the ummah received it with acceptance, it becomes a matter of consensus that it is the hadith of the Messenger, and consensus gives knowledge. The answer is that the transmission of this group does not necessarily entail consensus; it is possible that none of them are mujtahids at all regarding their consensus. Then specifying tawatur in the second century is arbitrary, because if the narration of this number were consensus, it would be consensus in every century, and thus definitive. And what is said that even if consensus is conceded, it does not necessitate the report's being proven from the Messenger; rather, at most it necessitates its being proven from that narrator and its authenticity is agreed upon and definitive. Likewise, the ummah's acceptance with approval is only for authenticity, not because it is from him definitively. But this is nothing, for the ummah's acceptance is only because it was established with them that it is the command of Allah and His Messenger. So after conceding that this acceptance is consensus, there is no ground for denial.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is divided into two main parts. First, it presents the Shafi'i/muhaddithin classification of ahad reports: gharib (one narrator at some link), aziz (two narrators at every link), and mashhur (three or more). It clarifies that gharib and aziz can be sahih and binding, and discusses Imam Bukhari's alleged condition of aziz. Second, it presents the Hanafi threefold division: mutawatir (definitive), mashhur (which starts as ahad but becomes mutawatir in later generations with ummatic acceptance, yielding theoretical knowledge), and ahad (the remainder). It also discusses al-Jassas's view that mashhur is a type of mutawatir (theoretical) and refutes it. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining that the Hanafi classification is based on the actual production of knowledge, not merely numbers.

Key Terms
مشهور (mashhur): Hanafi: a hadith that is ahad in origin but becomes mutawatir in later centuries with ummatic acceptance, yielding theoretical knowledge.
علم نظري (ilm nazari): Theoretical knowledge obtained through reflection and proof, as opposed to necessary knowledge (ilm daruri) which is immediate.
تواتر (tawatur): A transmission by a group whose collusion on lying is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the key distinction between mutawatir and mashhur?
A) Mutawatir yields theoretical knowledge while mashhur yields necessary knowledge.
B) Mutawatir is narrated by a group in every generation from the first, while mashhur becomes widespread only in later generations.
C) Mashhur is a type of ahad, while mutawatir is not.
D) Both give the same level of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Mashhur hadith in Hanafi usul bridges ahad and mutawatir, providing theoretical knowledge that commands higher authority in fiqh.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Trichotomy of Reports: Mutawatir, Mashhur, and Ahad
Classifying khabar into gharib, aziz, mashhur, and Hanafi division into mutawatir, mashhur, ahad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and define the three Hanafi categories of reports (mutawatir, mashhur, ahad) and distinguish them from the Shafi'i/muhaddithin classification (gharib, 'aziz, mashhur).

Core Idea
Hanafis divide reports into mutawatir (certain), mashhur (strongly conjectural), and ahad (conjectural).

This lesson introduces the classification of prophetic reports (khabar) as a source of Islamic law. You will learn the Hanafi tripartite division and how it differs from the classification used by hadith scholars and Shafi'is, setting the stage for understanding the evidentiary weight of each type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two classification systems
Read the passage and note that the first part presents the Shafi'i/muhaddithin classification into gharib, 'aziz, and mashhur based on narrator count. The second part presents the Hanafi classification into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad based on epistemological certainty and transmission pattern.
The Hanafi system is simpler but carries different implications for legal derivation.
2
Define each category in both systems
For Shafi'is: gharib = single narrator at some level; 'aziz = exactly two narrators at some level; mashhur = three or more. For Hanafis: mutawatir = group precluding collusion in every generation; mashhur = originally ahad but became widespread and accepted; ahad = does not meet tawatur or mashhur conditions.
Note that mashhur in Hanafi differs from mashhur in Shafi'i; the former has epistemological weight due to Ummah acceptance.
3
Understand the criterion for each system
The muhaddithin focus on narrator numbers at each level. Hanafis focus on the certainty of transmission: mutawatir is certain (qat'i), mashhur yields strong conjecture (zann qawi), ahad yields mere conjecture (zann).
The Hanafi classification is more about the authority of the report in legal reasoning.
4
Recognize the unique Hanafi category of mashhur
Unlike the Shafi'i classification where mashhur is merely a quantitative distinction, Hanafi mashhur is a distinct category with its own evidentiary value: it can restrict the absolute of the Quran.
This will be explored in detail in the next lesson.

وهي تفيد ظن المطابقة للواقع، لأن احتمال السهو والنسيان قائم بل احتمال الكذب وإن كان مرجوحاً فإن العدالة غير مقطوعة، وإذا لم يفد هذا الخبر إلا ظناً مثل ظن خبر الواحد فكيف يجوز تغيير المطلق المقطوع الثبوت، وأيد بأن هذا لا يزيد على السماع من الصحابي نفسه، وهو لا يزاد به على الكتاب، وتحقيق المقام أن عدالة الصحابة مقطوعة، لا سيما أصحاب بدر وبيعة الرضوان كيف لا وقد أثنى عليهم الله تعالى في مواضع غير عديدة من كتابه وبين رسوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فضائلهم غير مرة والإخبار فيها وإن كانت مروية أحاداً لكن القدر المشترك متواتر، وإذا كان كذلك فلا احتمال للكذب عمداً أصلاً، ثم إن بركة صحبة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم واختيار الله تعالى إياهم لتلك الصحبة وبذل جهدهم في حفظ الدين يبعد النسيان بأن لا يحفظوا وينسبوا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ما لم يسمعوا كل البعد ثم إن تلقي الأمة بالقبول يوجب عدم الاعتداد باحتمال النسيان، فإن التلقي بالقبول إنما هو لكونه قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، وبعد هذا فاحتمال النسيان ليس إلا كاحتمال المجاز في الخاص من غير قرينة، فإذن رواية الصحابي المقطوع العدالة الجليل مع تلقي الأمة إياها موجبة لليقين بالمعنى الأعم مثل اليقين في دلالة الخاص فإذا تواترت منه في القرن الثاني والثالث أورث القطع بأنها مروية عن الصحابي الذي هذا شأنه، وروايته مقطوعة بالمعنى الأعم، فالخبر المشهور مقطوع بالمعنى
The second principle: The Sunnah. 135 ... on himself in his Sahih. For studying it rules contrary to it. And what was narrated from al-Hakim al-Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, that Imam al-Bukhari committed in his Sahih to narrate from a Companion who had two narrators, then each of the two narrators had two narrators, and so on up to al-Bukhari. Perhaps his intent was that he was not content with a single verification, but he required for the verification of a trustworthy narrator that two or more narrate and benefit from him, not that he only included a Companion from whom two Followers narrated that hadith, then from each of them two narrated that same hadith. For that would probably contradict reality, even if some critics relied on it. So ponder well. (And if three or more narrate it) meaning the hadith has three chains with different narrators or more, and in each level there are no less than three, then it is mashhur and mustafid. It is said: up to three is 'aziz, and what exceeds three is mashhur. The first (i.e., the opinion that up to three is 'aziz) is most famous, and the lesser here overrides the greater, i.e., it prevails. So if one narrates in some position of the chain, and two or three in another position, then it is gharib. So gharib is what has a single narrator in one level of the chain, whether before or after there are two or more or not. 'Aziz is what has two chains with different narrators, and in no level does it exceed two narrators. If two narrate in one position and three or four in another, it is 'aziz only. Mashhur is what has three chains or more with different narrators. Know that this is the classification of the Shafi'is and the hadith scholars, and the derivation of these divisions and naming each with a specific name is only evident to one who gives weight to the multiplicity of narrators. But based on this, they should name every chain that increases but does not reach the level of tawatur with a specific name, as is not hidden from one possessing insight. And Allah knows best what is correct. And according to the generality of the Hanafis, may Allah have mercy on them, what is not mutawatir is ahad and mashhur. So the division is tripartite according to them. The reason for the limitation is that if a report is narrated by a group about whom it is inconceivable that they colluded in lying, generation after generation, then it is mutawatir. Otherwise, if it is narrated from a Companion by a group about whom it is inconceivable that they colluded in lying, generation after generation, and the Ummah has received it with acceptance, then it is mashhur, as he said: and it is originally ahad, meaning it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, by one or two, in short a number not reaching the level of tawatur, (but) it became mutawatir in the second and third centuries and after, with the acceptance of the Ummah. If it is not like that, then it is khabar al-wahid. And the Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, may Allah have mercy on him, made it a category of mutawatir, and some followed him like Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi and Ibn Furrak according to what is in the Hashiya, (considering it) useful for knowledge (by reflection). So according to him, mutawatir is useful for knowledge necessarily, and mashhur by reflection. He argued that when this group narrated it and the Ummah received it with acceptance, it becomes that the fact that it is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is a matter of consensus, and consensus is useful for knowledge. The answer to this is that the narration of this group does not necessitate consensus; rather it is possible that among them there is not a single mujtahid at all for their consensus. Then specifying tawatur in the second century is arbitrary, for if the narration of this number were consensus, then it would be mutawatir in every century and agreed upon, so it would be definitive. And what is said that even if consensus is granted, it does not necessitate establishing the report from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; rather at most it necessitates its establishment from that narrator, and the soundness is agreed upon and definitive. Similarly, the Ummah's reception with acceptance is only for its soundness, not because it is definitively from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. This is nothing, for the Ummah's reception is only because it is established with them that it is the command of Allah and His Messenger. So after conceding that this reception is consensus, there is no ground for denial, let alone... 136 ... for consensus is definitive in establishing what it is agreed upon, even if the people of consensus were conjecturing. So reflect. And it may be argued on his behalf that the narration of this great multitude of eminent scholars, while they are of great expertise in sciences and knowledge, yields certainty that it is his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. The answer is that the narration of this great multitude of eminent scholars only indicates that the one narrated from is trustworthy and that his narration is obligatory to act upon, not that their narrated material is definitively the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. How so? For the eminent scholars received Sahih al-Bukhari with acceptance while not being certain that its narrations are definitively his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Rather, at most there is strong conjecture with acceptance. So understand. And the agreement of all that one who denies it is not considered an unbeliever. As for other than Shaykh Abu Bakr, it is obvious. As for him, because his certainty is theoretical, it has entered into the realm of doubt. And what is said that there remains no fruit of the disagreement on this view is answered: the fruit is that according to him, since it is definitive, it can oppose the Book and abrogate it in various ways of abrogation, contrary to the majority, as will soon appear. Rather, its denier is deemed misguided and judged mistaken. And the mashhur report necessitates strong conjecture, like certainty that has no room for doubt or probability arising from a proof at all. This conjecture is called 'ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah (knowledge of tranquility), and it is sometimes expressed as certainty. It is said: the specific is useful for certainty, which is knowledge that does not admit of contrary probability arising from a proof; rather if there is a probability, it is not considered. This is stated by Sadr al-Shari'ah. So it restricts the absolute of the Book, because it is definitive like the definiteness of the absolute. And here there is a research that has been considered difficult: that the utmost that results from fame is the strength of its transmission from the narrator, not the strength of its transmission from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, since it is originally ahad and yields conjecture. The acceptance of the great multitude is only due to the trustworthiness of the narrator, which yields conjecture of correspondence to reality, because the probability of forgetfulness and inadvertence exists, and even the probability of lying, though outweighed, since trustworthiness is not definitive. And when this report yields only conjecture like the conjecture of khabar al-wahid, how is it permissible to change the absolute which is definitive in transmission? It is supported that this does not exceed hearing from the Companion himself, and that does not take precedence over the Book. The resolution of the matter is that the trustworthiness of the Companions is definitive, especially the people of Badr and the Pledge of Ridwan. How could it not be, since Allah Almighty has praised them in numerous places in His Book, and His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, has mentioned their virtues many times. The reports about that, though transmitted as ahad, are common to all in a mutawatir manner. When this is the case, there is no probability of intentional lying at all. Then, the blessing of companionship with the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and Allah's choice of them for that companionship, and their exertion of effort in preserving the religion, makes forgetfulness extremely unlikely, such that they would not preserve and attribute to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, what they did not hear. Then, the Ummah's reception with acceptance necessitates not considering the probability of forgetfulness, for the reception with acceptance is because it is the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. After this, the probability of forgetfulness is only like the probability of metaphorical meaning in the specific without a contextual clue. So the narration of the noble Companion whose trustworthiness is definitive, combined with the Ummah's reception of it, necessitates certainty in the broader sense, like certainty in the implication of the specific. When it becomes widespread (tawatur) from him in the second and third centuries, it engenders the certainty that it is narrated from the Companion who is of this status, and his narration is definitive in the broader sense. So the mashhur report is definitive in the broader sense.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of khabar (reports) in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the epistemological value of different types. The author first explains the classification according to the Shafi'is and hadith scholars, who divide non-mutawatir reports into gharib, 'aziz, and mashhur based on the number of narrators at each level. Gharib has a single narrator at some level, 'aziz has two, and mashhur has three or more. The author notes that this classification is based on preferring multiplicity of narrators. He then presents the Hanafi classification, which is tripartite: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. According to the Hanafis, mutawatir is reported by a group about whom collusion is inconceivable in every generation. If a report is originally ahad (i.e., not meeting tawatur conditions in the first generation) but later becomes widely transmitted and accepted by the Ummah in the second and third generations, it is called mashhur. If it remains with few narrators throughout, it is khabar al-wahid. The text then discusses a disagreement: Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas considered mashhur to be a category of mutawatir, yielding knowledge by reflection (nazaran), not necessarily. The author provides a rebuttal, arguing that acceptance by the Ummah does not automatically imply consensus, and even if it did, it would not prove the report is definitively from the Prophet. The passage continues to defend the Hanafi position that mashhur yields strong conjecture (zann qawi) akin to certainty, which can restrict the absolute (mutlaq) of the Quran. A potential objection is raised: since mashhur is originally ahad, it only gives conjecture about the narrator's trustworthiness, not certainty about the Prophet's words. The author resolves this by affirming the definitive trustworthiness of the Companions, especially the prominent ones, and the fact that widespread acceptance eliminates the probability of forgetfulness. Thus, mashhur, when combined with these factors, yields a broad certainty that can qualify the Quran. The text also notes the practical consequence: according to al-Jassas, mashhur can abrogate the Quran, unlike the majority view.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawātir): A report narrated by a group about whom it is inconceivable they colluded in lying, generation after generation.
المشهور (al-mashhūr): A report originally ahad (not mutawatir in first generation) but narrated by many in later generations and accepted by the Ummah.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A report that does not reach the level of tawatur or mashhur; its narrators are few.
الغريب (al-gharīb): A report with a single narrator at some level of the chain.
العزيز (al-'azīz): A report with exactly two narrators at some level, never more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, what is the defining characteristic of a mashhur report?
A) It has three or more chains at some level.
B) It is originally ahad but becomes widely narrated and accepted by the Ummah.
C) It has a single narrator at some level.
D) It is narrated by a group precluding collusion in every generation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tripartite classification (mutawatir, mashhur, ahad) is based on epistemological certainty and directly informs the legal authority of a report.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
15 min
The Epistemological Weight of Mashhur Reports and Their Ability to Restrict the Quran
Debate on the epistemological status of mashhur reports and their ability to restrict the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate al-Jassas's argument that mashhur reports are mutawatir and explain the Hanafi response that mashhur yields strong conjecture capable of restricting the Quran.

Core Idea
Mashhur reports, though originally ahad, gain near-certainty due to Companion trustworthiness and Ummah acceptance, enabling them to restrict the Quran.

This lesson examines a major debate in Hanafi usul: the epistemological value of mashhur reports. You will study al-Jassas's view that mashhur is a type of mutawatir, the Hanafi rebuttal, and the conclusion that mashhur yields 'ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah (strong conjecture) which allows it to qualify the absolute of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
State al-Jassas's position and argument
Al-Jassas considered mashhur a category of mutawatir, yielding knowledge by reflection (nazaran). His argument: widespread transmission and Ummah acceptance implies consensus (ijma), which is definitive.
This is an extreme view that elevates mashhur to the level of certainty.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to al-Jassas
The Hanafis rebut by pointing out that the narration group may not include mujtahids, so consensus is not certain. Also, Ummah acceptance is for soundness, not for certainty of origin from the Prophet.
The response uses the principles of usul to limit the implications of Ummah acceptance.
3
Identify the Hanafi position on mashhur
Mashhur yields strong conjecture (zann qawi) akin to certainty ('ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah), based on the definitive trustworthiness of Companions and the unlikelihood of forgetfulness. This permits it to restrict (yuqayyid) the absolute of the Quran.
This is a nuanced position that gives mashhur authority without equating it to mutawatir.
4
Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Al-Jassas allowed mashhur to abrogate the Quran. The majority Hanafis do not allow abrogation but allow restriction of the absolute. This affects how mashhur reports are used in legal derivation.
For example, the hadith 'La sadaqata illa 'an zahri ghina' restricts the absolute command of zakat.
5
Examine the resolution regarding Companion trustworthiness
The text resolves the objection that mashhur only gives certainty about the narrator, not the Prophet. It affirms that Companions' trustworthiness is definitive (qat'i), especially the prominent ones, and their widespread transmission eliminates the probability of forgetfulness.
Thus, the combination yields a broad certainty that can qualify the Quran.

وههنا بحث قد عدّ عويصاً بأن غاية ما لزم من الشهرة قوة ثبوته عن الراوي لا قوة ثبوته عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فإنه آحاد الأصل وهو يفيد الظن، وقبول الجم الغفير إنما هو بعدالة الراوي، وهي تفيد ظن المطابقة للواقع، لأن احتمال السهو والنسيان قائم بل احتمال الكذب وإن كان مرجوحاً فإن العدالة غير مقطوعة، وإذا لم يفد هذا الخبر إلا ظناً مثل ظن خبر الواحد فكيف يجوز تغيير المطلق المقطوع الثبوت، وأيد بأن هذا لا يزيد على السماع من الصحابي نفسه، وهو لا يزاد به على الكتاب، وتحقيق المقام أن عدالة الصحابة مقطوعة، لا سيما أصحاب بدر وبيعة الرضوان كيف لا وقد أثنى عليهم الله تعالى في مواضع غير عديدة من كتابه وبين رسوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فضائلهم غير مرة والإخبار فيها وإن كانت مروية أحاداً لكن القدر المشترك متواتر، وإذا كان كذلك فلا احتمال للكذب عمداً أصلاً، ثم إن بركة صحبة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم واختيار الله تعالى إياهم لتلك الصحبة وبذل جهدهم في حفظ الدين يبعد النسيان بأن لا يحفظوا وينسبوا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ما لم يسمعوا كل البعد ثم إن تلقي الأمة بالقبول يوجب عدم الاعتداد باحتمال النسيان، فإن التلقي بالقبول إنما هو لكونه قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، وبعد هذا فاحتمال النسيان ليس إلا كاحتمال المجاز في الخاص من غير قرينة، فإذن رواية الصحابي المقطوع العدالة الجليل مع تلقي الأمة إياها موجبة لليقين بالمعنى الأعم مثل اليقين في دلالة الخاص فإذا تواترت منه في القرن الثاني والثالث أورث القطع بأنها مروية عن الصحابي الذي هذا شأنه، وروايته مقطوعة بالمعنى الأعم، فالخبر المشهور مقطوع بالمعنى
The second principle: The Sunnah. 135 ... on himself in his Sahih. For studying it rules contrary to it. And what was narrated from al-Hakim al-Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, that Imam al-Bukhari committed in his Sahih to narrate from a Companion who had two narrators, then each of the two narrators had two narrators, and so on up to al-Bukhari. Perhaps his intent was that he was not content with a single verification, but he required for the verification of a trustworthy narrator that two or more narrate and benefit from him, not that he only included a Companion from whom two Followers narrated that hadith, then from each of them two narrated that same hadith. For that would probably contradict reality, even if some critics relied on it. So ponder well. (And if three or more narrate it) meaning the hadith has three chains with different narrators or more, and in each level there are no less than three, then it is mashhur and mustafid. It is said: up to three is 'aziz, and what exceeds three is mashhur. The first (i.e., the opinion that up to three is 'aziz) is most famous, and the lesser here overrides the greater, i.e., it prevails. So if one narrates in some position of the chain, and two or three in another position, then it is gharib. So gharib is what has a single narrator in one level of the chain, whether before or after there are two or more or not. 'Aziz is what has two chains with different narrators, and in no level does it exceed two narrators. If two narrate in one position and three or four in another, it is 'aziz only. Mashhur is what has three chains or more with different narrators. Know that this is the classification of the Shafi'is and the hadith scholars, and the derivation of these divisions and naming each with a specific name is only evident to one who gives weight to the multiplicity of narrators. But based on this, they should name every chain that increases but does not reach the level of tawatur with a specific name, as is not hidden from one possessing insight. And Allah knows best what is correct. And according to the generality of the Hanafis, may Allah have mercy on them, what is not mutawatir is ahad and mashhur. So the division is tripartite according to them. The reason for the limitation is that if a report is narrated by a group about whom it is inconceivable that they colluded in lying, generation after generation, then it is mutawatir. Otherwise, if it is narrated from a Companion by a group about whom it is inconceivable that they colluded in lying, generation after generation, and the Ummah has received it with acceptance, then it is mashhur, as he said: and it is originally ahad, meaning it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, by one or two, in short a number not reaching the level of tawatur, (but) it became mutawatir in the second and third centuries and after, with the acceptance of the Ummah. If it is not like that, then it is khabar al-wahid. And the Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, may Allah have mercy on him, made it a category of mutawatir, and some followed him like Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi and Ibn Furrak according to what is in the Hashiya, (considering it) useful for knowledge (by reflection). So according to him, mutawatir is useful for knowledge necessarily, and mashhur by reflection. He argued that when this group narrated it and the Ummah received it with acceptance, it becomes that the fact that it is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is a matter of consensus, and consensus is useful for knowledge. The answer to this is that the narration of this group does not necessitate consensus; rather it is possible that among them there is not a single mujtahid at all for their consensus. Then specifying tawatur in the second century is arbitrary, for if the narration of this number were consensus, then it would be mutawatir in every century and agreed upon, so it would be definitive. And what is said that even if consensus is granted, it does not necessitate establishing the report from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; rather at most it necessitates its establishment from that narrator, and the soundness is agreed upon and definitive. Similarly, the Ummah's reception with acceptance is only for its soundness, not because it is definitively from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. This is nothing, for the Ummah's reception is only because it is established with them that it is the command of Allah and His Messenger. So after conceding that this reception is consensus, there is no ground for denial, let alone... 136 ... for consensus is definitive in establishing what it is agreed upon, even if the people of consensus were conjecturing. So reflect. And it may be argued on his behalf that the narration of this great multitude of eminent scholars, while they are of great expertise in sciences and knowledge, yields certainty that it is his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. The answer is that the narration of this great multitude of eminent scholars only indicates that the one narrated from is trustworthy and that his narration is obligatory to act upon, not that their narrated material is definitively the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. How so? For the eminent scholars received Sahih al-Bukhari with acceptance while not being certain that its narrations are definitively his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Rather, at most there is strong conjecture with acceptance. So understand. And the agreement of all that one who denies it is not considered an unbeliever. As for other than Shaykh Abu Bakr, it is obvious. As for him, because his certainty is theoretical, it has entered into the realm of doubt. And what is said that there remains no fruit of the disagreement on this view is answered: the fruit is that according to him, since it is definitive, it can oppose the Book and abrogate it in various ways of abrogation, contrary to the majority, as will soon appear. Rather, its denier is deemed misguided and judged mistaken. And the mashhur report necessitates strong conjecture, like certainty that has no room for doubt or probability arising from a proof at all. This conjecture is called 'ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah (knowledge of tranquility), and it is sometimes expressed as certainty. It is said: the specific is useful for certainty, which is knowledge that does not admit of contrary probability arising from a proof; rather if there is a probability, it is not considered. This is stated by Sadr al-Shari'ah. So it restricts the absolute of the Book, because it is definitive like the definiteness of the absolute. And here there is a research that has been considered difficult: that the utmost that results from fame is the strength of its transmission from the narrator, not the strength of its transmission from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, since it is originally ahad and yields conjecture. The acceptance of the great multitude is only due to the trustworthiness of the narrator, which yields conjecture of correspondence to reality, because the probability of forgetfulness and inadvertence exists, and even the probability of lying, though outweighed, since trustworthiness is not definitive. And when this report yields only conjecture like the conjecture of khabar al-wahid, how is it permissible to change the absolute which is definitive in transmission? It is supported that this does not exceed hearing from the Companion himself, and that does not take precedence over the Book. The resolution of the matter is that the trustworthiness of the Companions is definitive, especially the people of Badr and the Pledge of Ridwan. How could it not be, since Allah Almighty has praised them in numerous places in His Book, and His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, has mentioned their virtues many times. The reports about that, though transmitted as ahad, are common to all in a mutawatir manner. When this is the case, there is no probability of intentional lying at all. Then, the blessing of companionship with the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and Allah's choice of them for that companionship, and their exertion of effort in preserving the religion, makes forgetfulness extremely unlikely, such that they would not preserve and attribute to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, what they did not hear. Then, the Ummah's reception with acceptance necessitates not considering the probability of forgetfulness, for the reception with acceptance is because it is the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. After this, the probability of forgetfulness is only like the probability of metaphorical meaning in the specific without a contextual clue. So the narration of the noble Companion whose trustworthiness is definitive, combined with the Ummah's reception of it, necessitates certainty in the broader sense, like certainty in the implication of the specific. When it becomes widespread (tawatur) from him in the second and third centuries, it engenders the certainty that it is narrated from the Companion who is of this status, and his narration is definitive in the broader sense. So the mashhur report is definitive in the broader sense.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of khabar (reports) in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the epistemological value of different types. The author first explains the classification according to the Shafi'is and hadith scholars, who divide non-mutawatir reports into gharib, 'aziz, and mashhur based on the number of narrators at each level. Gharib has a single narrator at some level, 'aziz has two, and mashhur has three or more. The author notes that this classification is based on preferring multiplicity of narrators. He then presents the Hanafi classification, which is tripartite: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. According to the Hanafis, mutawatir is reported by a group about whom collusion is inconceivable in every generation. If a report is originally ahad (i.e., not meeting tawatur conditions in the first generation) but later becomes widely transmitted and accepted by the Ummah in the second and third generations, it is called mashhur. If it remains with few narrators throughout, it is khabar al-wahid. The text then discusses a disagreement: Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas considered mashhur to be a category of mutawatir, yielding knowledge by reflection (nazaran), not necessarily. The author provides a rebuttal, arguing that acceptance by the Ummah does not automatically imply consensus, and even if it did, it would not prove the report is definitively from the Prophet. The passage continues to defend the Hanafi position that mashhur yields strong conjecture (zann qawi) akin to certainty, which can restrict the absolute (mutlaq) of the Quran. A potential objection is raised: since mashhur is originally ahad, it only gives conjecture about the narrator's trustworthiness, not certainty about the Prophet's words. The author resolves this by affirming the definitive trustworthiness of the Companions, especially the prominent ones, and the fact that widespread acceptance eliminates the probability of forgetfulness. Thus, mashhur, when combined with these factors, yields a broad certainty that can qualify the Quran. The text also notes the practical consequence: according to al-Jassas, mashhur can abrogate the Quran, unlike the majority view.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawātir): A report narrated by a group about whom it is inconceivable they colluded in lying, generation after generation.
المشهور (al-mashhūr): A report originally ahad (not mutawatir in first generation) but narrated by many in later generations and accepted by the Ummah.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A report that does not reach the level of tawatur or mashhur; its narrators are few.
علم الطمأنينة ('ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah): Knowledge of tranquility; strong conjecture that is akin to certainty, with no room for valid doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement between al-Jassas and the majority Hanafis regarding mashhur reports?
A) Al-Jassas allows mashhur to restrict the Quran; the majority does not.
B) Al-Jassas allows mashhur to abrogate the Quran; the majority allows only restriction.
C) Al-Jassas considers mashhur as ahad; the majority considers it mutawatir.
D) There is no practical difference.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on mashhur is that it yields strong conjecture ('ilm al-ṭuma'nīnah) due to definitive Companion trustworthiness and Ummah acceptance, allowing it to restrict the Quran but not abrogate it.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
15 min
Authority of Khabar Mashhur and Its Restriction of the Qur'an
Defending mashhur's ability to restrict the Qur'an's mutlaq against objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi argument for the authority of khabar mashhur to evaluate whether it can restrict the muṭlaq of the Qur'an and identify the limits of its authority over the Book.

Core Idea
Mashhur is a barzakh: it can restrict the muṭlaq but cannot abrogate the entire Qur'an.

This passage tackles a key usul dispute: can a well-known hadith (khabar mashhur) restrict an absolute (muṭlaq) verse of the Qur'an? The objection is fundamental—mashhur is originally ahad, yielding only probability, while the Qur'an is definitive in transmission. The author defends the Hanafi position by arguing that mashhur, through the definitive uprightness of the Companions and the Ummah's acceptance, attains a certainty in the broader sense (yaqīn bi-l-maʿnā al-ʿamm), matching the definitive indication of the muṭlaq. However, it cannot totally abrogate the Qur'an because that would overrule a text that is certain in the narrower sense (qatʿī al-thubut). Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The core debate is whether khabar mashhur can restrict (taqyid) the muṭlaq of the Qur'an. The objector says no, because mashhur is originally ahad, only giving probability (zann).
Mashhur is defined as a hadith narrated by less than three in the first generation but widespread in later generations.
2
State the Hanafi response to the objection
The Hanafi response argues that the uprightness of the Companions is definitive (qatʿī), especially for those like the participants of Badr. The possibility of intentional lying is eliminated.
The author cites the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun' and the many Quranic praises of the Companions.
3
Understand the role of Ummah acceptance
The acceptance of the mashhur by the Ummah (talqī al-umma bil-qabūl) eliminates the possibility of forgetfulness, because the Ummah would not collectively accept a false attribution.
This makes the possibility of forgetfulness negligible, like the possibility of metaphor in a specific text without evidence.
4
Analyze the epistemological status of mashhur
Mashhur thus yields certainty in the broader sense (al-yaqīn bi-l-maʿnā al-ʿamm), also called ʿilm al-ṭuma'nīna. This is equal to the certainty of the muṭlaq's indication (dalāla).
The muṭlaq's thubut is qatʿī in the narrower sense, but its indication of absoluteness is qatʿī in the broader sense. So both are equally authoritative.
5
Note the limit: partial vs total abrogation
Because mashhur is only qatʿī in the broader sense, it can restrict (taqyid) or specify (takhṣīṣ) the Qur'an, but it cannot abrogate the entire text (nasakh kullī). That would require overruling qatʿī al-thubut with a weaker authority.
The author uses the metaphor of a barzakh (isthmus) between mutawātir and ahad.

فإن الإجماع قطعي في إثبات ما أجمع عليه وإن كان أهل الإجماع ظانين فتأمل، وقد يستدل من قبله أن رواية هذا الجم الغفير من الفحول مع كونهم ذوي الأيدي الطولى في العلوم والمعارف تفيد القطع بأنه قوله صلى الله
