فيما يقال : الخاص مفيد لليقين وهو العلم الذي لا يحتمل الخلاف احتمالاً ناشئاً عن دليل بل لو كان احتمال كان غير معتد به صرح به صدر الشريعة (فيقيد به مطلق الكتاب لأنه قطعي مثل قطعية المطلق، وههنا بحث قد عدّ عويصاً بأن غاية ما لزم من الشهرة قوة ثبوته عن الراوي لا قوة ثبوته عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فإنه آحاد الأصل وهو يفيد الظن، وقبول الجم الغفير إنما هو بعدالة الراوي، وهي تفيد ظن المطابقة للواقع، لأن احتمال السهو والنسيان قائم بل احتمال الكذب وإن كان مرجوحاً فإن العدالة غير مقطوعة، وإذا لم يفد هذا الخبر إلا ظناً مثل ظن خبر الواحد فكيف يجوز تغيير المطلق المقطوع الثبوت، وأيد بأن وبين رسوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فضائلهم غير مرة والإخبار فيها وإن كانت مروية أحاداً لكن القدر المشترك متواتر، وإذا كان كذلك فلا احتمال للكذب عمداً أصلاً، ثم إن بركة صحبة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم واختيار الله تعالى إياهم لتلك الصحبة وبذل جهدهم في حفظ الدين يبعد النسيان بأن لا يحفظوا وينسبوا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ما لم يسمعوا كل البعد ثم إن تلقي الأمة بالقبول يوجب عدم الاعتداد باحتمال النسيان، فإن التلقي بالقبول إنما هو لكونه قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، وبعد هذا فاحتمال النسيان ليس إلا كاحتمال المجاز في الخاص من غير قرينة، فإذن رواية الصحابي المقطوع العدالة الجليل مع تلقي الأمة إياها موجبة لليقين بالمعنى الأعم مثل اليقين في دلالة الخاص فإذا تواترت منه في القرن الثاني والثالث أورث القطع بأنها مروية عن الصحابي الذي هذا شأنه، وروايته مقطوعة بالمعنى الأعم، فالخبر المشهور مقطوع بالمعنى الأعم، ثم مطلق الكتاب وإن كان ثبوته مقطوعاً بالمعنى الأخص لكونه متواتراً إلا أن دلالته على الإطلاق مقطوعة بالمعنى الأعم، فيكون الإطلاق حكم الله تعالى وحكم الخبر المشهور حكمه تعالى متساويان في المقطوعية العامة فيجوز إبطاله به فيجوز التقييد في الابتداء أو نسخ الإطلاق، وكذا يجوز تخصيص عام الكتاب ونسخ بعض أفراده به لهذا، لكن لا يجوز نسخ المطلق رأساً ولا نسخ جميع أفراد العام رأساً بالخبر المشهور، إذ يلزم منه إبطال المقطوع بالمعنى الأخص بالمقطوع بالمعنى الأعم هذا ما عند هذا العبد، ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمراً. والمشهور في إبانة هذا المطلب أن تقييد المطلق بيان من وجه وإبطال من وجه، وكذا الخبر المشهور برزخ بين المتواتر والآحاد فتوفر عليه شبههما فجوز التقييد به دون الإبطال بالكلية، ولا يخفى عليك أنه لو كان بياناً فبيان تغيير فهو إبطال له من كل وجه، فلا صحة لهذا إلا بالإرجاع إلى ما قلنا وقال بعضهم في إبانة هذا المطلب : إن رواية هذا الجم الغفير الذين بلغوا مبلغ التواتر وقد انضم إليه شهادة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالصدق بقوله : خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم يفشو الكذب» توجب للثبوت قوة بنية، فيبلغ مبلغ قوة إطلاق الكتاب فيجوز إبطاله بالتقييد وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن بلوغ الرواة عن الصحابي حد التواتر إنما يوجب ثبوته عنه قطعاً، ولا يلزم منه قوة الثبوت عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وشهادة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم للقرون الثلاثة إنما هي بكثرة العدول فيهم، ثم فشوا الكذب بعدهم، وهو لا يوجب قطعية عدالة كل راو وإما احتمال النسيان والسهو فقائم كما كان، فتأمل والحق لا يجاوز عما أقرأناك سابقاً
For consensus is definitive in establishing what is agreed upon, even if the people of consensus are speculative — so reflect. It may be argued from the former that the narration of this vast multitude of eminent scholars, given their expertise in sciences and knowledge, leads to certainty that it is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions). The answer is that the narration of this vast multitude of eminent scholars only indicates that the narrator is upright and that his narration is obligatory to act upon, not that what they narrate is definitely the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions). Indeed, how can that be when the eminent scholars accepted Ṣaḥīḥ al-Bukhārī without being certain that its narrations are definitely the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions)? Rather, the utmost is strong probability of acceptance — so understand. And the agreement of all that the denier of it is not deemed an unbeliever; as for other than Shaykh Abū Bakr, it is apparent. As for him, because its definitiveness is theoretical, it has entered the realm of ambiguity. And what is said that there remains no benefit in the disagreement — the benefit is that according to him, since it is definitive, it can oppose and abrogate the Book in various ways of abrogation, contrary to the majority, as will soon appear. Rather, its denier is misguided and judged to be in error. And the well-known (mashhur) report necessitates strong probability, like certainty that admits no doubt or possibility arising from evidence at all. This probability is called the knowledge of tranquility, which is sometimes expressed as certainty. It is said: the specific is beneficial for certainty, which is knowledge that does not admit opposition arising from evidence; even if there were a possibility, it would not be considered. This was stated by Ṣadr al-Sharīʿah. So it restricts the absolute (muṭlaq) of the Book because it is definitive like the definitiveness of the absolute. Here there is a discussion that has been considered problematic: the utmost that follows from fame (shuhra) is the strength of its transmission from the narrator, not the strength of its transmission from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), for it is originally a solitary report (āhād) which gives probability. The acceptance by the vast multitude is only due to the narrator's uprightness, which gives probability of correspondence to reality because the possibility of forgetfulness or error exists, as does the possibility of lying (though preponderantly unlikely), since uprightness is not certain. If this report gives only probability like the solitary report, how can it be permissible to change the absolutely established (qatʿī al-thubūt) muṭlaq? This is supported by the fact that it does not exceed hearing from the Companion himself, and that does not add to the Book. The verification of the matter is that the uprightness of the Companions is definitive, especially the participants in Badr and the Pledge of Riḍwān. How could it not be when Allah Almighty praised them in many places in His Book, and His Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions) mentioned their virtues repeatedly? The reports about that, even if narrated singly, the common factor is mutawātir. If so, there is no possibility of intentional lying at all. Then the blessing of companionship with the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) and Allah's choice of them for that companionship, and their utmost effort in preserving the religion, makes forgetfulness far-fetched — that they would fail to remember and attribute to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) what they did not hear. Then the acceptance by the Ummah (talqī al-umma bil-qabūl) necessitates disregarding the possibility of forgetfulness, for acceptance is only because it is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions). After this, the possibility of forgetfulness is only like the possibility of metaphor (majāz) in the specific without evidence. So then the narration of a dignified Companion whose uprightness is definitive, combined with the Ummah's acceptance of it, yields certainty in the broader sense (al-yaqīn bi-l-maʿnā al-ʿamm), like the certainty of the specific's indication. If it becomes mutawātir from him in the second and third centuries, it begets certainty that it is narrated from the Companion who is of this status, and his narration is definitive in the broader sense. Thus the mashhur report is definitive in the broader sense. Then the muṭlaq of the Book, though its establishment (thubūt) is definitive in the narrower sense (al-maʿnā al-akhṣṣ) due to being mutawātir, its indication (dalāla) of absoluteness is definitive in the broader sense. So the absoluteness is a ruling of Allah and the ruling of the mashhur report is a ruling of Allah, both equal in general definitiveness, so it is permissible to abrogate it with it — thus it is permissible to restrict it initially or to abrogate the absoluteness. Similarly, it is permissible to specify (takhṣīṣ) the general (ʿāmm) of the Book and to abrogate some of its individuals with it for this reason. But it is not permissible to abrogate the muṭlaq entirely nor to abrogate all individuals of the general entirely with the mashhur report, because that would entail abrogating the definitive in the narrower sense with the definitive in the broader sense. This is what this servant holds, and perhaps Allah will cause a new matter after this. The well-known expression in explaining this topic is that restricting the muṭlaq is an explanation (bayān) from one aspect and an abrogation (ibṭāl) from another. Similarly, the mashhur report is a barrier (barzakh) between mutawātir and āḥād, so it combines the similarities of both, thus restriction (taqyīd) with it is permitted, but total abrogation is not. It is not hidden from you that if it were an explanation, it would be an explanation of change, which is abrogation from every aspect, so there is no validity for this except by referring to what we said. And some said in explaining this topic: The narration of this vast multitude who reached the level of tawātur, combined with the testimony of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) of truthfulness by his saying, 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then falsehood spreads...' — this strengthens the establishment (thubūt) with a large power, so it reaches the level of the power of the Book's muṭlaq, so abrogation of its muṭlaq by restriction is permissible. There is apparent consideration in this: the reaching of tawātur of narrators from the Companion only necessitates its certainty from him, and does not necessitate strength of certainty from him (the Prophet). And the testimony of the Messenger of Allah about the three generations is only about the abundance of upright people among them, then falsehood spreads after them; this does not require the definitiveness of each narrator. The possibility of forgetfulness and error remains as before. So reflect, and the truth does not go beyond what we taught you previously.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an extensive usul dispute concerning the probative value of khabar mashhur (well-known hadith) and its capacity to restrict (taqyid) the muṭlaq of the Qur'an. The author, commenting on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, defends the Hanafi position that mashhur can indeed restrict the Book, despite the objection that mashhur only yields probability (zann) while the Qur'an is definitively established (qatʿī al-thubut). The objection argues that the strength of mashhur lies in its acceptance by the multitude, which only attests to the narrator's uprightness, not to the certainty of the Prophetic origin. The author refutes this by invoking the definitive uprightness of the Companions, the blessing of companionship, and the Ummah's acceptance (talqī bil-qabūl), which eliminates the possibility of intentional lying and renders the possibility of forgetfulness negligible. Thus, the mashhur report becomes definitive in the broader sense (al-yaqīn bi-l-maʿnā al-ʿamm), equivalent to the definitive indication of the muṭlaq. Therefore, it can abrogate the absoluteness (itlaq) of the Qur'an but cannot abrogate the entire text. The author critiques another view that claims the multitude reaching tawatur combined with the Prophet's praise of the early generations gives mashhur the same strength as the Qur'an, noting that this does not guarantee each narrator's uprightness. The final relied-upon position is that mashhur is a barzakh between mutawātir and ahad, permitting taqyid but not total nasikh.

Key Terms
خبر مشهور (khabar mashhur): A hadith that was narrated by less than three in the first generation but became widespread in the second and third generations — its thubut yields strong probability approaching certainty due to Ummah acceptance.
مطلق (muṭlaq): An unqualified expression in the Qur'an that does not specify quantity or condition; its indication of absoluteness is qatʿī in the broader sense.
علم الطمأنينة (ʿilm al-ṭuma'nīna): Knowledge of tranquility: a strong probability that admits no doubt arising from evidence, sometimes called certainty in the broader sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, can a khabar mashhur abrogate the entire muṭlaq of the Qur'an?
A) Yes, because it is definitive in the broader sense.
B) Yes, because it has the same strength as mutawātir.
C) No, it can only restrict (taqyid) but not totally abrogate.
D) No, mashhur cannot affect the Qur'an at all.

Key Takeaway
Khabar mashhur can restrict the muṭlaq of the Qur'an because it yields certainty in the broader sense (yaqīn bi-l-maʿnā al-ʿamm), but it cannot abrogate the entire text because that would overrule qatʿī al-thubut.

Definition of Khabar Ahad and Certainty of Mutawatir
Defining khabar ahad and affirming mutawatir certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar ahad according to Hanafi usul, distinguishing it from mutawatir and mashhur, and state that mutawatir yields certain knowledge, refuting the Sumaniyya.

Core Idea
Khabar ahad is what is not mutawatir nor mashhur; mutawatir gives certain knowledge.

In Hanafi usul, khabar ahad is defined negatively: any report that falls short of tawatur in the first two generations. This passage provides that definition and asserts the epistemological certainty of mutawatir reports, refuting the Sumaniyya who denied testimonial knowledge. The Sumaniyya are identified as idol worshippers distinct from Brahmins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of ahad
Khabar ahad is defined by exclusion: it is neither mutawatir nor mashhur. Understand that Hanafi usul has three categories: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad.
Ahad is the residual category after removing the other two.
2
Examine the temporal condition
The definition adds that the report was transmitted in the first two generations (Companions and Successors) without reaching the threshold of tawatur. This means the number of narrators at those stages is below what prevents collusion.
If the number reaches tawatur in a later generation, it may become mashhur, not ahad.
3
Grasp the epistemological claim of mutawatir
The passage states that knowledge (ilm) from mutawatir is a firmly established right (haqq thabit). This means such reports yield certain knowledge (yaqin).
This is opposed by the Sumaniyya who deny testimonial certainty.
4
Recognize the polemical context
The author identifies the Sumaniyya as idol worshippers of Somnath and clarifies they are distinct from Brahmins. This shows the historical refutation of those who reject the authority of mutawatir.
The Sumaniyya are not a recognized Islamic school; their objection is epistemological.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآحاد ما ليس أحدهما أي ما ليس متواتراً ولا مشهوراً، بل ما نقل في القرن الأول والثاني من غير بلوغ الرواة حد التواتر . مسألة: العلم بالمتواتر حق ثابت (خلافاً للسمنية من البراهمة) والمشهور أنهم فرقة أخرى غير البراهمة هم عبدة سومنات) اسم لصنم كسره السلطان محمود بن سبكتكين
And ahad (solitary reports) are what are not either of the two — i.e., what is neither mutawatir nor mashhur, but rather what was transmitted in the first and second generations without the narrators reaching the level of tawatur. Issue: Knowledge of the mutawatir is a firmly established right, contrary to al-Sumaniyya among the Brahmins. The well-known view is that they are another group besides the Brahmins — they are worshippers of Somnath, the name of an idol that Sultan Mahmud bin Sabuktigin broke.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage provides a concise definition of khabar ahad (solitary report) and a brief note on mutawatir. Khabar ahad is defined negatively: it is any report that is neither mutawatir (mass transmitted) nor mashhur (well-known). More specifically, it is a report whose number of narrators in the first and second generations (the generations of the Companions and Successors) does not reach the threshold of tawatur (i.e., a number that makes collusion impossible). The term 'ahad' literally means 'ones' or 'singular', indicating that it is not widespread enough to yield certainty. Then the author adds a separate issue (mas'ala): knowledge derived from mutawatir reports is a certain and firmly established truth. This position is held against the Sumaniyya, a sect among the Brahmins who deny the possibility of such knowledge. The author clarifies that the Sumaniyya are a distinct group from the Brahmins, and they are identified as idol worshippers of Somnath, an idol destroyed by Sultan Mahmud of Ghazni.

Key Terms
آحاد (āhād): Solitary reports that are neither mutawātir nor mashhūr; their number of narrators in the first two generations does not reach the threshold of tawātur.
متواتر (mutawātir): A report transmitted by a number that makes collusion impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
السمنية (al-Sumaniyya): A sect of Indian origin, likely Buddhist or idol-worshipping, who deny the possibility of certain knowledge from testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A report transmitted by a single narrator.
B) A report that is neither mutawatir nor mashhur.
C) A report that is weak (daif).
D) A report transmitted only in the second generation.

Key Takeaway
Khabar ahad is defined negatively as not being mutawatir or mashhur; mutawatir yields certain knowledge, refuting the Sumaniyya.

Definition of Khabar Ahad by Negation
Defining khabar ahad by negation of tawatur and mashhur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar ahad by distinguishing it from mutawatir and mashhur and apply the definition to classify a report.

Core Idea
Khabar ahad is any report that fails to meet the conditions of tawatur or shuhra.

In Hanafi usul, reports are classified by transmission strength. This passage gives the defining line for ahad reports: they are neither mutawatir nor mashhur. This negative definition is crucial because it sets the lowest category of transmitted knowledge, which yields only zanni certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two higher categories
Recognize that mutawatir and mashhur are the stronger categories. Mutawatir has many narrators in every generation; mashhur is well-known in the first two centuries but not reaching tawatur.
2
Understand the negative definition
Khabar ahad is defined by what it is not: it is neither mutawatir nor mashhur. This means any report that does not meet the criteria of those two is ahad.
The definition is inclusive: it covers reports with one or more narrators as long as the threshold is not met.
3
Note the time constraint
The definition mentions 'first and second century' for the transmission. This indicates that the classification depends on the early transmission strength, not later circulation.
Mashhur is well-known among scholars in the first two centuries; ahad lacks that status.
4
Apply the definition
Given a hadith, check if it has tawatur (many narrators in each generation) or if it was widely known among early scholars. If neither, it is ahad.
Example: a hadith transmitted by three companions only is ahad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآحاد ما ليس أحدهما أي ما ليس متواتراً ولا مشهوراً، بل ما نقل في القرن الأول والثاني من غير بلوغ الرواة حد التواتر .
And ahad is what is neither one of the two, i.e., it is not mutawatir nor mashhur, rather it is what was transmitted in the first and second century without the narrators reaching the level of tawatur.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is a clear definition of khabar ahad (solitary report). The author defines it negatively: a report that does not meet the conditions of tawatur nor mashhur. It is transmitted by fewer narrators, especially in the first two centuries of Islam, and its chain does not reach the quantity required for tawatur. This definition sets the lowest category of hadith in terms of numerical transmission.

Key Terms
الآحاد (al-ahad): A report that is neither mutawatir nor mashhur; transmitted without reaching the level of tawatur in the first two centuries.
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators in every generation, making falsehood impossible.
مشهور (mashhur): A report that is well-known among the scholars of the first two centuries, but not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A report that is mutawatir in meaning but not in wording.
C) A report that is neither mutawatir nor mashhur.
D) A report that is well-known but not widely transmitted.

Key Takeaway
Khabar ahad is defined by negation: it is any report that fails to meet the criteria of tawatur or shuhra in the first two centuries.

Is Tawatur Knowledge Daruri or Nazari? The Hanafi Stance
Debating the epistemological classification of mutawatir reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the epistemological nature of tawatur knowledge and evaluate the key argument used to defend it.

Core Idea
Tawatur knowledge is daruri because it arises without reflection, as even children and simpletons attain it.

In Hanafi usul, the classification of knowledge derived from mutawatir reports is foundational. This passage examines whether such knowledge is immediate (daruri) or acquired through reasoning (nazari). The majority of Hanafis, along with the author, hold it to be daruri, while some Mu'tazila and Shafi'iyya argue it is nazari. Understanding this distinction affects how we treat mutawatir reports as sources of certainty in law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing classifications
Recognise that the knowledge from tawatur is either daruri (self-evident) or nazari (requires reflection). The Hanafi position favours daruri.
Remember that daruri knowledge, like sensory perception, is immediate.
2
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The text argues: if tawatur knowledge were nazari, it would require explicit premises. But even children and the simple-minded acquire it, so it cannot be nazari. This is the core Hanafi evidence (lana).
The proof hinges on the absence of conscious reasoning in the recipient.
3
Examine the counterarguments
Opponents (al-Ka'bi, Abu al-Husayn, Imam al-Haramayn) hold that tawatur knowledge involves an implicit syllogism, making it nazari. Al-Ghazali’s view that it belongs to 'propositions whose syllogisms are with them' bridges the gap.
The dispute is largely semantic, as the author notes.
4
Consider the gradual strengthening argument
Mirzajan's note explains that belief from reports strengthens gradually; the final stage is still daruri because the exact threshold is not consciously known. The Hanafi response: gradual increase does not imply conscious reasoning.
This addresses the objection that tawatur knowledge builds over time.
5
Determine the practical import
The thamarah (practical consequence) may affect whether a person is considered a muqallid or mujtahid regarding mutawatir reports. But since the dispute is mostly terminological, the Hanafi ruling that tawatur gives yaqin remains unchanged.
The tarjih leans toward Ghazali’s compromise as nearest to correctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الجمهور على أن ذلك العلم الحاصل من المتواتر (ضروري) غير متوقف على النظر حاصل (بالعادة، ومال) الإمام حجة الإسلام (الغزالي قدس سره (إلى أنه من قبيل قضايا قياساتها معها والنزاع معنوي إن أراد الجمهور أنه قسم آخر من الضروري، وهو يحصل بالعادة وإن أرادوا بالضروري مطلق الضروري فلا نزاع بحسب المعنى، وهو الظاهر، فإن الأليق بالفقهاء والمتكلمين مطلق الضرورة (وهو) أي ميل الإمام حجة الإسلام (قريب) إلى الصواب، لأن الوسط متحقق البتة، ولما لم يتوقف عليه صار الوسط معه (وقال الكعبي وأبو الحسين كلاهما من المعتزلة (والإمام) إمام الحرمين من الشافعية (أنه نظري) حاصل بالفكر وتوقف المرتضى) الرافضي (والآمدي) من الشافعية (لنا) على كونه ضرورياً ولا فطرياً (لو كان العلم الحاصل بالتواتر (نظرياً لافتقر إلى توسط (المقدمتين أو أكثر، ولا يحصل بدون المقدمات أصلاً (والعلم بالمتواترات المذكورة ليس كذلك فإن العلم يحصل بمجرد سماع الخبر عن جماعة موصوفين حتى يحصل العلم به لمن لا يقدر على الكسب كالبله والصبيان (قيل) في حواشي ميرزاجان (الاعتقاد الحاصل بسماع الخبر يتقوى بتدريج) فإن الحاصل عند إخبار واحد ظن ضعيف، ثم إذا انضم إليه إخبار واحد آخر يتقوى ذلك الظن ثم وثم إلى أن يحصل العلم والقوة البشرية قاصرة عن ضبط ذلك البلوغ في أي وقت بلغ حد العلم
Issue: The majority (of scholars) hold that the knowledge obtained from mutawatir (is necessary) not dependent on reflection, obtained (by custom. And) the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali, may Allah sanctify his soul) (inclined) to the view that it belongs to the category of propositions whose syllogisms are with them; and the dispute is semantic. If the majority meant that it is another type of necessary knowledge, and it is obtained by custom, and if they meant by necessary absolute necessary knowledge, then there is no dispute in meaning. And that is apparent, for what is more fitting for jurists and theologians is absolute necessity. (And his inclination, i.e., the Proof of Islam, is near) to correctness, because the middle term is definitely realized, and since it is not dependent on it, the middle term is with it. (And al-Ka'bi and Abu al-Husayn, both from the Mu'tazila, (and al-Imam) Imam al-Haramayn from the Shafi'iyya (held that it is theoretical) obtained by reflection. And al-Murtada) the Rafidi, (and al-Amidi) from the Shafi'iyya, hesitated. (For us) in favor of its being necessary and not intuitive: (If the knowledge obtained from tawatur were theoretical, it would require the mediation of two premises or more, and would not be obtained without premises at all. (But the knowledge of the mentioned mutawatirat is not so, for knowledge is obtained merely by hearing the report from a group characterized as such, to the extent that it is obtained by one who cannot engage in reasoning, like the simple-minded and children. (It was said) in the footnotes of Mirzajan: (The belief obtained by hearing the report strengthens gradually,) for what is obtained from a single reporter is weak conjecture; then when another reporter joins, that conjecture strengthens, then again, until knowledge is obtained. Human power is incapable of pinpointing the exact moment when it reaches the limit of knowledge.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological nature of knowledge gained from tawatur. The majority (jumhur) of scholars, including many Hanafis, hold it to be necessary (daruri), meaning it arises automatically without conscious reasoning. Imam al-Ghazali inclined to the view that it is like 'propositions whose syllogisms are with them' – i.e., the inferential steps are implicitly present but not consciously engaged. The author considers Ghazali's view close to correct because the middle term (i.e., the evidence) is definitely present. Al-Ka'bi and Abu al-Husayn (Mu'tazila) and Imam al-Haramayn (Shafi'i) held it is theoretical (nazari), requiring reflection. Al-Murtada (Rafidi) and al-Amidi (Shafi'i) hesitated. The Hanafi proof is given: if it were theoretical, it would require explicit premises, but even children and the simple-minded gain knowledge from hearing mutawatir reports. A note from Mirzajan clarifies that belief from reports strengthens gradually, and human power cannot determine the exact threshold when it becomes certain.

Key Terms
ضروري (ḍarūrī): Knowledge that is self-evident and arises without reflection, like sensory knowledge.
نظري (naẓarī): Knowledge that requires reflection and inferential reasoning.
قضايا قياساتها معها (qaḍāyā qiyāsātuhā maʿahā): Propositions whose syllogistic form is implicitly contained within them, requiring no external premises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the Hanafi position (lana) for tawatur being daruri?
A) Even those unable to reason, like children, gain knowledge from mutawatir reports
B) Tawatur requires many transmitters
C) The Quran commands accepting testimony
D) It is a matter of consensus

Key Takeaway
Knowledge from tawatur is daruri because it is obtained without conscious reasoning, a fact evident from its acquisition by the least reflective individuals.

Is Knowledge from Mutawatir Reports Necessary or Theoretical?
Debate on whether knowledge from tawatur is necessary or theoretical

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the epistemological status of mutawatir knowledge, explain the Hanafi proof from immediate certainty, and evaluate the counterarguments from the opposing schools.

Core Idea
Knowledge from tawatur is necessary, not theoretical—even the insane attain it without reasoning.

This passage tackles a foundational usul question: does the certainty from massively transmitted reports (tawatur) arise necessarily or through deliberate reasoning? The Hanafi school, along with the majority, argues for necessity (daruri), while some Mu'tazila and Shafi'i scholars hold it is theoretical (nazari). The dispute has significant implications for how we understand the epistemology of transmitted knowledge in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
Is the knowledge from tawatur necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari)? Note that both sides agree on the certainty of the knowledge; the dispute is about its epistemic mechanism.
The question is epistemological, not about the validity of the report itself.
2
Pinpoint the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument (lana) is that knowledge from tawatur is obtained immediately by hearing a sufficient multitude, without need for reasoning, as demonstrated by the insane and children who cannot reason.
This is a direct observation (mushahada) that knowledge arises without syllogism.
3
Examine the opposing arguments
Opponents (al-Ka'bi, Abu al-Husayn, Imam al-Haramayn) argue that tawatur requires premises (e.g., the large group has no motive to lie) and if it were necessary its necessity would be self-evident, yet there is disagreement.
These are rational arguments that challenge the immediate nature of tawatur knowledge.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the premises are not consciously needed; the knowledge is immediate. The disagreement itself is verbal (ma'nawi) about the definition of 'necessary'—if 'necessary' excludes any reflection, then tawatur is not necessary, but if it means 'does not require explicit syllogistic reasoning,' then it is necessary.
The author sides with Ghazali that the dispute is close to verbal, with the Hanafi view being correct.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tawatur knowledge is necessary (daruri). This has no direct impact on fiqh rulings but affects how usul scholars argue about the foundation of transmitted knowledge.
All schools accept tawatur as certain; the dispute is academic.

هو محال بالذات والعادة تفيد العلم باستحالته فتأمل. وأيضاً : الممكن بالذات لا يلزم منه محال بالنظر إلى ذاته، وأما بحسب الواقع فقد يستلزم محالاً بالذات، فهذا الإخبار وإن كان في نفسه ممكناً غير مستلزم للمحال لعدم وجوب العلم منه بالذات لكنه مستحيل في الواقع بالعادة، فيستلزم في الواقع المحال لإيجاب العادة العلم به فافهم وعن) الدليل (الرابع) وهو لزوم صدق إخبار اليهود والنصارى الكاذبة بيقين بأن تواترها ممنوع و(أن ابتداءه ليس كوسطه) بل لم يوجد في الابتداء مخبرون بعدد التواتر إنما هم بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا أمثال هذه الأقاويل وأخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين وهم أخبروا ظناً، بل علماً بالكذب شياطينهم الآخرين، فقد وجد في الوسط مبلغ التواتر، ثم إن كلهم ظانون غير مستيقنين، فلم يوجد التواتر، ومثل هذا إخبار الشيعة بالنص الجلي على إمامة أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأشجعين علي بن أبي طالب كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام، فإن بعض شياطينهم اخترعوا وكذبوا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، ثم أخبروا شياطينهم الآخرين حتى صار منقولاً فيهم، ثم إن الشبهة إنما ترد على من لا يشترط العدالة في التواتر وأما على الشارط فلا تتجه أصلاً فتدبر (وعن) الدليل (الخامس) وهو وجدان التفاوت بينه وبين البديهي الآخر الموجب لاحتمال النقيض أن غاية ما لزم من شبههم التفاوت في الجملة و لا نسلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت) فإنه قد يكون البعض خفياً عن بعض لعدم ملاحظة الأطراف حقها، أو لمصاحبة بعض الوسط دون بعض نعم إنها لا تتفاوت بمعنى احتمال أحدها النقيض دون الاخر ولزومه ههنا ممنوع، بل المتواتر والواحد نصف الاثنين لا يحتمل كل منهما النقيض ( ولو سلم أن العلوم لا تتفاوت جلاء وخفاء أصلاً ( فالتفاوت) ههنا (للإنس وعدمه لا لكون أحدهما جلياً والآخر خفياً فتدبر

(مسألة: الجمهور على أن ذلك العلم الحاصل من المتواتر (ضروري) غير متوقف على النظر حاصل (بالعادة، ومال) الإمام حجة الإسلام (الغزالي قدس سره (إلى أنه من قبيل قضايا قياساتها معها والنزاع معنوي إن أراد الجمهور أنه قسم آخر من الضروري، وهو يحصل بالعادة وإن أرادوا بالضروري مطلق ،الضروري فلا نزاع بحسب المعنى، وهو الظاهر، فإن الأليق بالفقهاء والمتكلمين مطلق الضرورة (وهو) أي ميل الإمام حجة الإسلام (قريب) إلى الصواب، لأن الوسط متحقق البتة، ولما لم يتوقف عليه صار الوسط معه (وقال الكعبي وأبو الحسين كلاهما من المعتزلة (والإمام) إمام الحرمين من الشافعية (أنه نظري) حاصل بالفكر وتوقف المرتضى) الرافضي (والآمدي) من الشافعية (لنا) على كونه ضرورياً ولا فطرياً (لو كان العلم الحاصل بالتواتر (نظرياً لافتقر إلى توسط (المقدمتين أو أكثر، ولا يحصل بدون المقدمات أصلاً (والعلم بالمتواترات المذكورة ليس كذلك فإن العلم يحصل بمجرد سماع الخبر عن جماعة موصوفين حتى يحصل العلم به لمن لا يقدر على الكسب كالبله والصبيان (قيل) في حواشي ميرزاجان (الاعتقاد الحاصل بسماع الخبر يتقوى بتدرج) فإن الحاصل عند إخبار واحد ظن ضعيف، ثم إذا انضم إليه إخبار واحد آخر يتقوى ذلك الظن ثم وثم إلى أن يحصل العلم والقوة البشرية قاصرة عن ضبط ذلك البلوغ في أي وقت بلغ حد العلم

واليقين (فلعل العلم (الحاصل (أولاً) حاصل (بالفكر والذهن لم يحفظ كيفية حصوله) فلا يلزم البداهة (أقول) في الجواب إذا أخبر الجم الغفير العظيم البالغ حد التواتر (دفعة حصل العلم بغتة فلا تدريج) هناك في الحصول (ولا ترتيب في المقدمات قطعاً، والضرورة الغير المكذوبة شاهدة بأن المتواترات سواسية في حصول العلم، فإذا ثبت تحقق العلم في بعض المتواترات بالبداهة ثبت في الكل فتأمل) ولا يرد على ما قررنا أن حصول العلم بغتة من غير ترتيب في بعض الصور لا يلزم منه الحصول في الكل من غير ترتيب ولك أن تجيب أيضاً بأن تقوى الاعتقاد تدريجاً وقصور القوة البشرية عن حفظ وقت البلوغ وإن سلم لكن لا يلزم منهما أن لا يعلم كيفية الحصول، بل يعلم بالضرورة أن العلم الحاصل ضروري، وإن لم يعلم وقت حصوله، وأيضاً بينه بحصوله للبله والصبيان الذين لم يقدروا على الكسب فافهم. (واستدل) بأنه (لو كان) العلم الحاصل بالمتواتر (نظرياً لم يكن الخلاف فيه بهتاً) باطلاً، بل يجوز وقوع الخلاف فيه كما في سائر النظريات والتالي باطل ويرد عليه أنه يجوز أن يكون من النظريات الجلية أي الواضحة المقدمات التي لا يتطرق إليها المخالفة لصحة مقدمات الدليل بلا ريبة كالحسابيات والهندسيات) التي لا يخالف فيها غافل، فإن قلت غرض المستدل لو كان نظرياً لم يكن الخلاف فيه مكابرة والحسابيات ليس الخلاف فيها مكابرة بل لصحة المقدمات لم يخالف قيل إن أردت بالمكابرة خلاف البداهة فبطلان اللازم ،ممنوع بل يكاد يكون مصادرة، وإن أردت إنكار القطعي فالملازمة ممنوعة، فإنكار الحسابيات أيضاً مكابرة بهذا المعنى فتدبر، والحق أن غرض المستدل أنه لو كان نظرياً لاستفيد من أنه خبر جماعة بالغة حد التواتر، وكل كذلك فهو حق، ولا يخفى أنه يتطرق إليه الشغب وليس إنكارها مثل إنكار القطعيات وليس توجد مقدمات قطعية أخرى يمكن الاكتساب منها، فلا يكون الإنكار بهتاً، كإنكار سائر القواطع والتالي ،باطل فلزم البداهة قطعاً، ولعله هو مراد المصنف مما قال في «الحاشية» : إن مرادهم أنه لو كان نظرياً لم يكن التشكيك في بادىء الرأي مثل تشكيك السوفسطائية، فلا يرد عليه أنه إن أراد أنه مثل تشكيك السوفسطائية قبل ملاحظة المقدمات فممنوع، وبعد ملاحظتها فمثله التشكيك في الحسابيات وسائر القواطع النظرية، فتأمل (قالوا: أولاً لا يحصل العلم بالمتواتر إلا بعد العلم بأنه خبر في المحسوس عن جماعة لا داعي لهم إلى الكذب، وكل ما كان كذلك كان صادقاً وهذا دليل، فقد حصل العلم في المتواتر بالاستدلال، فلا بداهة (والجواب) لا نسلم توقف العلم بالمتواتر على هذه المقدمات و أن وجود صورة الترتيب يوجب الاحتياج إليه فإنها ممكنة في كل ضروري مثلاً الأربعة زوج) فإنه يمكن فيه أن يقال إنه منقسم بمتساويين، وكل منقسم بمتساويين زوج والكل أعظم من الجزء) فيمكن فيه أن الكل مشتمل على الجزء، وما سواه وما هو كذلك أعظم (و) قالوا (ثانياً : لو كان العلم) بالمتواتر (ضرورياً لعلم أنه ضروري بالضرورة) من غير حاجة إلى تجشم، لأن المراجعة إلى الوجدان وكيفية الحصول كافٍ فيه، وإن كان ضرورياً فلم يختلف فيه) والتالي باطل (والجواب) المعارضة بالقلب بأن يقال : (لو كان نظرياً لعلم نظريته بالضرورة) بالمراجعة إلى ما لا هو
It is inherently impossible, and custom/nature informs of knowledge of its impossibility, so reflect. Also: the inherently possible does not necessitate impossibility in itself, but in actuality it may entail inherent impossibility. So this report, although in itself possible and not entailing impossibility due to lack of necessary knowledge from it inherently, is actually impossible by custom, so it entails actual impossibility because custom necessitates knowledge of it, so understand. (And as for) the fourth proof (which is the necessary truth of the false reports of Jews and Christians because their tawatur is denied, and that its beginning is not like its middle, but rather at the beginning there were no reporters in the number of tawatur; rather they were some of their devils who invented such sayings and informed their other devils, and they informed their other devils with presumption, indeed with knowledge of falsehood, so in the middle there was the amount of tawatur, but then all of them were presuming, not certain, so tawatur did not occur. And similar to this is the report of the Shia of the explicit text on the Imamate of the Commander of the Faithful and the Imam of the brave, Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family), for some of their devils invented and lied against the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), then informed their other devils until it became transmitted among them. Then the doubt only applies to those who do not require probity in tawatur; as for those who require it, it does not apply at all, so ponder. (And as for) the fifth proof (which is the perception of difference between it and other self-evident [knowledge], which necessitates possibility of the opposite, the utmost that follows from their doubt is difference in general, and we do not concede that knowledge does not differ, for sometimes some is hidden from some due to lack of proper consideration of aspects, or due to accompanying some intermediaries without others. Yes, they do not differ in the sense that one of them could admit the opposite while the other does not, and its necessitation here is denied, rather the mutawatir and the fact that two is half of four do not admit the opposite. (And if it is conceded that knowledge does not differ in clarity and obscurity at all, then the difference here is due to familiarity and its absence, not because one is clear and the other obscure, so ponder. (Issue: The majority are of the view that this knowledge obtained from tawatur is necessary [daruri], not dependent on reflection, obtained by custom. Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah sanctify his secret) inclined to the view that it belongs to the category of propositions whose middle terms accompany them. The dispute is verbal. If the majority mean that it is another type of the necessary, and it is obtained by custom, and if they mean by necessary the absolute necessary, then there is no dispute in meaning - and this is apparent, for it is more fitting for jurists and theologians to mean absolute necessity. (And his inclination - i.e., Imam al-Ghazali - is close to correctness, because the middle term is definitely present, but since knowledge does not depend on it, the middle term is with it. (And al-Ka'bi and Abu al-Husayn, both from the Mu'tazila, and Imam al-Haramayn from the Shafi'is said that it is theoretical [nazari], obtained by thought. And al-Murtada the Rafidi and al-Amidi from the Shafi'is hesitated. (Our proof for it being necessary and not innate: If knowledge from tawatur were theoretical, it would require mediation of two or more premises, and would not be obtained without premises at all. But knowledge of the mentioned mutawatir reports is not like that, for knowledge is obtained simply by hearing the report from a group described [as numerous], so that it is obtained by one who cannot acquire [knowledge], like the insane and children. (It was said in the glosses of Mirzajan: The belief obtained by hearing a report increases gradually, for what is obtained from a single reporter is a weak presumption, then when another reporter joins it, that presumption strengthens, then again and again until knowledge is obtained. And human power is incapable of grasping that limit, at what point it reached the limit of knowledge and certainty. So perhaps the knowledge obtained first is obtained by thought and mind, but one does not preserve how it occurred, so self-evidence does not follow.) (I say in response: If a great multitude reaching the limit of tawatur reports all at once, knowledge occurs suddenly without gradation or order in the premises, certainly. And undeniable necessity witnesses that mutawatir reports are equal in the attainment of knowledge. So if the attainment of knowledge in some mutawatir reports is established as self-evident, it is established in all, so ponder. And it is not refuted against what we have stated that sudden occurrence without order in some cases does not necessitate occurrence in all without order. But you may also respond that the gradual strengthening of belief and the deficiency of human power to retain the time of attainment - even if conceded - they do not entail that one does not know the manner of occurrence. Rather, one knows necessarily that the knowledge obtained is necessary, even if one does not know the time of its occurrence. Also, it is proven by its occurrence to the insane and children who are incapable of acquisition, so understand. (And they argued) that if knowledge from tawatur were theoretical, then disagreement about it would not be blatantly false, rather disagreement would be possible as in other theoretical matters - but the consequent is false. It is replied that it could be among the clear theoretical matters, i.e., those with clear premises that are not subject to objection because of the soundness of the premises without doubt, like arithmetic and geometry, about which no inattentive person disagrees. If you say: The aim of the arguer is that if it were theoretical, disagreement about it would not be obstinate; and in arithmetic, disagreement is not obstinate but because of sound premises no one disagrees. It is said: If you mean by obstinate disagreement against self-evidence, then the denial of the consequent is prevented; indeed it is nearly a petitio. And if you mean denial of certainty, the implication is prevented, for denial of arithmetic is also obstinate in this sense, so ponder. The truth is that the arguer's aim is that if it were theoretical, it would be derived from its being a report of a group reaching tawatur, and everything like that is true. It is not hidden that it is subject to cavil, and its denial is not like denial of certainties, and there are no other certain premises from which it can be acquired, so denial is not obstruct; rather it is like denial of other certainties, and the consequent is false, so self-evidence necessarily follows. Perhaps this is what the author meant in his hashya: They intended that if it were theoretical, then doubt at first glance would not be like the doubt of the Sophists. So it is not refuted that if he means it is like the doubt of the Sophists before examining premises, it is prevented, and after examining them, it is like doubt in arithmetic and other theoretical certainties, so ponder. (They said: First, knowledge from tawatur is not obtained except after knowing that it is a report of sense perception from a group with no motive to lie, and everything like that is true. This is a proof, so knowledge in tawatur is obtained by deduction, not self-evidence. (The response: We do not concede that knowledge from tawatur depends on these premises, and that the existence of a form of order necessitates need for it, for it is possible in every necessary [knowledge], e.g., four is even, for it can be said that it is divisible into two equals, and everything divisible into two equals is even; and the whole is greater than the part, for it can be said that the whole contains the part and what is beyond it, and whatever is like that is greater. (And they said: Second, if knowledge were necessary, it would be known as necessary by necessity without need for effort, because recourse to inner sense and the manner of occurrence suffices. But if it were necessary, there would be no disagreement about it. The consequent is false. (The response) is a counter-objection by saying: If it were theoretical, its theoretically would be known by necessity by recourse to ... (text cut off at page end)

Commentary
This passage addresses the epistemological status of knowledge from mutawatir (massively transmitted) reports: is it necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari)? The author first refutes two objections against tawatur: the fourth objection regarding false reports from Jews/Christians/Shia is answered by noting that their transmissions lack probity (adala) and started from liars; the fifth objection about perceived differences between tawatur and other self-evident knowledge is answered by attributing apparent differences to familiarity, not to inherent uncertainty. Then the main dispute is presented: the majority (Jumhur) say tawatur knowledge is necessary, obtained by custom. Imam al-Ghazali inclines that it is like propositions with their middle terms (qadaya qiyasatuha ma'aha), making it close to necessary but technically theoretical. Al-Ka'bi, Abu al-Husayn (Mu'tazila), and Imam al-Haramayn (Shafi'i) hold it is purely theoretical. The Hanafi argument (lana) for necessity is that tawatur knowledge is obtained immediately by hearing the report from a sufficient multitude, even by those incapable of reasoning (insane, children). An objection from Mirzajan's glosses that knowledge increases gradually is answered by noting that if the multitude reports simultaneously, knowledge occurs suddenly without gradation. Further arguments: if tawatur were theoretical, disagreement would be possible, but it is considered obstinate; opponents respond that it could be clear theoretical like arithmetic. The author counters that denial of tawatur is indeed obstinate like denial of arithmetic. Finally, opponents argue that tawatur requires premises (report of a group with no motive to lie, etc.), but the author responds that such premises are not explicitly required; they are implicit in the very act of hearing a massive report, just as necessary truths like 'four is even' can be structured syllogistically without actually requiring syllogism for their knowledge. The second objection (if necessary, its necessity would be self-evident) is met with a counter-objection: if theoretical, its theoretically would be self-evident, but it is not, so it is necessary. The passage concludes with the author affirming that tawatur knowledge is necessary (daruri) as per the Hanafi position, though the dispute is largely verbal regarding what 'necessary' means.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): A transmission (of a report) by such a large number of narrators in each generation that it is impossible for them to have colluded on a falsehood, producing certain knowledge.
ضروري (ḍarūrī): Knowledge that is acquired necessarily (iḍṭirār) without need for reflection (naẓar) or acquisition (kasb), arising from custom ('āda).
نظري (naẓarī): Knowledge that requires reflection, reasoning, and premises; it is acquired through theoretical investigation (naẓar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the nature of knowledge from mutawatir (massively transmitted) reports?
A) It is theoretical (nazari) and depends on explicit syllogistic premises.
B) It is necessary (daruri) and arises immediately from hearing the report from a sufficient multitude.
C) It is impossible to obtain certainty from tawatur.
D) It is theoretical but the dispute is merely verbal.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge from mutawatir reports is necessary (daruri) in Hanafi usul, arising immediately upon hearing the report from a sufficient multitude, not through syllogistic reasoning.

advanced
10 min
Knowledge from Tawatur: Necessary or Acquired?
Debate on whether knowledge from tawatur is badihi or nazari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi claim that knowledge from mutawatir is necessary (badihi) and distinguish it from the opposing view that it is acquired (nazari), using the proofs and responses presented in the text.

Core Idea
Knowledge from tawatur is necessary, not inferred—just as 'four is even' is known without syllogism.

This passage delves into a foundational debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: is the certainty derived from mass-transmitted (mutawatir) reports immediate (badihi) or does it require inference (nazari)? The commentator defends the Hanafi position that such knowledge is necessary, citing the sudden and uniform occurrence of conviction even in children. The opposing view, held by some mutakallimun, is refuted through careful epistemological analysis. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the Hanafi stance and the key arguments on both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
Read the first few lines to find the central dispute: whether knowledge from tawatur is badihi (necessary) or nazari (acquired).
The commentator uses 'قلت' (I say) to signal his own defense of the Hanafi view.
2
Analyze the first Hanafi argument
Look for the claim that knowledge arises 'دفعة' (suddenly) without gradation or order of premises, and note the example of simple-minded and children who lack reasoning capacity.
This is a key evidence: if tawatur were acquired, such individuals could not obtain it.
3
Examine the opponent's objection
The opponent argues that if tawatur were necessary, disagreement would be impossible (like with arithmetic). Find this objection and note how the Hanafi responds by distinguishing between clear theoretical matters (nazariyat jaliyya) and true necessities.
The Hanafi response uses the example of 'four is even' to show that even necessary truths can be cast as syllogisms after the fact.
4
Unpack the second objection (premises required)
The opponent claims that tawatur knowledge depends on premises (e.g., reporters are truthful). Find the Hanafi counter: these premises are not consciously considered; the knowledge is direct.
The commentator argues that the existence of a syllogistic form does not prove actual derivation.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if tawatur is necessary, one need not verify conditions for certainty; if acquired, verification is required. The text sides with necessity.
This outcome affects how mutawatir hadith and Quranic transmission are treated epistemologically.

واليقين (فلعل العلم (الحاصل (أولاً) حاصل (بالفكر والذهن لم يحفظ كيفية حصوله) فلا يلزم البداهة (أقول) في الجواب إذا أخبر الجم الغفير العظيم البالغ حد التواتر (دفعة حصل العلم بغتة فلا تدريج) هناك في الحصول (ولا ترتيب في المقدمات قطعاً، والضرورة الغير المكذوبة شاهدة بأن المتواترات سواسية في حصول العلم، فإذا ثبت تحقق العلم في بعض المتواترات بالبداهة ثبت في الكل فتأمل) ولا يرد على ما قررنا أن حصول العلم بغتة من غير ترتيب في بعض الصور لا يلزم منه الحصول في الكل من غير ترتيب ولك أن تجيب أيضاً بأن تقوى الاعتقاد تدريجاً وقصور القوة البشرية عن حفظ وقت البلوغ وإن سلم لكن لا يلزم منهما أن لا يعلم كيفية الحصول، بل يعلم بالضرورة أن العلم الحاصل ضروري، وإن لم يعلم وقت حصوله، وأيضاً بينه بحصوله للبله والصبيان الذين لم يقدروا على الكسب فافهم. الخلاف فيها مكابرة بل لصحة المقدمات لم يخالف قيل إن أردت بالمكابرة خلاف البداهة فبطلان اللازم ،ممنوع بل يكاد يكون مصادرة، وإن أردت إنكار القطعي فالملازمة ممنوعة، فإنكار الحسابيات أيضاً مكابرة بهذا المعنى فتدبر، والحق أن غرض المستدل أنه لو كان نظرياً لاستفيد من أنه خبر جماعة بالغة حد التواتر، وكل كذلك فهو حق، ولا يخفى أنه يتطرق إليه الشغب وليس إنكارها مثل إنكار القطعيات وليس توجد مقدمات قطعية أخرى يمكن الاكتساب منها، فلا يكون الإنكار بهتاً، كإنكار سائر القواطع والتالي ،باطل فلزم البداهة قطعاً، ولعله هو مراد المصنف مما قال في «الحاشية» : إن مرادهم أنه لو كان نظرياً لم يكن التشكيك في بادىء الرأي مثل تشكيك السوفسطائية، فلا يرد عليه أنه إن أراد أنه مثل تشكيك السوفسطائية قبل ملاحظة المقدمات فممنوع، وبعد ملاحظتها فمثله التشكيك في الحسابيات وسائر القواطع النظرية، فتأمل (قالوا: أولاً لا يحصل العلم بالمتواتر إلا بعد العلم بأنه خبر في المحسوس عن جماعة لا داعي لهم إلى الكذب، وكل ما كان كذلك كان صادقاً وهذا دليل، فقد حصل العلم في المتواتر بالاستدلال، فلا بداهة (والجواب) لا نسلم توقف العلم بالمتواتر على هذه المقدمات و أن وجود صورة الترتيب يوجب الاحتياج إليه فإنها ممكنة في كل ضروري مثلاً الأربعة زوج) فإنه يمكن فيه أن يقال إنه منقسم بمتساويين، وكل منقسم بمتساويين زوج والكل أعظم من الجزء) فيمكن فيه أن الكل مشتمل على الجزء، وما سواه وما هو كذلك أعظم (و) قالوا (ثانياً : لو كان العلم) بالمتواتر (ضرورياً لعلم أنه ضروري بالضرورة) من غير حاجة إلى تجشم، لأن المراجعة إلى الوجدان وكيفية الحصول كافٍ فيه، وإن كان ضرورياً فلم يختلف فيه) والتالي باطل (والجواب) المعارضة بالقلب بأن يقال : (لو كان نظرياً لعلم نظريته بالضرورة) بالمراجعة إلى كيفية الحصول فلم يختلف فيه والحل (أن الملازمة الأولى ممنوعة، فإن (بداهة البديهي يجوز أن تكون نظرية فإن البداهة صفة خارجة عن الشيء، فيجوز أن لا يعلم ثبوته إلا بالكسب والمراجعة إلى كيفية الحصول غير كافية فإنها قد تنسى بتطاول الزمان وكثرة الصور ووجود صورة الترتيب، هل كان هذا حاصلاً بالنظر وقد نسي، أو بالبديهة لا سيما في التصديقات، فإنه بعد البيان بالمقدمات يبقى العلم بالمطلوب ضرورة، فيقع الشك في أنه هل كان ههنا مقدمات نسيت أو لم تكن بل حصل ضرورة، وأما في التصورات فقد ناقش بعض المتأخرين، وقد بينا ما هو الحق في حواشينا على الحاشية الزاهدية المتعلقة بشرح المواقف ولو سلم) أن بداهة البديهي بديهية فلا تستلزم البداهة الوفاق لجواز الخفاء) فإنّ البديهي ربما يكون خفياً فيختلف فيه فلا نسلم الملازمة الثانية، ألم تر السوفسطائية كيف خالفوا في القضايا الضرورية ( فتدبر) ولا تزل فإنه مزلة .
And certainty (perhaps the knowledge obtained (first) is obtained (by thought and mind but its manner of acquisition is not preserved) so necessity is not required. (I say) in response: when a large multitude reaching the level of tawatur reports (suddenly knowledge is obtained instantaneously without gradation) there is no gradation in acquisition (and certainly no order in the premises, and undeniable necessity witnesses that mutawatirat are equal in obtaining knowledge. So if it is established that knowledge in some mutawatirat is obtained by necessity, it is established in all, so reflect.) And it is not refuted by our assertion that obtaining knowledge suddenly without order in some forms does not entail obtaining in all without order. You may also respond by saying that strength of belief gradually and the inadequacy of human power to preserve the time of attainment, even if conceded, do not entail that one does not know the manner of acquisition; rather, one knows necessarily that the obtained knowledge is necessary, even if one does not know its time of attainment. Also, he explained it by its occurrence to the simple-minded and children who are not capable of acquisition, so understand. (And he argued) that (if) knowledge obtained by tawatur (were acquired (nazari), then disagreement about it would not be sheer obstinacy) invalid; rather disagreement about it would be permissible as in other theoretical matters, and the consequent is false. It is refuted that it may be among the evident theoretical matters, i.e., those with clear premises that are not subject to opposition due to the soundness of the premises of the proof without doubt, like arithmetic and geometry, in which no heedless person disagrees. If you say: the arguer's purpose is that if it were acquired, disagreement about it would not be obstinacy, but disagreement about arithmetic is not obstinacy; rather, due to the soundness of the premises, no one disagrees. It is said: if you mean by obstinacy contradiction of necessity, then the falsity of the consequent is denied; rather it is almost begging the question. If you mean denial of certainty, then the entailment is denied, for denial of arithmetic is also obstinacy in this sense, so reflect. The truth is that the arguer's purpose is that if it were acquired, it would be derived from the fact that it is the report of a group reaching the level of tawatur, and everything like that is truth, and it is not hidden that it is subject to quibbling, and its denial is not like denial of certainties, and there are no other certain premises from which it can be acquired, so the denial is not obstinacy, like denial of other certainties. The consequent is false, so necessity necessarily follows. Perhaps this is what the author meant in what he said in 'Al-Hashiya': that their meaning is that if it were acquired, skepticism at first glance would not be like the skepticism of the Sophists. So it is not refuted by saying that if he meant it is like the skepticism of the Sophists before considering the premises, it is denied; after considering them, skepticism about it is like skepticism about arithmetic and other theoretical certainties, so reflect. (They said: First, knowledge of the mutawatir is not obtained except after knowing that it is a report about the sensible from a group with no motive to lie, and everything like that is truthful, and this is a proof. So knowledge in mutawatir is obtained by reasoning, so it is not necessary. (The answer) We do not concede that knowledge of the mutawatir depends on these premises, and that the existence of a form of order necessitates need for it; for it is possible in every necessary matter, e.g., four is even) for it can be said about it that it is divisible into two equals, and everything divisible into two equals is even, and the whole is greater than the part, so it can be said about it that the whole includes the part and what is besides it, and that which is so is greater. (And) they said (secondly: if knowledge) of the mutawatir (were necessary, then it would be known as necessary by necessity) without need for effort, because reference to conscience and manner of acquisition is sufficient for it; and if it were necessary, why would there be disagreement about it?) The consequent is false. (The answer) Counter objection by heart by saying: (if it were acquired, its acquiredness would be known by necessity) by reference to the manner of acquisition, so why would there be disagreement about it? The solution (is that the first entailment is denied, for the (necessity of the necessary may be acquired, for necessity is an attribute external to the thing, so it may not be known except by acquisition. Reference to the manner of acquisition is insufficient, for it may be forgotten due to length of time and multiplicity of forms and the existence of the form of order: was this obtained by reasoning and then forgotten, or by intuition? Especially in affirmations, after explanation by premises, knowledge of the sought remains necessary, so doubt arises whether there were premises here that were forgotten or none and it was obtained necessarily. As for conceptualizations, some later scholars have discussed it, and we have explained what is right in our glosses on al-Hashiya al-Zahidiyya related to Sharh al-Mawaqif. And even if it is conceded) that the necessity of the necessary is necessary, it does not entail agreement due to the possibility of hiddenness) for the necessary may be hidden, so disagreement about it occurs. So we do not concede the second entailment. Have you not seen how the Sophists disagreed about necessary propositions? (So reflect) and do not slip, for it is a slippery place.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh dispute concerning the epistemological nature of knowledge obtained through tawatur (mass transmission). The central question is whether such knowledge is badihi (necessary/intuitive) or nazari (acquired through reasoning). The Hanafi position, as represented in this commentary, affirms that knowledge from tawatur is necessary, not acquired. The text begins by addressing a potential objection: if knowledge arises suddenly without perceived premises, it might be thought necessary, but the objector argues that the manner of acquisition may be forgotten. The commentator responds that the suddenness and lack of gradation are characteristics of necessary knowledge, and that even if some mutawatirat seem to involve premises, the occurrence of knowledge in simple-minded and children proves its necessity. The argument from the opposing side is then presented: if tawatur knowledge were acquired, disagreement would not be sheer obstinacy, unlike the case with necessary truths. The Hanafi response clarifies that such knowledge can still be from evident theoretical matters (nazariyat jaliyya) like arithmetic, where disagreement is not obstinacy but due to clear premises. However, the Hanafi insists that tawatur knowledge is actually necessary, not theoretical, because any theoretical derivation would be open to doubt, whereas tawatur yields certainty without such process. Two specific objections from the opponents are addressed: (1) that tawatur knowledge requires prior knowledge of premises (e.g., that the reporters are truthful), which would imply reasoning; the answer is that these premises are not consciously needed, as they are implicit in the very occurrence of the knowledge. (2) That if it were necessary, everyone would know it is necessary; the answer is that the necessity of such knowledge can itself be unrecognized due to forgetfulness or complexity, especially in affirmations (tasdiqat), and that even necessary propositions can be disputed (as with Sophists). The commentary thus defends the Hanafi view that tawatur knowledge is a form of necessary knowledge, not requiring conscious inferential steps, and that this is consistent with occasional disagreements due to hiddenness or forgetfulness.

Key Terms
بديهي (badihi): Knowledge that is immediate and necessary, requiring no reasoning or acquisition; it forces itself upon the mind.
نظري (nazari): Knowledge that is acquired through reasoning and inference from premises.
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by such a large number that collusion on falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the epistemological status of knowledge obtained from a mutawatir report?
A) It is acquired (nazari) because it depends on premises about the reporters.
B) It is necessary (badihi) because it occurs suddenly without conscious reasoning.
C) It is a combination of both necessary and acquired elements.
D) It is probabilistic and never certain.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge from tawatur is necessary (badihi), not acquired (nazari), because it arises immediately and uniformly even in those incapable of reasoning.

Conditions of Tawatur for Certain Knowledge
Listing conditions for tawatur and debating the necessity of reporter certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for tawatur, explain why each is necessary, and evaluate the Hanafi position against Ibn al-Hajib's objection regarding the certainty of reporters.

Core Idea
Tawatur yields certainty only when reporters are numerous, sensory-based, equally numerous across generations, and themselves certain.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' systematically lists the conditions (shurut) that must be present for a report to achieve the level of tawatur and produce certain knowledge. Understanding these conditions is crucial for evaluating the reliability of transmitted reports in usul al-fiqh. The passage also presents a key dispute regarding the fourth condition—whether all reporters must be certain—illustrating the Hanafi rigor in defining epistemological certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Conditions
Read the passage and list each condition as stated. Note the Arabic term for each.
The conditions are: (1) multiplicity preventing collusion, (2) reliance on sense perception, (3) equality of generations in number, (4) reporters must be certain.
2
Understand the Rationale
For each condition, explain why it is necessary for the report to yield certain knowledge (ʻilm yaqīnī).
For example, condition (2) excludes intellectual matters because they are not based on sense perception.
3
Examine the Dispute on Certainty
Identify the opposing view of Ibn al-Hajib regarding the fourth condition. Summarize his argument that the first three conditions already entail that some reporters are certain.
Ibn al-Hajib says the condition is unnecessary because either it is covered by the previous conditions or it is too strict.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The commentator adds a third argument: that the entire group collectively must be certain, and this is not entailed by the previous conditions. Understand why a group could prevent collusion without being certain.
A large group of ignorant people could also prevent collusion but not yield certainty.
5
Apply the Conditions
Given a hypothetical report, determine if it meets all four conditions and thus qualifies as mutawatir.
Practice with scenarios involving different numbers, sensory bases, and levels of certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Issue: Tawatur has conditions; with the absence of any one of them, it ceases. So whoever claims its theoreticalness (i.e., the theoreticalness of knowledge from it) conditions prior knowledge of them. Perhaps they claimed that these are conditions upon which its acquisition depends, as appears from their first proof. And whoever says it is necessary does not condition prior knowledge of them at all; rather, he says that the occurrence of knowledge from it in reality depends on their realization in it. Among them: the multiplicity of reporters to a number that prevents collusion on lying (neither intentionally nor unintentionally nor forgetfully) (customarily). And there is disagreement on the specification of this number as we will mention if Allah wills. (And among them: reliance on sense perception, that the first reporters perceived the content of the report. So there is no tawatur in intellectual matters; hence the folly of the peripatetic philosophers that there is no resurrection of bodies is not accepted. That is because if the intellectual matter is necessary, it yields knowledge by itself, so the reporter has no role; otherwise, error is possible. Rather, perhaps one becomes certain of it as in the report of the foolish peripatetics. (And among them: the equality of all generations, if there are generations, (in a number that yields certainty). So the first reporters must be a group whose collusion on lying is impossible, and likewise those reporting from them, and so on. (And among them: that they be (knowing and certain, not guessers nor doubters, (about the reported matter), for there is no knowledge except from knowledge. One may say: The benefit of tawatur is knowledge by custom, not by logical necessity, so it is possible that the report of guessers may strengthen the listener's conjecture to the point of certainty. It is better to refer to necessity, for we know necessarily that if the reporters say: 'We are not certain about the report, and it is possible in our view that it is not so,' then certain knowledge does not occur, and its denial is obstinacy. (And Sheikh Ibn al-Hajib said: This condition is not needed, because if by it is meant the knowledge of all the reporters (it is false, for it is possible that some of them are guessers; for if a group of reporters are certain, and some are guessers, it still yields certain knowledge. (And if by it is meant partial knowledge, i.e., knowledge of some of them, then it is necessitated by the three previous conditions (customarily, because they do not gather) to prevent collusion on lying (except) that some of them are certainly knowledgeable; so there is no need for this condition. (I say: I add) a third branch: the totality that achieves the number of tawatur in each generation. The necessity of this from the three mentioned conditions (is denied) for the fact that the group is a number whose collusion on lying is impossible in each generation does not entail that they are knowledgeable, and this is very clear. If you say: reliance on sense perception suffices for it,
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents the conditions (shurūṭ) for a report to be truly mutawātir and yield certain knowledge. It begins by noting the divergence between those who consider tawātur knowledge theoretical (nazarī) and those who consider it necessary (badīhī). For the former, prior knowledge of these conditions is required; for the latter, the conditions must be present in actuality but need not be consciously known. The first condition is the multiplicity of reporters to a number that customarily prevents collusion on lying, whether intentionally or unintentionally. The exact number is disputed and will be discussed later. The second condition is that the first reporters must have sensory experience of the reported content; hence intellectual matters (ʻaqliyyāt) cannot be mutawātir. This is used to reject the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection, as their claim is based on reasoning, not sense perception. The third condition is that all generations (if there are multiple) must be equal in number reaching the level of tawātur. The fourth condition is that the reporters are certain (mutayaqqin) and not merely guessing or doubting. A possible objection is raised: could reports of guessers cumulatively produce certainty? The answer is that we know by necessity that if reporters admit uncertainty, certainty does not arise. Then Ibn al-Hajib's view is cited: this condition is unnecessary because either it requires all reporters to be certain (which is false, as some may be guessers and certainty still arises from the certain ones), or it requires some to be certain, which is already entailed by the earlier conditions (since a number that prevents collusion on lying would necessarily include some certain individuals). The commentator adds a third possibility: that the entire group collectively must be certain, but this is not entailed by the earlier conditions, as a group of ignorant people could still be numerous enough to prevent collusion. The passage ends mid-sentence, noting that reliance on sense perception may suffice.

Key Terms
شروط التواتر (shurut al-tawatur): The conditions that must be met for a report to be considered mutawatir and produce certain knowledge.
استناد إلى الحس (istinad ila al-hass): The requirement that the first reporters must have sensed (seen, heard, etc.) the reported event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the conditions of tawatur discussed in this passage, which type of matter cannot be established by tawatur?
A) Historical events like battles.
B) Intellectual matters (aqliyyat) such as philosophical claims.
C) Religious doctrines confirmed by many scholars.
D) Reports about sensory experiences.

Key Takeaway
A mutawatir report must satisfy four conditions: multiplicity preventing collusion, sensory basis, generational equality in number, and certainty of reporters—otherwise it cannot yield certain knowledge.

The Minimum Number for Tawatur: No Fixed Count
Discussing various opinions on the minimum number for mutawatir reports and settling on no fixed number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position that tawatur requires no fixed minimum number and explain the rational arguments against specific numerical thresholds.

Core Idea
Tawatur's certainty depends on context, not a fixed transmitter count; the Hanafi school rejects all numerical thresholds.

In this passage from a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, the author surveys numerous opinions on the minimum number of transmitters needed for a mutawatir report—ranging from seven to beyond three hundred—and systematically refutes each. The discussion culminates in the Hanafi chosen view that no specific number can be fixed, because certainty is attained gradually and varies with the strength of reporters and the nature of the event. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this rejection and clarifies why tawatur is a matter of reliable context, not arithmetic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debate's core question
The passage addresses the minimum number of transmitters required for a report to produce certain knowledge (tawatur). Various opinions propose fixed numbers: 7, 10, 12, 20, 40, 50, 70, 300+, and countless. Recognize that each is supported by a specific dalil (Quranic verse, hadith, or qiyas).
The author presents these views not as authoritative but as targets for critique.
2
Analyze the critique of fixed-number views
The author declares all these opinions 'false' and their arguments 'weak'. For each proposed number, identify the type of evidence used (e.g., verse, hadith, analogy) and note how the author dismisses them—often by pointing out that the evidence does not actually prove a minimum, or that the analogy fails (e.g., the hadith about seven washes is abrogated).
The author does not provide detailed refutations, asserting that the arguments are too weak to need explicit rebuttal.
3
Extract the rationale for the chosen view
The chosen view is 'no specific minimum number' (al-mukhtār: 'adam ta'yīn al-adad al-aqall). The rational proofs are: (1) knowledge from reports is built gradually, like the intellect in children, and human capacity cannot pinpoint the threshold; (2) certainty can be attained suddenly, but this is rare and not regulative; (3) the Lawgiver did not specify a number; (4) the required number varies with the strength of reporters' access (e.g., king's confidants) and the proximity of the event to reason.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) argument, not based on specific transmitted texts.
4
Address the additional condition of adala and Islam
Some scholars, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, conditioned tawatur on the transmitters being just and Muslim, to exclude reports like the Christian account of Jesus' crucifixion. The author responds that reporters are not equal in rank; the event in question involves specific individuals, not all Christians, so the objection fails.
This reinforces that context matters more than a fixed numerical or qualifying condition.
5
Apply the rule: no fixed minimum
As a futuwwa (operative principle), when assessing a report for tawatur, do not look for a specific number. Instead, evaluate whether the circumstances (e.g., number of independent chains, impossibility of collusion, nature of the event) produce overwhelming certainty.
This is the practical takeaway for usul al-fiqh: the category of tawatur is determined by the outcome of certainty, not by a count.

Source Text

أصلاً (ولو سلم) عدم لزوم العلم بالعدد المشروط فلا يصح التحديد فالعدد يقل بقوة اطلاع المخبرين كدخاليل الملك) فإن أخبار العدد الأقل منهم عن أخبار الملك يفيد العلم والدخاليل جمع دخلل بمعنى المداخل ومظنة
