الدليل، فلا يتجه عليه أن مقصود صاحب الحواشي التكلم على الدليل المشهور ولا إنكار أصل المدعي حتى يتوجه إليه إثباته بهذا النحو فافهم. ثم قد شرط قوم ومنهم الإمام فخر الإسلام) رحمه الله تعالى العدالة والإسلام لئلا يراد إخبار النصارى بقتل المسيح عيسى ابن مريم عليه وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه السلام فإنهم أخبروا به فإن لم يشترط الإسلام وجب إفادة إخبارهم إفادة إخبارهم هذا العلم، وهو باطل قطعاً (والجواب منع الاستواء في طبقات المخبرين، بل إنما قتل عدة من الرجال الغير
The Second Principle: The Sunnah. It benefits knowledge of similar occurrences in incidental matters. This does not suffice to rebut the objection, because witnessing adultery is usually rare, occurring mostly in secluded places, so four do not produce knowledge, though they may in other cases where witnessing is easier. The judge hesitated regarding five and did not rule out its impossibility. It is objected that the obligation of tazkiya (validation) is common to four and five when they testify to adultery, so they should not produce knowledge either. Rather, tawatur should not occur at all, because any number testifying to adultery requires tazkiya. Unless the judge distinguishes between the two cases: every truthful group of five may produce knowledge of what they report. If they do not produce knowledge in the case of adultery, it is known that there is a liar among them, but not specifically identified, not that there is a liar in their reports so that one lie necessitates falsehood of all. Their statement is one, so tazkiya confirms the truthfulness of the remaining number (nisaab). Thus the report of five truthful persons is not necessarily unbeneficial; the possibility remains as before, unlike four, where if one is known to be a liar, the remaining do not constitute a nisaab, so tazkiya is ineffective and obligatory. Therefore, four definitely do not produce knowledge; the difference is clear. This is the best justification of the judge's statement, but something remains: it was previously stated that any number producing knowledge in one case does so in all cases. If five produce knowledge in one case, they would do so in adultery as well, and then tazkiya would be invalid. When it does not produce knowledge, it is not known that there is a liar; rather it is known that it does not produce knowledge in that case at all. The possibility of lying does not negate the attainment of knowledge, because justice is not a condition in tawatur. Understand. It is said that the minimum number is seven, by analogy with washing a vessel after a dog drinks seven times. The Prophet said: 'If a dog drinks from your vessel, wash it seven times.' This hadith is abrogated in our school by the hadith of sufficiency of three washes, as explained elsewhere. The analogy is that seven has an effect in purification, and certainty is also purification. Contemplate. It is said the minimum is ten, based on the verse 'Those are ten complete' (al-Baqarah) where ten is described as complete, thus beneficial for knowledge. It is said the minimum is twelve, the number of the leaders of the Children of Israel whom Moses sent as trustees to learn news of the giants; had their report not been beneficial for knowledge, he would not have sent them. It is said the minimum is twenty, based on the verse 'If there be among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred' (al-Anfal). Jihad was prescribed because their report of the messenger's coming and the obligation of faith produced knowledge, so fighting them upon their opposition became obligatory. It is said the minimum is forty, based on the hadith 'The best of raiding parties is forty,' and the excellence is because their report produces knowledge, so fighting upon their opposition is obligatory. It is said the minimum is fifty, by analogy with qasama (oath-taking), where fifty men swear that they did not kill and do not know the killer; the specification of fifty is because their report produces knowledge, not fewer. It is said the minimum is seventy, because Moses chose seventy men for his appointment to hear God's speech and inform others; had their report not been beneficial for knowledge, he would have chosen more, and if fewer were sufficient, he would have sufficed with them. It is said the minimum is more than three hundred, the number of the people of Badr. The reasoning is as with twenty steadfast. It is said the minimum is a number beyond counting due to multitude preventing collusion in falsehood. All these opinions are false, undeserving of attention, and their arguments are weak, needing no explicit refutation. The chosen view is that there is no specific minimum number, because certainty is attained through the reports of a group without prior or subsequent knowledge of a specific number. If a specific number were a condition, knowledge of that number would be required before (for those who hold knowledge is acquired) or after (for those who hold it is intuitive). Yet it is not known either way. Additionally, there is no customary way to know the specific number, because belief strengthens through a gradual process like the intellect of children. When one reports, conjecture arises; by adding another, the conjecture strengthens until certainty is reached. Human capability is insufficient to pinpoint this strengthening, making specification impossible. Sudden attainment of knowledge through reports is rare and not considered. It is said in the glosses of Mirzajan: perhaps the specific number is a condition in reality for tawatur according to those who specify, but knowledge of that number is not required before or after. I say in response: the discussion here is about specification and determination, which depends on knowledge of that number. If it is accepted that the number is unknown, the claim is proven. If one claims it is known but not necessarily at the time of attaining knowledge of the mutawatir report, we say this is invalid because we are certain of having no knowledge of the number; human capability is incapable. If one says: assume human capability is incapable, but knowledge could be attained through the report of the Lawgiver, they said? I say: this is among their nonsense; the Lawgiver did not specify at all. Even if we accept that knowledge of the specific number is unnecessary, specification is invalid because the number varies with the strength of the reporters' access, like the confidants of a king: the report of a smaller number of them about the king's affairs produces knowledge. Also, the closeness of events to reason affects speed of acceptance. Thus, the minimum can be as low as two if it produces knowledge in a given case, else three, etc. The discussion is about knowing the limit, which is inconceivable. Reflect deeply to realize that this is an answer by changing the proof. Then some, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, conditioned justice (adala) and Islam, so as not to include the report of Christians about the killing of Jesus, which would obligate knowledge if Islam were not a condition, which is false. The answer is to deny equality among classes of reporters; rather, only several non-Muslim men killed him.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion from a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut regarding the minimum number of transmitters required for a report to be considered mutawatir (conveyed by multiple chains that yield certainty). The author begins by analyzing the case of four witnesses for adultery and the judge's opinion about five. He explains the argument about tazkiya (validation of witnesses) and why four cannot produce knowledge while five might. He then systematically presents numerous opinions on the minimum number: 7 (by analogy with washing a dog's vessel, though that hadith is abrogated), 10 (based on 'ten complete'), 12 (the leaders of the Children of Israel), 20 (the steadfast in Quran), 40 (the best raiding party), 50 (qasama oath), 70 (Moses' chosen men), more than 300 (the people of Badr), and even a number beyond counting. Each opinion is briefly stated with its supporting proof. The author then declares all these views false and weak, and presents the chosen view: no specific minimum number can be fixed. The reasoning is that certainty from reports is attained gradually, and human capability cannot pinpoint the exact threshold. Moreover, knowledge of any specific number is not possible, and the Lawgiver did not specify one. The number varies according to the strength of the reporters' access and the nature of the event. Finally, he addresses the condition of adala (justice) and Islam, citing the objection that without these conditions, the Christian report of Jesus' crucifixion would produce certainty. The answer is that reporters are not equal in rank; only certain non-Muslims killed him, not all. The overarching lesson is that tawatur is a matter of certainty, not a fixed quantity; it depends on the context and the collective strength of the transmission.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): A report conveyed by such a large number of transmitters that collusion on falsehood is impossible, producing certain knowledge. The text concludes that no specific number is required.
عدد الأقل (adad al-aqall): The minimum number of transmitters needed for tawatur. The text rejects all fixed numbers, stating that the minimum varies by context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's chosen view in the passage, what is the minimum number of transmitters required for a report to be considered mutawatir?
A) 4
B) 5
C) No fixed number; it varies based on context and certainty
D) 40

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tawatur has no fixed minimum number; attainment of certain knowledge is the only criterion.

8 min
The Minimum Number for Tawatur: Hanafi Refutation
Refuting the condition of a specific number for tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the minimum number for tawatur and evaluate the argument that a specific number is required.

Core Idea
Certainty from collective reports arises gradually; no specific number can be pinpointed.

This passage addresses a fundamental dispute in usul al-fiqh: is there a specific minimum number of reporters required for tawatur? The Hanafi school argues that no such number can be determined, because certainty develops gradually and human capacity cannot pinpoint the threshold. Let us walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is whether tawatur requires a specific minimum number of reporters (e.g., 20, 40, etc.).
Some scholars argue for a fixed number, others reject it.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that no specific number is necessary; certainty can arise from a group without knowing the exact count.
The text calls opposing views 'false and not worth attention.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil aqli
Belief strengthens gradually (like a child's intellect). Each additional reporter strengthens the probability until certainty is reached, but humans cannot measure this process, so specification is impossible.
The argument is inductive: because we cannot pinpoint the moment of certainty, we cannot assign a number.
4
Evaluate the counter-argument
Opponents might claim the number is known by revelation or intuition. The Hanafi response is that no such revelation occurred, and intuition is unreliable.
The text dismisses these as 'ravings' (hawsat).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafis accept tawatur from any sufficiently large group without requiring knowledge of the exact count; others may reject reports if the number is not met.
This impacts acceptance of widely transmitted reports.

سلم) عدم لزوم العلم بالعدد المشروط فلا يصح التحديد فالعدد يقل بقوة اطلاع المخبرين كدخاليل الملك) فإن أخبار العدد الأقل منهم عن أخبار الملك يفيد العلم والدخاليل جمع دخلل بمعنى المداخل ومظنة السامعين فإنه إذا كان لهم مظنة يحصل بأخبار الأقلين (وقرب الوقائع عقلاً) فإنه إذا كانت الواقعة قريباً من العقل يتسارع إلى التصديق فكل أقل يمكن منه الأقل) فلا يتيسر التحديد، وإن كان في نفس الأمر محدوداً كيف والأعداد متناهية في القلة إلى الاثنين، فإن أفاد هو في واقعة فهو الأقل، وإلا فإن أفاد ثلاثة فهو الأقل، وهكذا، وإنما الكلام في معرفة المحدود ولا يتصور فتأمل) حق التأمل فتعرف أن هذا جواب بتغيير الدليل، فلا يتجه عليه أن مقصود صاحب الحواشي التكلم على الدليل المشهور ولا إنكار أصل المدعي حتى يتوجه إليه إثباته بهذا النحو فافهم. ثم قد شرط قوم ومنهم الإمام فخر الإسلام) رحمه الله تعالى العدالة والإسلام لئلا يراد إخبار النصارى بقتل المسيح عيسى ابن مريم عليه وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه السلام فإنهم أخبروا به فإن لم يشترط الإسلام وجب إفادة إخبارهم إفادة إخبارهم هذا العلم، وهو باطل قطعاً (والجواب منع الاستواء في طبقات المخبرين، بل إنما قتل عدة من الرجال الغير الأصل الثاني/ السنة العارفين بعيسى شبه نفسه رجلاً قد ألقى عليه شبه عيسى كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ وَمَا صَلَبُوهُ وَلَكِن سيِّدَ لَهُمْ ﴾ [النساء : ١٥٧] ثم ألقوا جسد ذلك المقتول على الصليب، ثم أخبروا بعد ذلك أنهم قتلوا عيسى وصلبوه وشكوا فيه أيضاً، حتى قال بعضهم لبعض: إن قتلنا عيسى فأين صاحبنا ذلك الرجل؟ وإن قتلنا ذلك الرجل فأين عيسى؟ فلا تواتر ههنا فلا إيراد، ثم أيد عدم اشتراط الإسلام والعدالة بقوله : ( ولو أخبر أهل قسطنطينية) - بضم القاف والطاءين المهملتين بينهما نون ساكنة والأول منهما مضموم والثاني مكسور وبعدها ياء ساكنة ثم نون مكسورة ثم ياء مشددة ـ بلدة بالروم دار سلطنة وكان سكانها كفاراً لم تفتح على وجه أتم وسيفتحها الإمام محمد المهدي الموعود كان غزاه معاوية وبعث سرية فيهم أبو أيوب الأنصاري ومات هو رضي الله عنه في الطريق. كذا في جامع الأصول بقتل ملكهم حصل العلم بلا ريب، فعلم أن العدالة غير مشروطة، وكذا الإسلام ( نعم ذلك) أي العدالة والإسلام (دخيل في تقليل العدد) الموجب للعلم ومؤكد لعدم التواطؤ على الكذب و أما الشرطية فكلا، ومن ههنا أي من أجل أن التواتر مفيد للعلم وإن كان المخبرون غير عدول (قالوا: إن التواتر ليس من مباحث علم الإسناد بل التواتر كالمشافهة في إفادة العلم ومن ثمة كان ثلاثيات البخاري رباعيات لنا، لأن «صحيحه» متواتر عنه، فكأنا سمعنا من البخاري، فلم يزد إلا واسطة واحدة، وهي فتدبر، واعلم أن عبارة الإمام فخر الإسلام رحمه الله تعالى هكذا الخبر المتواتر كالمعاين المسموع منه عليه السلام ،وذلك لأنه يرويه قوم لا يحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب لكثرتهم وعدالتهم وتباين أماكنهم ، ويدوم هذا الحد فيكون آخره كأوله، وأوله كآخره وأوسطه وذلك مثل نقل القرآن، والصلوات الخمس وعدد الركعات ومقادير الزكاة وما أشبه ذلك انتهى . ويوهم ذلك اشتراط عدم إحصاء الرواة وعدالتهم وتباين أمكنتهم، ووجه كلامه بأنه لم يأخذ هذه الشروط إلا إيذاناً بأن التواتر المحقق فيما ذكر من هذا القبيل دفعاً للشغب، فإنه لم ينكره أحد ممن بعقله اعتداد وأما الاستدلال بورود أخبار النصارى كما ذكره المصنف، فليس له عين ولا أثر في كلامه الشريف كيف وقد قال هو نفسه : إن أخبارهم مرجعها إلى الآحاد وليس أوله كآخره فافهم . واشترط (الشيعة) خذلهم الله تعالى في التواتر (المعصوم فيهم) أي في الرواة وهذا بهت فإنه إذا كان روى المعصوم فروايته وحده تفيد اليقين ولا حاجة إلى التواتر والعاملي منهم لما تفطن أن هذا الشرط مكابرة لوقوع العلم بدونه اختار سبيل التكذيب والجحود وقال : هذا النقل تهمة عليهم كيف لا وأنهم لا يقبلون خبر الواحد، فيجب أن تكون الأخبار المنقولة من الإمام الثاني عشر أو الحادي عشر كلها متواترة عندهم، والعصمة قد انحصرت في أربعة عشر على زعمهم فلو كان التواتر مشروطاً بأخبار المعصوم لما كانت هذه الأخبار عندهم حجة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن ناقلي هذا المذهب ثقات لا يتأتى إنكاره ، وهذا العبد غفر الله له رأي في بعض كتبهم وسمع عن بعض من يتبعونه أنهم أنكروا بعض القرآن بعدم رواية المعصوم كما قالوا في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنزَلَ اللهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٤٠] إن الصحيح فأنزل الله سكينته على رسوله، فالأول مع كونه متواتراً لم :
The number of the people of Badr (may Allah be pleased with them) is an indication, as in 'twenty patient ones' (Quran 8:66). It is said that the minimum is what cannot be counted due to its large number, because large numbers prevent conspiracy to lie. All these views are false and not worth attention. The chosen view is not to specify a minimum number, as certainty is obtained from the reports of a group without knowledge of a specific number, neither before nor after. If a specific number were a condition, knowledge of that condition would be required. The text discusses that it is impossible to know the specific number habitually, because belief strengthens gradually like the intellect. The human ability to measure this strengthening is insufficient, so specification is difficult. Then it mentions the condition of justice and Islam by some, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, to avoid the report of Christians about killing Jesus. The response is that there is no equality in the layers of reporters, as they killed a man who resembled Jesus. Then it supports the non-conditionality of Islam and justice by the report of the people of Constantinople about the death of their king, which brings certainty. It states that justice and Islam help reduce the number but are not conditions. Then it discusses that tawatur is not part of the science of isnad, and the example of Bukhari's collections. Finally, it refutes the Shi'a condition of infallibility in the reporters, showing its absurdity.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the conditions of tawatur (concurrent transmission) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It addresses three main issues: (1) the minimum number required for tawatur, (2) whether justice (adala) and Islam are conditions, and (3) the Shi'a condition of infallibility ('isma). The author refutes the view that a specific number is necessary, arguing that certainty can arise from a group without knowing the exact count. He also refutes the necessity of justice and Islam by giving examples: the report of Christians about killing Jesus is not tawatur because they were uncertain and contradictory, and the report of the non-Muslim people of Constantinople about the death of their king brings certainty, showing that non-Muslims can also produce tawatur. He explains that justice and Islam are not conditions but factors that can reduce the number needed for tawatur. Lastly, he critiques the Shi'a condition that the reporters must include an infallible imam, arguing that if an infallible reports alone, his report already brings certainty, rendering tawatur unnecessary. The passage reinforces the Hanafi position that tawatur is based on the collective report of a large group that cannot be imagined to conspire on a lie, without requiring specified numbers or personal characteristics of the reporters.

Key Terms
التواتر (al-tawatur): Concurrent transmission; a report by a large group that cannot conspire to lie, yielding certainty.
العدد المخصوص (al-adad al-mukhtass): The specific minimum number of reporters required for tawatur according to some.
التقوّي بالتدرج الخفي (al-taqawwi bil-tadarruj al-khafi): Gradual strengthening of belief imperceptibly, like the development of intellect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, which of the following is true about the minimum number for tawatur?
A) It must be at least 20 reporters.
B) It must be the number that precludes conspiracy, which can be known.
C) No specific number can be determined; certainty arises from a group without knowing the exact count.
D) It is determined by the scholarly consensus of each generation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects any fixed numerical condition for tawatur, basing itself on the rational argument that certainty is gradual and its threshold unknowable.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
Justice, Islam, and Infallibility: Conditions for Tawatur?
Refuting the conditions of justice, Islam, and infallibility for tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require justice, Islam, or infallibility for tawatur, and evaluate the evidence from the Constantinople report and the Christian report about Jesus.

Core Idea
Justice and Islam are not conditions for tawatur; they only reduce the required number. Infallibility is absurdly unnecessary.

This passage continues the discussion on the conditions for tawatur, specifically addressing whether the reporters must be just (adil), Muslim, or even infallible (ma'sum). The Hanafi school strongly rejects these as conditions, providing concrete examples: the report of Christians about Jesus (which is not tawatur) and the report of non-Muslim inhabitants of Constantinople about the death of their king (which yields certainty). Additionally, the Shi'a claim that an infallible imam must be among the reporters is refuted as self-defeating. Let us examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested conditions
Some scholars require the reporters to be just and Muslim; the Shi'a also require an infallible imam.
Imam Fakhr al-Islam is mentioned as one who required justice and Islam.
2
State the Hanafi position
Justice and Islam are not conditions; they only help reduce the number needed for certainty. Infallibility is rejected entirely.
The text calls the Shi'a condition 'calumny' (bahat).
3
Analyze the evidence for non-conditionality
The report of Christians about killing Jesus is not tawatur because they were uncertain and contradictory. The report of the people of Constantinople (non-Muslims) about their king's death brings certainty, proving that non-Muslims can produce tawatur.
This shows that adala and Islam are not necessary.
4
Refute the Shi'a condition of infallibility
If an infallible reports alone, his report already brings certainty, so tawatur would be redundant. The Shi'a themselves do not have tawatur for their key claims.
The author accuses Shi'a of inconsistency.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis accept tawatur from non-Muslims and non-just individuals; others reject such reports, limiting the scope of authoritative sunnah.
This expands the sources of certainty.

سبيل التكذيب والجحود وقال : هذا النقل تهمة عليهم كيف لا وأنهم لا يقبلون خبر الواحد، فيجب أن تكون الأخبار المنقولة من الإمام الثاني عشر أو الحادي عشر كلها متواترة عندهم، والعصمة قد انحصرت في أربعة عشر على زعمهم فلو كان التواتر مشروطاً بأخبار المعصوم لما كانت هذه الأخبار عندهم حجة، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن ناقلي هذا المذهب ثقات لا يتأتى إنكاره ، وهذا العبد غفر الله له رأي في بعض كتبهم وسمع عن بعض من يتبعونه أنهم أنكروا بعض القرآن بعدم رواية المعصوم كما قالوا في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنزَلَ اللهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٤٠] إن الصحيح فأنزل الله سكينته على رسوله، فالأول مع كونه متواتراً لم :
The number of the people of Badr (may Allah be pleased with them) is an indication, as in 'twenty patient ones' (Quran 8:66). It is said that the minimum is what cannot be counted due to its large number, because large numbers prevent conspiracy to lie. All these views are false and not worth attention. The chosen view is not to specify a minimum number, as certainty is obtained from the reports of a group without knowledge of a specific number, neither before nor after. If a specific number were a condition, knowledge of that condition would be required. The text discusses that it is impossible to know the specific number habitually, because belief strengthens gradually like the intellect. The human ability to measure this strengthening is insufficient, so specification is difficult. Then it mentions the condition of justice and Islam by some, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, to avoid the report of Christians about killing Jesus. The response is that there is no equality in the layers of reporters, as they killed a man who resembled Jesus. Then it supports the non-conditionality of Islam and justice by the report of the people of Constantinople about the death of their king, which brings certainty. It states that justice and Islam help reduce the number but are not conditions. Then it discusses that tawatur is not part of the science of isnad, and the example of Bukhari's collections. Finally, it refutes the Shi'a condition of infallibility in the reporters, showing its absurdity.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the conditions of tawatur (concurrent transmission) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It addresses three main issues: (1) the minimum number required for tawatur, (2) whether justice (adala) and Islam are conditions, and (3) the Shi'a condition of infallibility ('isma). The author refutes the view that a specific number is necessary, arguing that certainty can arise from a group without knowing the exact count. He also refutes the necessity of justice and Islam by giving examples: the report of Christians about killing Jesus is not tawatur because they were uncertain and contradictory, and the report of the non-Muslim people of Constantinople about the death of their king brings certainty, showing that non-Muslims can also produce tawatur. He explains that justice and Islam are not conditions but factors that can reduce the number needed for tawatur. Lastly, he critiques the Shi'a condition that the reporters must include an infallible imam, arguing that if an infallible reports alone, his report already brings certainty, rendering tawatur unnecessary. The passage reinforces the Hanafi position that tawatur is based on the collective report of a large group that cannot be imagined to conspire on a lie, without requiring specified numbers or personal characteristics of the reporters.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-adala): Justice; religious uprightness and integrity of a reporter.
المعصوم (al-ma'sum): The infallible; one protected from sin and error, as claimed for Shi'a imams.
أهل قسطنطينية (ahl Qustantiniyya): The people of Constantinople; non-Muslim inhabitants who reported the death of their king, producing certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Christian report about the killing of Jesus not considered tawatur?
A) Because the reporters were not just.
B) Because the reporters were not Muslim.
C) Because the reporters themselves doubted and contradicted each other.
D) Because the number of reporters was insufficient.

Key Takeaway
Justice, Islam, and infallibility are not conditions for tawatur; certainty can arise from any group that precludes conspiracy, and the Hanafi school defends this with clear examples.

Justice and Islam Are Not Conditions for Tawatur
Refutation of requiring justice and Islam for tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether justice and Islam are conditions for tawatur and identify the supporting evidence from the crucifixion and Constantinople examples.

Core Idea
Justice and Islam are not conditions for tawatur—mere impossibility of collusion suffices for certain knowledge.

This passage refutes the notion that the narrators in a mutawatir report must be just or Muslim. Using the example of the crucifixion of 'Isa (AS) and a hypothetical report from infidels in Constantinople, the author demonstrates that tawatur does not require such conditions. Justice and Islam merely reduce the required number and reinforce certainty, but they are not essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the central question: whether justice and Islam are conditions for a report to be mutawatir.
The Hanafi position is that they are not conditions, but some scholars disagree.
2
Analyze the crucifixion example
Examine why the Jews' report about killing 'Isa is not mutawatir according to the passage. Note the presence of doubt and internal contradiction among the narrators.
3
Analyze the Constantinople example
Consider the hypothetical report of infidels about their king's death. Understand why such a report yields certain knowledge despite the narrators being non-Muslim.
4
Distinguish conditions from factors
Recognize that justice and Islam are not essential conditions but facilitating factors that help reduce the number required and reinforce the impossibility of collusion.
5
Apply to hadith criticism
Understand the implication: for Hanafis, tawatur is not part of 'ilm al-isnad (hadith criticism) because it is like direct hearing, as illustrated by the thulathiyyat of Bukhari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفسه رجلاً قد ألقى عليه شبه عيسى كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ وَمَا صَلَبُوهُ وَلَكِن شُبِّهَ لَهُمْ﴾ [النساء : ١٥٧] ثم ألقوا جسد ذلك المقتول على الصليب، ثم أخبروا بعد ذلك أنهم قتلوا عيسى وصلبوه وشكوا فيه أيضاً، حتى قال بعضهم لبعض: إن قتلنا عيسى فأين صاحبنا ذلك الرجل؟ وإن قتلنا ذلك الرجل فأين عيسى؟ فلا تواتر ههنا فلا إيراد، ثم أيد عدم اشتراط الإسلام والعدالة بقوله : ( ولو أخبر أهل قسطنطينية) - بضم القاف والطاءين المهملتين بينهما نون ساكنة والأول منهما مضموم والثاني مكسور وبعدها ياء ساكنة ثم نون مكسورة ثم ياء مشددة ـ بلدة بالروم دار سلطنة وكان سكانها كفاراً لم تفتح على وجه أتم وسيفتحها الإمام محمد المهدي الموعود كان غزاه معاوية وبعث سرية فيهم أبو أيوب الأنصاري ومات هو رضي الله عنه في الطريق. كذا في جامع الأصول بقتل ملكهم حصل العلم بلا ريب، فعلم أن العدالة غير مشروطة، وكذا الإسلام ( نعم ذلك) أي العدالة والإسلام (دخيل في تقليل العدد) الموجب للعلم ومؤكد لعدم التواطؤ على الكذب و أما الشرطية فكلا، ومن ههنا أي من أجل أن التواتر مفيد للعلم وإن كان المخبرون غير عدول (قالوا: إن التواتر ليس من مباحث علم الإسناد بل التواتر كالمشافهة في إفادة العلم ومن ثمة كان ثلاثيات البخاري رباعيات لنا، لأن «صحيحه» متواتر عنه، فكأنا سمعنا من البخاري، فلم يزد إلا واسطة واحدة، وهي فتدبر، واعلم أن عبارة الإمام فخر الإسلام رحمه الله تعالى هكذا الخبر المتواتر كالمعاين المسموع منه عليه السلام ،وذلك لأنه يرويه قوم لا يحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب لكثرتهم وعدالتهم وتباين أماكنهم ، ويدوم هذا الحد فيكون آخره كأوله، وأوله كآخره وأوسطه وذلك مثل نقل القرآن، والصلوات الخمس وعدد الركعات ومقادير الزكاة وما أشبه ذلك انتهى . ويوهم ذلك اشتراط عدم إحصاء الرواة وعدالتهم وتباين أمكنتهم، ووجه كلامه بأنه لم يأخذ هذه الشروط إلا إيذاناً بأن التواتر المحقق فيما ذكر من هذا القبيل دفعاً للشغب، فإنه لم ينكره أحد ممن بعقله اعتداد وأما الاستدلال بورود أخبار النصارى كما ذكره المصنف، فليس له عين ولا أثر في كلامه الشريف كيف وقد قال هو نفسه : إن أخبارهم مرجعها إلى الآحاد وليس أوله كآخره فافهم .
It was made to appear to them like 'Isa. Then they cast the body of that killed person on the cross, then they reported after that that they had killed 'Isa and crucified him, and they also doubted that. So there is no tawatur here, thus no objection. Then he supported the non-requirement of Islam and justice by saying: 'And if the people of Constantinople had reported the killing of their king, knowledge would have been obtained without doubt'—so it is known that justice is not a condition, nor Islam. Yes, justice and Islam are factors in reducing the number required for knowledge and strengthening against collusion, but not as conditions. From this they said that tawatur is not from the topics of hadith criticism but like direct hearing. Hence the thulathiyyat of Bukhari are ruba'iyyat for us, because his Sahih is mutawatir from him, so it is as if we heard from Bukhari, with only one additional intermediary. Know that the expression of Imam Fakhr al-Islam is that mutawatir news is like seeing and hearing directly from the Prophet, because it is narrated by a countless group whose collusion is inconceivable due to their number, justice, and diverse locations. This continues such that its end is like its beginning. And this implies conditions of innumerability, justice, and diverse locations, but he only mentioned them to indicate that the tawatur in these examples is of that type, to refute objections.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage addresses whether justice and Islam are necessary conditions for tawatur. The author uses the case of the crucifixion of 'Isa (AS) to show that even when the narrators are Jews and Christians who doubt and contradict themselves, their report is not mutawatir because it lacks certainty, not because they are unjust or non-Muslim. Then, the hypothetical example of Constantinople—where infidels report the death of their king—shows that such a report would yield certainty, proving that justice and Islam are not conditions. However, justice and Islam help reduce the required number and reinforce the impossibility of collusion. The author also clarifies that Imam Fakhr al-Islam's mention of conditions (number, justice, diverse locations) is not meant as essential conditions but as descriptive features of typical tawatur cases. Finally, the comparison with Bukhari's thulathiyyat and ruba'iyyat illustrates the concept of tawatur in isnad.

Key Terms
التواتر (al-tawatur): A report that is transmitted by a large number of narrators in every generation, making collusion on falsehood inconceivable and yielding certain knowledge.
العدالة (al-‘adala): The quality of being just and upright in character, often required for witnesses and narrators in some schools.
الإسلام (al-Islam): Being Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the king's death was witnessed by many
B) Because infidels are reliable in their own affairs
C) Because the number and circumstances make collusion impossible
D) Because they have no motive to lie

Key Takeaway
Justice and Islam are not conditions for tawatur; the impossibility of collusion is sufficient for certain knowledge.

Invalid Conditions for Tawatur: A Hanafi Refutation
Refuting conditions for tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for tawatur rejected by the Hanafi school and apply the rational proof to refute them.

Core Idea
Tawatur produces certain knowledge; extra conditions are unnecessary and contradictory.

The Hanafi school holds that tawatur, a report from a large group that cannot collude, yields certain knowledge (ilm yaqini). This passage examines and refutes conditions imposed by the Rafidah, the Jews, and others. By exposing internal contradictions and appealing to actual human experience, the Hanafi position is vindicated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups and their conditions
List the three groups mentioned: Rafidah (Shia), Jews, and an unnamed group. For each, note the condition they impose for tawatur: Rafidah require an infallible Imam; Jews require the reporters to be of low status (dhimmah and miskinah); others require the reporters to be from different cities, or of different lineage, religion, and homeland.
The passage also mentions the condition of reporters not being from a single city.
2
Understand the Hanafi rational proof
The Hanafi refutation relies on a rational argument (dalil aqli): we observe that we gain certain knowledge from reports of a large group (tawatur) without needing any of these conditions. For example, the existence of Makkah or historical events like the conquest of Makkah are known through tawatur even though the reporters share the same city, religion, etc.
The author says 'al-ilm bi-al-ilm' meaning the certain knowledge is present regardless.
3
Analyze the internal contradictions
Examine each condition: The Rafidah accept ahad reports from their Imams, contradicting their own requirement for tawatur. The Jews argue that only powerless people can produce tawatur, but their logic can be reversed: the powerless might collude to please the powerful. The condition of different cities, lineage, etc., is refuted by the fact that we have tawatur from single cities (e.g., the Quran was transmitted from the city of Madinah).
The text calls all these conditions 'batil' (invalid).
4
Apply the refutation to each condition
For each condition, articulate the Hanafi response as a logical rebuttal. For Rafidah: point out their acceptance of ahad. For Jews: reverse the argument. For others: cite examples of tawatur from single communities.
This step demonstrates the practical use of the rational proof.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi rule is that tawatur, by definition, produces certain knowledge (ilm yaqini). No extrinsic conditions are required. The validity of tawatur is based on the impossibility of collusion (istihalat al-tawatu) due to the large number, not on the sociopolitical status of the reporters. This principle ensures the preservation of many religious reports.
This principle is foundational in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقبلوه لعدم رواية المعصوم على زعمهم والثاني نسبوه إلى الإمام زين العابدين علي بن الحسين عليه وعلى آله الكرام الرضوان وقبلوه مع كونه من الآحاد، ونقل في «مجمع البيان» عن بعض شياطينهم الذين هم عندهم ثقات أنه ذهب من القرآن آيات كثيرة والعياذ بالله، لا يعلمها إلا المعصوم، وسيبينها الإمام محمد المهدي الموعود مع أنه قد تواتر أن القرآن هو هذا؛ وما ذكره العاملي فمع كونه لا يفيد إلا عدم اشتراط التواتر عند عدم وجود معصومهم ويجوز أن يكون الشارطون شرطوا عند وجوده ومع كونه مبنياً على عدم قبول الآحاد مع أن البعض منهم قبلوا الآحاد ، ولعل قبولهم إياه لهذا الاشتراط ليس بعد تمامه إلا اعتراضاً عليهم، فيوجب فساد مذهبهم لا عدم صحة النقل عنهم (و) اشتراط (اليهود أهل الذمة والمسكنة في التواتر لإمكان تواطؤ من عداهم من أهل العزة على الكذب لعدم خوفهم، ولك أن تقلب عليهم أن خوفهم يورث احتمال التواطؤ مرضاة لأهل العز بخلافهم فإنهم لا يطلبون مرضاة أحد لعدم الخوف (و) اشتراط (قوم أن لا يحويهم بلد لأنّ أهل بلد واحد مما يمكن اجتماعهم على الكذب لعرض (و) اشتراط (قوم اختلاف النسب والدين والوطن) لذلك (والكل) من المذاهب (باطل للعلم بالعلم أي لليقين بوجود العلم عند أخبار الجماعة (بدون ذلك) أي بدون كل واحد من الشروط الثلاثة المذكورة، وهذا ظاهر جداً.
They accept it due to lack of narration of the infallible according to their claim, and the second they attributed to Imam Zayn al-Abidin Ali ibn al-Husayn, peace and blessings upon him and his noble family, and they accepted it despite it being ahad. And it is transmitted in 'Majma' al-Bayan' from some of their devils who are trustworthy according to them that many verses of the Quran were lost, God forbid, known only to the infallible, and they will be revealed by the promised Imam Mahdi, despite it being mutawatir that the Quran is this. And what al-Amili mentioned, despite not indicating anything but the non-requirement of tawatur in the absence of their infallible, and it is possible that the conditioners conditioned its presence, and despite being based on non-acceptance of ahad while some of them accepted ahad, perhaps their acceptance of it for this condition is not after its completion except as an objection against them, thus necessitating the corruption of their madhhab not the unsoundness of transmission from them. (And) the Jews, the people of covenant and lowliness, stipulated in tawatur the possibility of collusion of those besides them from the people of power on lies due to lack of fear, and you can reverse that their fear creates the possibility of collusion to please the people of power, unlike them, for they do not seek to please anyone due to lack of fear. (And) a group stipulated that no one city contain them, because the people of one city could possibly agree on a lie for a purpose. (And) a group stipulated difference of lineage, religion, and homeland for that. And all of these schools are invalid because of knowledge by knowledge, that is, certainty of the existence of knowledge upon the report of a group without that, that is, without each of the three mentioned conditions, and this is very apparent.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of various invalid conditions imposed by different groups for accepting tawatur. The author first addresses the Rafidah, who condition the presence of an infallible Imam for tawatur, yet contradict themselves by accepting ahad reports from their Imams. The author then refutes the Jewish condition that only powerless people can produce tawatur because others might collude, turning their argument against them. Next, the author refutes conditions of being from different towns, lineage, religion, etc. The conclusion is that all these conditions are baseless; tawatur produces certain knowledge without them. This is a rational proof supported by the fact that we actually find knowledge from reports of a group without such conditions, as in the case of cities and historical events.

Key Terms
التواتر (al-tawatur): A report transmitted by such a large number that it precludes the possibility of collusion on a lie, producing certain knowledge.
المعصوم (al-ma'soum): The infallible, specifically a prophet or Imam protected from sin and error.
الآحاد (al-ahad): Reports that do not reach the level of tawatur; they convey knowledge only if accompanied by supporting qara'in.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they themselves accept ahad reports from their Imams
B) Because the Quran is mutawatir without an infallible Imam
C) Because the reporters are all from the same city
D) Because the condition was added later

Key Takeaway
Tawatur is inherently certain; no extra conditions are needed.

Tawatur Ma'nawi and the Role of Divine Custom
Defining tawatur ma'nawi and defending its epistemological basis via divine custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tawatur ma'nawi, explain how it produces certain knowledge via divine custom, and refute the objection that all reports could be false.

Core Idea
Tawatur ma'nawi yields certainty not from rational necessity but from divine custom, which accumulates conjectures into certain knowledge.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut defines tawatur ma'nawi — a key Hanafi concept for deriving certain knowledge from numerous ahad reports that share a common meaning. The author also counters a philosophical objection by grounding knowledge in divine practice ('adah), demonstrating how accumulation of conjectures (zunun) prepares the mind for certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the definition of tawatur ma'nawi: what produces knowledge, what is that knowledge about, and what is the epistemological status?
The passage states it produces knowledge of the common element (qadr mushtarak) without needing a separate proof.
2
Study the examples
Review the examples (Hatim's generosity, Ali's bravery, etc.) and note that individual reports are ahad, yet the common meaning is certain. Why?
The common meaning is known through tawatur ma'nawi, not through each individual report.
3
Grasp the objection
Understand the philosophical objection: if each individual report could be false, why could not all be false, making the universal possibly non-existent?
The objection is based on the premise that a universal can exist without instances (Platonic forms).
4
Follow the response
See how the author answers: knowledge is not from rational necessity that one report is true, but from divine custom ('adah) which produces certainty from such reports.
This is similar to empirical sciences where repeated experiments yield certain knowledge by divine custom.
5
Reflect on the secret
Why does this custom produce certainty? The accumulation of conjectures prepares the mind, and the custom only occurs when the common meaning is true.
Denial is obstinacy — the knowledge is necessary (daruri) for one who reflects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: كثرة الآحاد المتفقة في معنى ولو التزاماً أي ولو كان المعنى التزامياً (توجب العلم بالقدر المشترك بين تلك الآحاد ولا يحتاج إلى ذلك إلى الدليل، لأن هذا العلم ضروري يعلم تحققه عند الرجوع إلى الوجدان ولو وجد منكر لا يلتفت إليه ويكذب ببداهة العقل (وهو التواتر المعنوي في الاصطلاح وذلك كوقائع حاتم في عطاياه، و وقائع أمير المؤمنين (علي) رضي الله عنه في حروبه) ووقائع أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه في عدله وجلادته في الدين ووقائع أبي ذر رضي الله عنه في زهده إلى غير ذلك من أخبار الصحابة والتابعين وغيرهم وككرامات قطب الأقطاب الملة والدين عبد القادر الجيلاني قدس سره العزيز (فليعلم السخاوة والشجاعة والعدل والزهد والولاية والكرامة وغيرها (مع أن شيئاً تلك الجزئيات لم يتواتر) بخصوصه إلا شيئاً قليلاً من كرامات قطب الأقطاب، فإنها وجدت متواترة اللفظ أيضاً (أقول : ههنا إشكال موقوف على مقدمة وهي : أن الكلي إذا كان كل واحد من أفراده جائز العدم انفراداً ، ومعاً كان هذا الكلي (أيضاً جائز الانتفاء، وإلا) يكن جائز لعدم لزم جواز المثل (الأفلاطونية وهي الماهيات الموجودة معراة الملازمة أنه إذا جاز وجود الكلي مع انتفاء جميع الأفراد بدلاً ومعاً فقد جاز وجود الكلي، من غير تشخص وهي المثل، وإذا تمهد هذا فنقول ههنا كذلك أي في متواتر المعنى يجوز انتفاء كل خبر انفراداً ومعاً (أما) انتفاؤه (انفراداً فالبفرض) لأنه قد فرض أن كلاً منها آحاد جائز العدم والكذب لعدم اليقين (وأما) انتفاؤها (معاً فلأنه لا علاقة بينها بحيث يلزم من انتفاء واحد منها وجود الآخر لأن هذا إنما يكون في المتنافيين ولا تنافي ،ههنا ثم هذا يجري في المتواتر لفظاً أيضاً، لأنه لا علاقة بين الأخبارات يوجب انتفاء واحد تحقق الآخر، ولك أن تمنع اختصاص هذه العلاقة بالمتنافين، ألا ترى أنه يجوز لزوم شيء ووجوبه مع تفارق أفراده وإمكانها كما بين في العلوم العقلية وغاية ما يقال) في الجواب (أنه) أي القدر المشترك بين الأخبار المنقولة (معلوم لا، لأن أحدها صدق قطعاً عقلاً حتى يرد ما قلت (بل) إنما هو معلوم (بالعادة) فإنّ العادة الإلهية قد جرت بإحداث العلم عند وجود هذه الإخبارات (وذلك كما في التجربيات فإن العادة الإلهية بإحداث العلم بعد التجربة والتكرار (والسر) فيه أن اجتماع الظنون) الحاصلة بإخبارات كثيرة بعد الذهن عادة لقبول العلم واليقين الواقعي والإخبارات على هذا الوجه إنما لا تكون عادة إلا فيما كان القدر المشترك حقاً مطابقاً للواقع (فتفكر) فإن إنكار ذلك مكابرة
Issue: The abundance of ahad reports that agree in meaning, even if implicatively (i.e., even if the meaning is implicit), necessitates knowledge of the common element among those ahad reports, and there is no need for a proof for that, because this knowledge is necessary, known to be realized when one refers to inner consciousness, and if there is a denier, he is not heeded and is belied by the necessity of reason. And it is called tawatur ma'nawi in terminology. That is like the accounts of Hatim in his generosity, and the accounts of the Commander of the Faithful (Ali), may Allah be pleased with him, in his battles, and the accounts of the Commander of the Faithful Umar in his justice and firmness in religion, and the accounts of Abu Dharr in his asceticism, and other reports of the Companions and Followers, and like the miracles of the Pole of Poles of the religion, Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, may his noble secret be sanctified. So is known generosity, bravery, justice, asceticism, sainthood, miracles, etc., even though none of those particulars are mutawatir individually except a few of the miracles of the Pole of Poles, which were found to be mutawatir in wording as well. I say: There is an objection here that depends on a premise: The universal, if each of its individuals is possibly non-existent individually and together, then this universal is also possibly non-existent; otherwise it would entail the possibility of the Platonic forms, which are essences existing stripped of particularity, that if it is possible for the universal to exist with the non-existence of all individuals one by one and together, then it is possible for the universal to exist without individuation, and that is the forms. If this is established, we say that it is similar here in tawatur ma'nawi: it is possible for each report to be non-existent individually and together. As for its non-existence individually, it is by assumption, because it is assumed that each of them is ahad, possibly non-existent and false due to lack of certainty. And as for its non-existence together, it is because there is no relation between them such that the non-existence of one necessitates the existence of another, because that only occurs in mutually exclusive things, and there is no mutual exclusion here. Then this also applies to tawatur in wording, because there is no relation between the reports that necessitates the non-existence of one becoming the existence of another. But you may prevent the exclusivity of this relation to mutually exclusive things; do you not see that the necessity of a thing is possible with the separation of its individuals and their possibility, as explained in the rational sciences? And the utmost that can be said in response is that the common element between the transmitted reports is known, not because one of them is certifiably true by reason so that what you said is refuted, but rather it is known by custom. For the divine custom has proceeded to produce knowledge upon the existence of these reports, just as in empirical matters, the divine custom produces knowledge after experience and repetition. And the secret is that the accumulation of conjectures from numerous reports prepares the mind customarily to accept real knowledge and certainty, and reports in this manner customarily occur only when the common element is true and corresponds to reality. So reflect, for denying that is obstinacy.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines tawatur ma'nawi (moral tawatur) — many reports that individually are ahad but collectively convey certain knowledge of a common meaning. Examples include generosity of Hatim, bravery of Ali, justice of Umar, asceticism of Abu Dharr, and miracles of Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. The author then addresses a philosophical objection: if each report individually could be false, why can't all be false together, making the universal (common meaning) also possibly non-existent? The objection relies on the Platonic ideal that a universal can exist without instances, but in tawatur, the universal (e.g., generosity) is known from the reports. The answer is that this knowledge arises from divine custom ('adah) — God's consistent practice to produce certainty from such reports, similar to empirical sciences where repeated experiments yield knowledge. The secret is that accumulated conjectures (zunun) prepare the mind to accept certainty, and this custom only holds when the common meaning is actually true. This is a key Hanafi argument that tawatur ma'nawi yields necessary knowledge without formal proof.

Key Terms
التواتر المعنوي (al-tawatur al-ma'nawi): The transmission of numerous reports that agree in a common meaning (even if the words differ), producing certain knowledge of that meaning.
العادة الإلهية (al-'adah al-ilahiyyah): The consistent divine practice in creation that produces knowledge from repeated occurrences or numerous reports.
القدر المشترك (al-qadr al-mushtarak): The common element or shared meaning that emerges from multiple reports, even if their details differ.
العلم الضروري (al-'ilm al-daruri): Necessary knowledge that is self-evident and does not require explicit proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do we know the common meaning (e.g., generosity of Hatim) from multiple ahad reports?
A) By rational deduction that at least one report must be true
B) By divine custom that accumulates conjectures to produce certainty
C) By testimony of an infallible Imam
D) By mathematical probability

Key Takeaway
Tawatur ma'nawi produces necessary knowledge (ilm daruri) of a common meaning through divine custom, not through rational necessity or individual report verification.

The Abundance of Mutawatir Hadith: Refuting Claims of Scarcity
Listing several hadiths that are mutawatir and discussing the existence of mutawatir hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of mutawatir hadith and explain why the Hanafi school considers them abundant.

Core Idea
Mutawatir hadith are plentiful – the claim of scarcity is refuted by numerous textual and practical examples.

Some scholars have claimed that no hadith meets the strict criteria of tawatur, rendering mutawatir reports virtually nonexistent. This lesson examines that claim and the Hanafi refutation, which lists many hadiths and practices that are indisputably mutawatir. By the end, you will see that mutawatir transmission is both real and essential for establishing certain knowledge in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Claim
Recognize that some scholars (e.g., Ibn al-Salah) argued that no mutawatir hadith exists, or only one exists. Understand the basis: they may have required uncountability and difference of religion among narrators.
This sets up the problem the passage addresses.
2
Identify the Hanafi Response
The author counters by listing numerous examples of mutawatir hadith. Note the distinction between tawatur in wording (lafẓī) and in meaning (maʿnawī). The hadith against lying on the Prophet is cited as the only example of lafẓī tawatur according to Ibn al-Salah, but the author broadens the scope.
The Hanafi school emphasizes abundance.
3
Categorize the Examples
Group the examples: specific hadiths (e.g., mash 'ala al-khuffayn, heels in fire, seven ahruf) and practical matters (rak'ahs, battles, adhan). The latter are mutawatir in meaning.
This shows tawatur is not limited to a few texts.
4
Analyze the Epistemological Weight
Note the strong statements: Abu Hanifa said he fears disbelief for deniers of mash 'ala al-khuffayn. This highlights that mutawatir hadith produce certain knowledge (ʿilm yaqīnī) and denial can be kufr.
Hanafi usul: mutawatir is qaṭʿī al-thubūt.
5
Apply to Usul al-Fiqh
Understand how mutawatir hadith function as a source of law. They override zannī reports and are binding without question. This lesson shows that the Hanafi school relies on a wide corpus of mutawatir material.
Essential for istinbāṭ.

Source Text

فائدة المتواتر من الحديث قيل : لا يوجد) ولعلهم شرطوا عدم الإحصاء واختلاف : الدين (وقال ابن الصلاح من المحدثين لا يوجد (إلا) أن يدعي في حديث: «من كذب علي : متعمداً فليتبوأ مقعده من النار فإن رواته أزيد من مائة صحابي وفيهم العشرة المبشرة) بالجنة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وقد يقال : مراده التواتر (لفظاً أي لم يوجد التواتر اللفظي إلا في ذلك الحديث (وإلا فحديث المسح على الخفين متواتر رواه سبعون صحابياً) قاله الحسن البصري، وقد عد الرواة في الفتح القدير، وقال الإمام الهمام أبو حنيفة رضوان الله تعالى عليه : ما قلت بالمسح على الخف، إلا أنه جاء مثل ضوء النهار، وأخاف الكفر على من أنكره. وقال الإمام بن حنبل : ليس في قلبي من المسح على الخف شيء. ثم في هذا التأويل أيضاً شيء، فإنه قد تواتر قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : ويل للأعقاب من النار رواه اثنا عشر صحابياً مقطوعاً بعدالتهم أكثرهم من أصحاب بيعة الرضوان رضي الله تعالى عنهم، وقد تقدم تواتر: لا نورث ما تركناه صدقة ولعل تأويل قوله إنه مبالغة في القلة (وقيل: حديث: «أنزل القرآن على سبعة أحرف متواتر رواه عشرون من الأصحاب مع كونهم عدولاً قطعاً، وفي تفسير سبعة أحرف، اختلاف مذكور في موضعه وقال ابن الجوزي) تتبعت الأحاديث المتواترة فبلغت جملة منها حديث الشفاعة وحديث الحساب وحديث النظر إلى الله تعالى في الآخرة، ة، وحديث غسل الرجلين في الوضوء. رواه أربعة عشر كما بين في «فتح القدير» وغيره وحديث عذاب القبر) ورواته كثيرة في الغاية وحديث المسح على الخفين ولم يرد الحصر فيه. فإنّ أعداد الركعات وذهاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إلى بدر وأحد وسائر الغزوات والأذان والإقامة والجماعة، وفضائل الخلفاء الراشدين، وفضل أصحاب بدر، بعمومه متواترة من غير ريبة، وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى حديث: «لن تجتمع أمتي على ضلالة» بمعناه متواتر، وكذا حديث الحوض والمغفرة والشفاعة وغيرها فافهم والله أعلم بالصواب
Benefit: The mutawatir among hadith is said: It does not exist. Perhaps they conditioned uncountability and difference of religion. Ibn al-Salah from the hadith scholars said it does not exist except that it may be claimed in the hadith: 'Whoever lies upon me intentionally, let him take his seat in Hellfire,' because its narrators are more than a hundred Companions, among them the ten promised Paradise, may Allah be pleased with them. And it may be said: He meant tawatur in wording, i.e., tawatur in wording is not found except in that hadith. Otherwise, the hadith of wiping over the leather socks is mutawatir, narrated by seventy Companions, said by al-Hasan al-Basri, and the narrators were counted in Fath al-Qadir. And Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I only said about wiping over the socks that it came like the brightness of the day, and I fear disbelief for the one who denies it. And Imam ibn Hanbal said: There is nothing in my heart against wiping over the socks. Then in this interpretation there is also something, for his statement, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions, has been mutawatir: 'Woe to the heels from the Hellfire,' narrated by twelve Companions, their justice being certain, most of them from the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, may Allah be pleased with them. And the tawatur of 'We do not bequeath, what we leave is charity' has preceded. And perhaps the interpretation of his statement is that it is an exaggeration in scarcity. And it is said: The hadith 'The Quran was revealed on seven ahruf' is mutawatir, narrated by twenty Companions, they being certainly just, and there is disagreement on the interpretation of seven ahruf mentioned in its place. And Ibn al-Jawzi said: I pursued the mutawatir hadiths and found among them the hadith of intercession, the hadith of reckoning, the hadith of looking at Allah in the Hereafter, the hadith of washing the feet in wudu, narrated by fourteen as explained in Fath al-Qadir and others, the hadith of punishment of the grave, its narrators are extremely numerous, and the hadith of wiping over the socks, and the enumeration is not limited. Indeed, the numbers of rak'ahs, the going of the Messenger of Allah to Badr, Uhud, and the rest of the battles, the adhan, iqamah, congregation, the virtues of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the virtue of the people of Badr generally are mutawatir without doubt. And there will come, if Allah wills, the hadith 'My community will not agree on error' in meaning mutawatir, and likewise the hadith of the Basin, forgiveness, intercession, and others. So understand, and Allah knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This benefit (fā'ida) addresses the claim that no mutawatir hadith exists, attributed to some scholars who may have conditioned uncountability and difference of religion. Ibn al-Salah is quoted as saying only the hadith against lying on the Prophet is mutawatir in wording. The author counters by listing numerous examples: the hadith of wiping over the socks (mash 'ala al-khuffayn) narrated by seventy Companions, the hadith about heels in the fire by twelve, the inheritance hadith, the seven ahruf hadith, and many more from Ibn al-Jawzi's compilation. He also includes practical matters like numbers of rak'ahs, battles, adhan, etc., as mutawatir in meaning. Notably, Abu Hanifa is quoted affirming the strength of the mash hadith, even threatening disbelief for deniers. This passage demonstrates that mutawatir hadith are abundant, both in wording and meaning, contra some claims.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A hadith narrated by such a large number of chains that collusion on a lie is impossible, generating certain knowledge.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): The practice of wiping over leather socks in wudu, a specific hadith example cited as mutawatir.
التواتر اللفظي (al-tawatur al-lafẓī): Tawatur in literal wording, where the exact same text is transmitted by many chains.
التواتر المعنوي (al-tawatur al-maʿnawī): Tawatur in meaning, where multiple hadiths with different wordings convey the same core meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Twelve
B) Seventy
C) Twenty
D) Over one hundred

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith are plentiful and provide certain knowledge; the Hanafi school affirms their abundance across both specific texts and widespread practices.

Khabar al-Wahid and Certainty: The Hanafi Position
Stating the position of most usul scholars including the three Hanafi imams on khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether khabar al-wahid conveys certain knowledge and identify the opposing view, including the role of qara'in.

Core Idea
For the Hanafi school, a solitary report never yields certainty, even with supporting indicators.

In usul al-fiqh, the epistemological weight of evidence determines how rulings are derived. A key point of debate is whether a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) from a non-infallible reporter can produce certain knowledge (ilm). The passage before you states the dominant Hanafi view, shared by the three founding imams, and notes a minority opinion. Understanding this position is essential to grasping how Hanafi scholars evaluate hadith evidence in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
What is the exact question being debated? It is whether a report from a single non-infallible person can produce certain knowledge (as opposed to probable knowledge, zann).
2
State the Hanafi Position
The majority, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that such a report does not convey knowledge at all—neither with nor without external indicators (qara'in).
This is a strict view; it does not mean the report is rejected, but it remains zanni.
3
Identify the Opposing View
The text uses 'qīl' (it is said) to refer to scholars who argue that qara'in can raise a khabar al-wahid to the level of certainty.
The phrase 'sawa' in the Arabic likely introduces that qara'in can be 'accidental or inherent'.
4
Appreciate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: for the Hanafi, a solitary hadith is always zanni and may be harmonized with stronger evidence; for the opposing view, if qara'in are strong, it becomes qati' and overrides weaker evidence.
This affects how rulings are derived from ahad reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في أخبار الآحاد (مسألة الأكثر من أهل الأصول، ومنهم الأئمة الثلاثة (على أن خبر الواحد إن لم يكن هذا الواحد المخبر (معصوماً) نبياً (لا يفيد العلم مطلقاً) احتف بالقرائن أو لا وقيل : يفيد) خبر الواحد الغير المعصوم (بالقرينة زائدة كانت ولازمة، سواء
Chapter: On Ahad Reports. Issue: The majority of usul scholars, including the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), hold that khabar al-wahid, if the reporter is not infallible (a prophet), does not convey knowledge absolutely, whether it is accompanied by qara'in or not. And it is said: It conveys knowledge (for the non-infallible) with qara'in, whether the qara'in are accidental or inherent...
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on ahad reports and states the well-known Hanafi position: khabar al-wahid from a non-infallible reporter does not produce certain knowledge under any circumstances, even with supporting qara'in. The 'three imams' refer to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. A contrary opinion (qīl) holds that it can convey knowledge if accompanied by qara'in that raise it to certainty. The text is cut off mid-word ('sawa' likely beginning 'sawa'an kanat laziman aw za'idatan'), but the core dispute is clear. This is a foundational usul al-fiqh issue: what level of certainty does a solitary report provide? The Hanafi view insists on absolute Zann; the qīl view allows for possible certainty with external indicators.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
القرينة (al-qarinah): An external indicator or contextual evidence that might support the truth of a report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Yes, if accompanied by qara'in
C) No, it never conveys certain knowledge, even with qara'in
D) No, but only if the reporter is a sahabi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats khabar al-wahid as zanni evidence that can support rulings but never reaches the level of certainty, regardless of accompanying indicators.

The Epistemology of Mutawatir Hadith
Defining tawatur and proving its existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir, explain how it produces certainty via divine custom, and list several examples to refute the claim that mutawatir hadith are non-existent.

Core Idea
Mutawatir certainty comes from divine custom, not rational necessity; many hadith meet this standard.

In Hanafi usul, the definition and existence of mutawatir hadith are foundational. This passage addresses two key issues: first, how the common element in multiple reports generates knowledge through divine custom, and second, a refutation of the claim that no mutawatir hadith exist. You will learn the mechanism of certainty and see that the school holds numerous narrations as mutawatir, with significant consequences for denial.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the definition of mutawatir
Locate the key elements: the common element (qadr mushtarak) among reports, the role of divine custom (ʿādah ilāhiyyah) in generating certain knowledge, and the analogy to experiential knowledge (tajribiyyāt).
Note that Hanafis do not require rational necessity; custom suffices.
2
2. Understand the epistemological basis
The text explains that certainty arises not from each individual report but from the convergence of many reports that prepare the mind. This is why it is known by custom, not reason.
The 'secret' (sirr) is the accumulation of probabilities (zunun).
3
3. Recognize the dispute over existence
Some scholars (Ibn al-Salah) claimed mutawatir hadith are extremely rare or non-existent. The author counters by listing several well-known mutawatir narrations.
Note the refutation includes examples from fiqh and creed.
4
4. Analyze the examples provided
Work through the examples: the hadith against lying, wiping over socks, punishment of the grave, etc. Consider why each is considered mutawatir by Hanafis.
Imam Abu Hanifa's statement about the strength of the masḥ hadith is particularly important.
5
5. Derive the thamarah (practical consequence)
If a hadith is mutawatir, its denial can lead to disbelief. This shows the high stakes of the classification.
Thus, the dispute is not merely academic.

Source Text

الأصل الثاني/ السنة هذه العلاقة بالمتنافين، ألا ترى أنه يجوز لزوم شيء ووجوبه مع تفارق أفراده وإمكانها كما بين في العلوم العقلية وغاية ما يقال) في الجواب (أنه) أي القدر المشترك بين الأخبار المنقولة (معلوم لا، لأن أحدها صدق قطعاً عقلاً حتى يرد ما قلت (بل) إنما هو معلوم (بالعادة) فإنّ العادة الإلهية قد جرت بإحداث العلم عند وجود هذه الإخبارات (وذلك كما في التجربيات فإن العادة الإلهية بإحداث العلم بعد التجربة والتكرار (والسر) فيه أن اجتماع الظنون) الحاصلة بإخبارات كثيرة بعد الذهن عادة لقبول العلم واليقين الواقعي والإخبارات على هذا الوجه إنما لا تكون عادة إلا فيما كان القدر المشترك حقاً مطابقاً للواقع (فتفكر) فإن إنكار ذلك مكابرة . (فائدة المتواتر من الحديث قيل : لا يوجد) ولعلهم شرطوا عدم الإحصاء واختلاف : الدين (وقال ابن الصلاح من المحدثين لا يوجد (إلا) أن يدعي في حديث: «من كذب علي : متعمداً فليتبوأ مقعده من النار فإن رواته أزيد من مائة صحابي وفيهم العشرة المبشرة) بالجنة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم وقد يقال : مراده التواتر (لفظاً أي لم يوجد التواتر اللفظي إلا في ذلك الحديث (وإلا فحديث المسح على الخفين متواتر رواه سبعون صحابياً) قاله الحسن البصري، وقد عد الرواة في الفتح القدير، وقال الإمام الهمام أبو حنيفة رضوان الله تعالى عليه : ما قلت بالمسح على الخف، إلا أنه جاء مثل ضوء النهار، وأخاف الكفر على من أنكره. وقال الإمام بن حنبل : ليس في قلبي من المسح على الخف شيء. ثم في هذا التأويل أيضاً شيء، فإنه قد تواتر قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : ويل للأعقاب من النار رواه اثنا عشر صحابياً مقطوعاً بعدالتهم أكثرهم من أصحاب بيعة الرضوان رضي الله تعالى عنهم، وقد تقدم تواتر: لا نورث ما تركناه صدقة ولعل تأويل قوله إنه مبالغة في القلة (وقيل: حديث: «أنزل القرآن على سبعة أحرف متواتر رواه عشرون من الأصحاب مع كونهم عدولاً قطعاً، وفي تفسير سبعة أحرف، اختلاف مذكور في موضعه وقال ابن الجوزي) تتبعت الأحاديث المتواترة فبلغت جملة منها حديث الشفاعة وحديث الحساب وحديث النظر إلى الله تعالى في الآخرة، ة، وحديث غسل الرجلين في الوضوء. رواه أربعة عشر كما بين في «فتح القدير» وغيره وحديث عذاب القبر) ورواته كثيرة في الغاية وحديث المسح على الخفين ولم يرد الحصر فيه. فإنّ أعداد الركعات وذهاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إلى بدر وأحد وسائر الغزوات والأذان والإقامة والجماعة، وفضائل الخلفاء الراشدين، وفضل أصحاب بدر، بعمومه متواترة من غير ريبة، وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى حديث: «لن تجتمع أمتي على ضلالة» بمعناه متواتر، وكذا حديث الحوض والمغفرة والشفاعة وغيرها فافهم والله أعلم بالصواب .
The second principle: the Sunnah has this relationship with the two conflicting things. Do you not see that it is permissible for a thing to be binding and obligatory despite the divergence of its individuals and their possibility, as explained in the rational sciences. The ultimate statement in response is that the common element between the transmitted reports is known — not because one of them is absolutely true rationally, as you claimed — but rather it is known by custom. For the divine custom has proceeded to generate knowledge upon the existence of these reports, just as in experiential matters where the divine custom generates knowledge after experiment and repetition. The secret is that the coming together of multiple opinions (zunun) obtained from many reports usually prepares the mind to accept real knowledge and certainty. Reports in this manner are not customary except when the common element is true and corresponding to reality. So ponder, for denying that is stubbornness. (Benefit: Mutawatir hadith is said not to exist.) Perhaps they stipulated lack of enumeration and difference in religion. Ibn al-Salah, among the hadith scholars, said it does not exist, except one might claim it in the hadith: 'Whoever intentionally lies about me, let him take his seat in Hellfire,' for its narrators exceed one hundred companions, including the ten promised Paradise. It may be said that he meant tawatur in wording — i.e., verbal tawatur exists only in that hadith. Otherwise, the hadith on wiping over the leather socks is mutawatir, narrated by seventy companions, as stated by al-Hasan al-Basri. The narrators were counted in Fath al-Qadir. Imam Abu Hanifa said: 'I did not speak about wiping over socks except that it came like the light of day, and I fear disbelief for whoever denies it.' Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: 'There is nothing in my heart regarding wiping over socks.' Then there is also something in this interpretation, for the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Woe to the heels from the Fire' is mutawatir, narrated by twelve companions, decisively trustworthy, most of them from the people of the pledge of Ridwan. The tawatur of 'We do not bequeath, what we leave is charity' has preceded. Perhaps his statement is an exaggeration of scarcity. It is said that the hadith 'The Quran was revealed on seven modes' is mutawatir, narrated by twenty companions, decisively trustworthy. There is difference regarding the interpretation of 'seven modes' mentioned in its place. Ibn al-Jawzi said: 'I followed the mutawatir hadith and they amounted to: the hadith of intercession, the hadith of reckoning, the hadith of seeing Allah in the Hereafter, the hadith of washing the feet in ablution — narrated by fourteen as explained in Fath al-Qadir etc. — and the hadith of the punishment of the grave, whose narrators are extremely many, and the hadith of wiping over socks.' H is not limited. The number of rak'as, the Prophet's going to Badr, Uhud, and other battles, the adhan, iqama, congregation, the virtues of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the virtue of the people of Badr in their entirety are mutawatir without doubt. There will come, Allah willing, the hadith 'My community will not unite on error' in its meaning as mutawatir, and likewise the hadith of the Pond, Forgiveness, Intercession, and others. So understand, and Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the nature of mutawatir reports within the Hanafi usul framework. It begins by addressing an earlier objection about the common element (qadr mushtarak) among conflicting reports. The author argues that knowledge from mutawatir is not rationally necessary (ʿaqlan) but comes through divine custom (ʿādah ilāhiyyah), similar to experiential knowledge gained through repetition. This is a key Hanafi principle: certainty from tawatur is not a logical necessity but an established custom. The text then addresses the claim that mutawatir hadith do not exist. It refutes this by listing several examples, including the famous hadith about lying against the Prophet, the hadith on wiping over shoes (masḥ ʿalā al-khuffayn), and others. The author emphasizes that Imam Abu Hanifa considered the evidence for wiping over socks so strong that denial could lead to disbelief. The passage also mentions al-Masḥ ʿalā al-khuffayn as a well-known example of tawatur, and includes other mutawatir narrations like the punishment of the grave and the pool (hawḍ). The genre is a fāʾidah (benefit) within a larger usul work, aimed at establishing the epistemic value of mutawatir reports.

Key Terms
القدر المشترك (al-qadr al-mushtarak): The common element that is present in all the reports of a mutawatir transmission, which is what generates knowledge
العادة الإلهية (al-ʿādah al-ilāhiyyah): The established divine practice (sunnat Allāh) that normally operates in the physical and epistemic worlds; it is not a logical necessity but a constant pattern that can be relied upon

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the certain knowledge produced by mutawatir reports?
A) Rational necessity
B) Divine custom (al-ʿādah al-ilāhiyyah)
C) The number of narrators exceeding one hundred
D) The lack of any conflicting reports

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith exist and yield certain knowledge through divine custom; Hanafi usul emphasizes that this certainty is not rational but divinely ordained, with serious consequences for those who deny it.
